Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Prayer Times for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr with the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Zuhr's End
Defines prayer times with proofs and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the times of Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr according to the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the end of Zuhr time.

Core Idea
The end of Zuhr time is disputed: Abu Hanifa sets it at double shadow (excluding zenith), while the Sahibayn set it at equal shadow.

Prayer times are foundational to salah, and their precise definition ensures the validity of worship. This passage from al-Quduri's matn provides clear definitions for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr, supported by Quranic verses and hadith. A key intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples on the end of Zuhr time is also presented, with practical consequences for daily prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify Fajr time and its proofs
Locate the definition of Fajr's first time (true dawn) and last time (sunrise). Then review the four proofs cited: two Quranic verses, a hadith about the false dawn, and the fasting verse.
Distinguish true dawn (horizontal whiteness) from false dawn (vertical pillar).
2
Recognize Zuhr start and the dispute on its end
Note that Zuhr begins at zawal (declination). Then carefully read the two opinions: Abu Hanifa (end when shadow is double, excluding zenith shadow) and Sahibayn (end when shadow equals height).
The exclusion of fay' al-zawal (zenith shadow) is unique to Hanafis.
3
Understand the impact on Asr start
Asr begins when Zuhr time ends, according to whichever view is adopted. Thus Asr start differs between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
This is an example of thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
4
Summarize the mufta bihi position
Identify that the relied-upon view (tarjih) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Zuhr ends when shadow equals height, making it the easier and more common practice.
This tarjih is based on the hadith of Jibril and practicality for the community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الْفَجْرِ إِذَا طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ الْبَيَاضُ الْمُعْتَرِضُ فِي الْأُفُقِ وَآخِرُ وَقْتِهَا مَا لَمْ تَطْلُعْ الشَّمْسُ وَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الظُّهْرِ إِذَا زَالَتْ الشَّمْسُ

وجه: (١) الآية: ﴿إِنَّ الصَّلَوةَ كَانَتْ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ كِتَبًا مَّوْقُوتَا﴾ (النساء: 103)
وجه: (٢) الآية: ﴿وَسَبِّحْ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّكَ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَقَبْلَ غُرُوبِهَا﴾ (طه: 130)
وجه: (٣) الحديث: عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ: «لَا يَغُرَّنَّكُمْ أَذَانُ بِلَالٍ، وَلَا هَذَا الْبَيَاضُ - لِعَمُودِ الصُّبْحِ - حَتَّى يَسْتَطِيرَ هَكَذَا» (رواه مسلم وأبو داود)
وجه: (٤) الآية: ﴿وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الخَيْطُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الْأَسْوَدِ مِنَ الْفَجْرِ﴾ (البقرة: 187)

وَآخِرُ وَقْتِهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِذَا صَارَ ظِلُّ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ مِثْلَيْهِ سِوَى فِيءِ الزَّوَالِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ إِذَا صَارَ ظِلُّ كُلّ شَيْءٍ مِثْلَهُ.
وَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الْعَصْرِ إِذَا خَرَجَ وَقْتُ الظُّهْرِ عَلَى الْقَوْلَيْنِ وَآخِرُ وَقْتِهَا مَا لَمْ تَغْرُبُ الشَّمْسُ

وجه: (١) الحديث: حديث ابن عباس: «أَمَّنِي جِبْرِيلُ عِنْدَ البَيْتِ مَرَّتَيْنِ...» (رواه الترمذي وأبو داود)
وجه: (٢) الآية: ﴿وَسَبِّحْ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّكَ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَقَبْلَ غُرُوبِهَا﴾ (طه: 130)
وجه: (٣) الحديث: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: «مَنْ أَدْرَكَ مِنَ الصُّبْحِ رَكْعَةً قَبْلَ أَنْ تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الصُّبْحَ، وَمَنْ أَدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مِنَ العَصْرِ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ العَصْرَ» (رواه البخاري والترمذي)

أصول: وقت نماز کے لئے شرط ہے، اگر وقت نہ ہو تو نماز ہی واجب نہیں ہوتی، وقت آنے پر وجوب ہوتا ہے
أصول: ظہر کا وقت عصر تک رہتا ہے اور عصر کا وقت مغرب تک البتہ آفتاب زرد ہونے لگے تو نماز مکروہ ہونے
The first time of Fajr is when the second dawn appears, which is the white light spreading across the horizon, and its last time is as long as the sun has not risen. The first time of Zuhr is when the sun declines. Proof (1): The verse 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at appointed times' (4:103). Proof (2): The verse 'And exalt [Allah] with praise of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting' (20:130). Proof (3): The hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub: 'Do not let the adhan of Bilal or this whiteness (the vertical column of dawn) deceive you until it spreads like this' (Muslim, Abu Dawud). Proof (4): The verse 'And eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn' (2:187). And its last time according to Abu Hanifa is when the shadow of everything becomes twice its length excluding the shadow of zenith. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: when the shadow of everything becomes equal to its length. The first time of Asr is when the time of Zuhr exits according to the two opinions, and its last time is as long as the sun has not set. Proof (1): The hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Jibril led me in prayer at the House twice...' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). Proof (2): The verse 'And exalt [Allah] with praise of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting' (20:130). Proof (3): The hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches a rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr' (Bukhari, Tirmidhi). Principles: Time is a condition for prayer; if there is no time, prayer is not obligatory; obligation occurs when time enters. Principles: Zuhr time lasts until Asr, and Asr time lasts until Maghrib; but when the sun becomes yellow, prayer becomes makruh.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the classical Hanafi matn of al-Quduri, accompanied by hadith and usul commentary. The author first defines the time of Fajr: it begins with the true dawn (al-fajr al-thani), which is the horizontal whiteness spreading across the horizon, and ends at sunrise. Four proofs are cited: two verses from Surah an-Nisa and Surah Taha emphasizing fixed prayer times, a hadith warning against the false dawn (the vertical column of light), and the fasting verse from Surah al-Baqarah that uses the same dawn to mark the start of fasting. For Zuhr, the first time is when the sun passes its zenith (zawal). A key intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Zuhr time ends when the shadow of an object becomes twice its length (excluding the zenith shadow), while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it ends when the shadow equals the object's height. This difference affects the beginning of Asr, which starts when Zuhr time ends according to either opinion. Asr time continues until sunset. The hadith of Jibril (Ibn Abbas) is the primary proof for these timings, showing the Prophet being led in prayer at different times on two consecutive days. The hadith of Abu Hurayrah confirms that one who catches a rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise or a rak'ah of Asr before sunset has performed the prayer in time. Finally, two Urdu usul notes remind that time is a condition for prayer obligation, and that while Zuhr time extends into Asr and Asr into Maghrib, praying when the sun turns yellow is disliked (makruh). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the end of Zuhr when shadow equals length) because it is based on the hadith of Jibril and is easier for the community.

Key Terms
الفجر الثاني (al-fajr al-thani): The true dawn which is the horizontal whiteness spreading across the horizon, as opposed to the false dawn (al-fajr al-awwal) which is vertical.
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The shadow remaining at zenith when the sun is at its highest point, which is subtracted when measuring shadow lengths for prayer times.
البياض المعترض (al-bayad al-mu'tarid): The spreading whiteness of dawn horizontally across the horizon, marking the entry of Fajr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what indicates the beginning of Fajr time?
A) The appearance of a vertical column of light.
B) The spreading of white light horizontally across the horizon.
C) The adhan of Bilal.
D) The dawn after sunrise.

Key Takeaway
Prayer times are defined by clear natural indicators; the end of Zuhr is disputed within the Hanafi school, with the mufta bihi being the Sahibayn's view (equal shadow).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Zuhr End Time: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Ruling on end of Zuhr time with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the end time of Zuhr according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute by analyzing the hadith of Jibril.

Core Idea
Zuhr ends at double shadow for Abu Hanifa, at equal shadow for the Sahibayn — both derive from Jibril's second leading.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the end of Zuhr time. While both Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) agree that Zuhr begins at zawal, they differ on the precise moment it ends and Asr begins. The difference hinges on how they interpret the same hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer twice. Understanding this dispute refines your ability to apply prayer times and appreciate the internal diversity of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate in the text the exact wording for Abu Hanifa's position (shadow twice the height) and the Sahibayn's position (shadow equal to height). Note that both exclude the midday shadow (fay' al-zawal).
The phrase 'siwa fay'i al-zawal' is crucial for Hanafi measurement.
2
Locate the common dalil
Find the hadith of Jibril. It describes two prayer sessions: in the first, Zuhr was at a very small shadow and Asr at equal shadow; in the second, Zuhr was at equal shadow and Asr at double shadow.
This hadith is the proof for both views.
3
Analyze the interpretation difference
Explain how Abu Hanifa takes the second session as the definitive end: Zuhr ends when shadow is double (since Jibril prayed Asr then). The Sahibayn take the first session as the end: Zuhr ends when shadow is equal (since Jibril prayed Asr then).
Abu Hanifa sees the first as early time (mustahab) and second as end; Sahibayn see first as end and second as last possible time.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if someone prays Zuhr when shadow equals height, is it valid? According to Abu Hanifa, Zuhr time has ended so the prayer would be a missed Zuhr (qada). According to Sahibayn, it is still Zuhr time so the prayer is on time.
The mufta bihi follows Sahibayn out of caution.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa relies on the Sahibayn (equal shadow) to avoid uncertainty. The text of al-Quduri presents both views without explicit tarjih, but the school's operative position is the Sahibayn's.
See commentaries like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah for tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَآخِرُ وَقْتِهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِذَا صَارَ ظِلُّ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ مِثْلَيْهِ سِوَى فِيءِ الزَّوَالِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ إِذَا صَارَ ظِلُّ كُلّ شَيْءٍ مِثْلَهُ . وَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الْعَصْرِ إِذَا خَرَجَ وَقْتُ الظُّهْرِ عَلَى الْقَوْلَيْنِ وَآخِرُ وَقْتِهَا مَا لَمْ تَغْرُبُ الشَّمْسُ . أَخْبَرَنِي ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ : " أَمَّنِي جِبْرِيلُ عِنْدَ البَيْتِ مَرَّتَيْنِ، فَصَلَّى الظُّهْرَ فِي الْأُولَى مِنْهُمَا حِينَ كَانَ الفَيْءُ مِثْلَ الشَّرَاكِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى العَصْرَ حِينَ كَانَ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ مِثْلَ ظِلِهِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى المَغْرِبَ حِينَ وَجَبَتِ الشَّمْسُ وَأَفْطَرَ الصَّائِمُ ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى العِشَاءَ حِينَ غَابَ الشَّفَقُ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الفَجْرَ حِينَ بَرَقَ الفَجْرُ، وَحَرُمَ الطَّعَامُ عَلَى الصَّائِمِ، وَصَلَّى المَرَّةَ الثَّانِيَةَ الظُّهْرَ حِينَ كَانَ ظِلُّ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ مِثْلَهُ لِوَقْتِ العَصْرِ بِالْأَمْسِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى العَصْرَ حِينَ كَانَ ظِلُّ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ مِثْلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ لِوَقْتِهِ الْأَوَّلِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى العِشَاءَ الآخِرَةَ حِينَ ذَهَبَ ثُلُثُ اللَّيْلِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الصُّبْحَ حِينَ أَسْفَرَتِ الْأَرْضُ، ثُمَّ التَفَتَ إِلَيَّ جِبْرِيلُ، فَقَالَ : يَا مُحَمَّدُ، هَذَا وَقْتُ الأَنْبِيَاءِ مِنْ قَبْلِكَ، وَالوَقْتُ فِيمَا بَيْنَ هَذَيْنِ الْوَقْتَيْنِ "(سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مَوَاقِيتِ الصَّلَاةِ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر149/ابوداؤد، بَابٌ في الْمَوَاقِيتِ، نمبر (393) وَسَبِّحْ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّكَ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَقَبْلَ غُرُوبِهَا وَمِنْ ءَانَايِ الَّيْلِ فَسَبِّحْ وَأَطْرَافَ النَّهَارِ لَعَلَّكَ تَرْضَى (سورة طه 20 آيت نمبر 130) عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ أَدْرَكَ مِنَ الصُّبْحِ رَكْعَةً قَبْلَ أَنْ تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ ، فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الصُّبْحَ، وَمَنْ أَدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مِنَ العَصْرِ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ، فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ العَصْرَ» (بخاري بَابُ مَنْ أَدْرَكَ مِنَ الْفَجْرِ رَكْعَةً، نمبر 579/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أَدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مِنَ العَصْرِ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ، نمبر 186)
And the end of its time according to Abu Hanifa is when the shadow of everything becomes twice its length excluding the declination shadow. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: when the shadow of everything becomes equal to its length. And the beginning of Asr time is when Zuhr time ends according to the two opinions. And the end of its time is as long as the sun has not set. Ibn Abbas informed me that the Prophet said: 'Jibril led me in prayer at the House twice. He prayed Zuhr in the first time when the shade was like sandal straps, then he prayed Asr when everything's shadow was like its length...' and the verse: 'And glorify the praises of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting...' and from Abu Huraira: the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught Fajr, and whoever catches a rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr.'
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the end time of Zuhr and the beginning of Asr. It first states the ruling: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Zuhr time ends when the shadow of any object becomes twice its height (excluding the shadow at midday). According to the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), it ends when the shadow equals the height. Asr begins immediately after Zuhr time ends on both opinions, and its end is sunset. The proof cited is the famous hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet twice: in the first, Jibril prayed Zuhr when the shadow was very small (like sandal straps) and Asr when each thing's shadow was equal to its height; in the second, he prayed Zuhr when the shadow was equal to the height (i.e., the end of Zuhr time according to the Sahibayn) and Asr when the shadow was double (i.e., according to Abu Hanifa). This indicates that both times are permissible. The verse from Surah Taha (130) mentions glorification before sunrise and before sunset, indicating the times for Fajr and Asr. The hadith of Abu Huraira establishes that the end of Asr is sunset, as catching a rak'ah before sunset means the prayer is valid.

Key Terms
فَيْءُ الزَّوَالِ (fay' al-zawal): The shadow at midday when the sun is at its zenith; excluded from shadow measurement for prayer times.
ظِلُّ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ مِثْلَيْهِ (zillu kulli shay'in mithlayhi): When the shadow of any object is twice its height (excluding midday shadow), marking the end of Zuhr time according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does Zuhr time end?
A) When the shadow of everything is equal to its height
B) When the shadow of everything is twice its height, excluding the midday shade
C) When the sun begins to decline from the zenith
D) When the shadow is three times the height

Key Takeaway
The end of Zuhr time is disputed within the Hanafi school; the relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's (equal shadow), out of caution.

Maghrib Time and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Shafaq
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on definition of shafaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for Maghrib time and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the definition of shafaq, citing the relevant hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Maghrib time ends when shafaq disappears, but what is shafaq? Redness or whiteness determines when Isha begins.

This passage from Al-Quduri establishes the ruling for Maghrib prayer time: it begins at sunset and ends with the disappearance of shafaq (twilight). It then introduces a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa defines shafaq as the white twilight after sunset, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), define it as the red twilight. The passage provides multiple hadith to support each position, making this a rich example of how the Hanafi school uses textual evidence and resolves internal differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the first sentence to extract the beginning and end of Maghrib time. Note that the ruling is clear: Maghrib begins at sunset and ends when shafaq disappears.
The ruling is straightforward; the dispute is about the definition of shafaq, not the ruling itself.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa says shafaq is the white twilight (al-bayad), while the Sahibayn say it is the red twilight (al-humrah). Understand that this affects when Maghrib time ends and thus when Isha begins.
This is an example of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, not between schools.
3
Analyze the hadith proofs for each position
For each hadith cited, determine which position it supports. The hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly defines shafaq as redness, supporting the Sahibayn. The practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz uses whiteness for Isha, supporting Abu Hanifa. The other hadiths are neutral but relevant.
Pay attention to the wording: 'shafaq al-humrah' vs 'bayad al-ufuq'.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative view)
Understand that although Abu Hanifa's view is part of Zahir al-Riwayah, later Hanafi jurists (e.g., Al-Quduri himself in his commentary) adopted the Sahibayn's view, making it the relied-upon position for fatwa. Note the authority weight.
The tarjih (preference) is based on the strength of the hadith evidence.
5
Apply the practical consequence
Recognize that the difference in definition changes the end time of Maghrib and start time of Isha in practice. In many Hanafi communities today, Isha is prayed after the redness disappears (Sahibayn), which is earlier than waiting for whiteness.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical fruit of the dispute).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الْمَغْرِبِ إِذَا غَرَبَتْ الشَّمْسُ وَآخِرُ وَقْتِهَا مَا لَمْ يَعِبُ الشَّفَقُ فِي وَهُوَ الْبَيَاضُ الَّذِي فِي الْأُفُق بَعْدَ الحُمْرَةِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ هُوَ الخَمْرَةُ . عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، أَنَّ نَبِيَّ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، قَالَ: «إِذَا صَلَّيْتُمُ الْمَغْرِبَ فَإِنَّهُ وَقْتُ إِلَى أَنْ يَسْقُطُ الشَّفَقُ» (مسلم شريف، بَابُ أَوْقَاتِ الصَّلَوَاتِ الْخَمْسِ، نمبر 612/ سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مَوَاقِيتِ الصَّلَاةِ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر 151). سَمِعْتُ أَبَا مَسْعُودٍ الْأَنْصَارِيُّ يَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: وَيُصَلِّي الْمَغْرِبَ حِينَ تَسْقُطُ الشَّمْسُ وَيُصَلِّي الْعِشَاءَ حِينَ يَسْوَدُّ الْأُفُقُ، وَرُبَّمَا أَخَّرَهَا حَتَّى يَجْتَمِعَ النَّاسُ (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْمَوَاقِيتِ،نمبر 394). كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ: «أَنْ صَلُّوا صَلَاةَ الْعِشَاءِ إِذَا ذَهَبَ بَيَاضُ الْأُفُقِ، فِيمَا بَيْنَكُمْ وَبَيْنَ ثُلُثِ اللَّيْلِ، وَمَا عَجَّلْتُمْ بَعْدَ ذَهَابِ الْأُفُقِ فَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، بَابُ وَقْتِ الْعِشَاءِ الْآخِرَةِ، غبر (2110). عَن ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الشَّفَقُ الْحُمْرَةُ فَإِذَا غَابَ الشَّفَقُ وَجَبَتِ الصَّلَاةُ» (سنن دارقطني، بَابٌ في صِفَةِ الْمَغْرِبِ وَالصُّبْحِ، نمبر 1056).
And the beginning of Maghrib time is when the sun sets, and the end of its time is as long as the shafaq has not disappeared. It is the whiteness in the horizon after the redness. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: it is the redness. From Abdullah ibn Amr that the Prophet said: 'When you pray Maghrib, it is time until the shafaq falls.' ...
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for Maghrib prayer time: it begins at sunset and ends with the disappearance of shafaq (twilight). It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of shafaq. Imam Abu Hanifa defines it as the whiteness (al-bayad) that appears after the redness, i.e., the white twilight. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad define it as the redness (al-humrah) itself. The proofs include hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr stating Maghrib time until shafaq falls, hadith from Abu Mas'ud indicating that Maghrib is at sunset and Isha when the horizon darkens, and the statement of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz (a tabi'i) that Isha is when the whiteness of the horizon disappears. The hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly defines shafaq as 'al-humrah' (redness), supporting the Sahibayn's view. The legal consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, the Maghrib time extends longer (until white twilight), so Isha begins later; according to Sahibayn, Maghrib ends earlier (with disappearance of red twilight).

Key Terms
الشَّفَقُ (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; disputed whether it is the redness or the following whiteness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school, what is the definition of shafaq that determines the end of Maghrib time?
A) The whiteness on the horizon after sunset
B) The redness on the horizon after sunset
C) The complete darkness of the sky
D) The absence of any color in the sky

Key Takeaway
Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight (shafaq) according to the operative Hanafi view, and the dispute with Abu Hanifa's whiteness definition shows how evidence leads to tarjih within the school.

Isha Time: When Does It Begin and End?
Ruling on Isha prayer times with intra-Hanafi start time dispute and hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning and end of Isha time according to the Hanafi school and identify the hadith proof that establishes its end time.

Core Idea
Isha time begins when shafaq disappears and ends at true dawn — the Prophet's delay proves the time extends.

In this passage, Al-Quduri states the ruling on Isha prayer time and supports it with the well-known hadith of Aisha. We will explore the two definitions of shafaq that affect the start time and note that the end time is unanimously true dawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the prayer time for Isha. Determine what is being ruled: the beginning and end of the time.
Prayer times are conditions for the validity of salah.
2
Understand the start time dispute
The text says 'according to the two opinions.' Recognize that this refers to the definition of shafaq: Abu Hanifa considers white twilight; the Sahibayn consider red twilight.
The relied-upon position is the earlier time (red twilight).
3
Note the end time
The passage states the end time is the rising of the second dawn (true dawn). This is agreed upon and not disputed.
Do not confuse with midnight; the time extends until Fajr.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith of Aisha shows the Prophet delayed Isha until late night. However, this does not mean the time ends at midnight; rather it shows the time extends until dawn.
The hadith is used to prove the extension, not to recommend delay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الْعِشَاءِ إِذَا غَابَ الشَّفَقُ عَلَى الْقَوْلَيْنِ وَآخِرُ وَقْتِهَا مَا لَمْ يَطْلُعْ الْفَجْرُ الثَّانِي . عَنْ عَائِشَةَ؛ قَالَتْ: أَعْتَمَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ذَاتَ لَيْلَةٍ. حَتَّى ذَهَبَ عَامَّةُ اللَّيْلِ. وَحَتَّى نَامَ أَهْلُ الْمَسْجِدِ (مسلم شريف، بَاب وَقْتِ الْعِشَاءِ وَتَأْخِيرهَا، نمبر 638).
And the beginning of Isha time is when the shafaq disappears according to the two opinions, and the end of its time is as long as the second dawn has not risen. From Aisha: she said: 'The Prophet delayed Isha one night until a great portion of the night had passed, and until the people of the mosque slept.'
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for Isha prayer time: it begins with the disappearance of shafaq (twilight) based on the two definitions of shafaq (redness or whiteness), and it ends at the break of true dawn (al-fajr al-thani). The hadith of Aisha is cited as proof that the Prophet delayed Isha until late night, showing that the time extends, but it also indicates that it is permissible to delay. However, the Hanafi school considers delaying Isha without excuse as makruh (disliked). The saying 'according to the two opinions' refers to the earlier ikhtilaf on shafaq: for Abu Hanifa, the disappearance of white twilight means later Isha time; for the Sahibayn, the disappearance of red twilight means earlier Isha time.

Key Terms
الْفَجْرُ الثَّانِي (al-fajr al-thani): The true dawn; the second light that spreads horizontally across the horizon, marking the end of Isha and the beginning of Fajr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does Isha time end according to the Hanafi school?
A) At midnight
B) When the second dawn (true dawn) rises
C) When the sun rises
D) When half the night has passed

Key Takeaway
Isha time begins with the disappearance of shafaq (according to the relied-upon view, red twilight) and ends at the emergence of true dawn.

Recommended Times for Fajr and Zuhr
States recommended delay for Fajr and Zuhr in summer, early Zuhr in winter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on isfar for Fajr and ibrad for Zuhr, and identify the hadith evidence supporting each.

Core Idea
Pray Fajr when light spreads and delay Zuhr in summer heat – both are recommended, not obligatory.

This lesson examines two recommended practices in prayer timing: delaying Fajr until the dawn is bright (isfar) and postponing Zuhr in summer until the intense heat subsides (ibrad). Al-Quduri states these as mustahabb, supported by explicit commands and practices of the Prophet (saw) and the Companions. Understanding the evidence and the level of obligation helps avoid misunderstanding these as compulsory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What action is being ruled upon? Determine the hukm level (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.) for isfar with Fajr and ibrad with Zuhr.
The text says 'yustahabb' (recommended), indicating sunnah, not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith quoted: for Fajr, the command 'asfiru bi al-fajr'; for Zuhr, the command to delay in heat. Note the references to Bukhari, Muslim, and Tirmidhi.
Ahadith are from authoritative collections but are ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the imperative prove recommendation? Hanafi usul interprets al-amr as wujub unless there is a qarinah (context) shifting it to nadb. The practice of the women (coming in darkness) and the explanation 'greater reward' indicate recommendation, not obligation.
The Prophet's own practice, as reported by Anas, confirms the recommendation.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
Is this ruling agreed upon? All schools generally accept isfar and ibrad as recommended. There is no significant ikhtilaf.
Some Shafi'is prefer early Fajr, but the Hanafi position is sound.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, should one wait for full light for Fajr or delay Zuhr in summer? Yes, as sunnah mu'akkadah. In winter, Zuhr may be prayed early.
The allowance for seasonal adjustment is based on the hadith from Anas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ الإِسْفَارُ بِالْفَجْرِ وَالْإِبْرَادُ بِالظُّهْرِ فِي الصَّيْفِ وَتَقْدِيمُهَا فِي الشَّتَاءِ . وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت عَنْ رَافِعِ بْنِ خَدِيجٍ، قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «أَسْفِرُوا بِالفَجْرِ، فَإِنَّهُ أَعْظَمُ لِلأَجْرِ» (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الإِسْفَارِ بِالفَجْرِ، نمبر 154/ سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي وَقْتِ الصُّبْحِ، نمبر 424) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت أَنَّ عَائِشَةَ أَخْبَرَتْهُ قَالَتْ: «كُنَّ نِسَاءُ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ يَشْهَدْنَ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَاةَ الْفَجْرِ، مُتَلَفِعَاتٍ بِمُرُوطِهِنَّ، ثُمَّ يَنْقَلِبْنَ إِلَى بُيُوتِهِنَّ حِينَ يَقْضِينَ الصَّلَاةَ لَا يَعْرِفُهُنَّ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْغَلَسِ» (بخاري شريف، بَابُ وَقْتِ الْفَجْرِ، نمبر 578/ مسلم شريف بَاب اسْتِحْبَابِ التَّبْكِيرِ بِالصُّبْحِ فِي أَوَّلِ وَقْتِهَا، نمبر 645) ووجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ : أَنَّهُمَا حَدَّثَاهُ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «إِذَا اشْتَدَّ الْحَرُّ فَأَبْرِدُوا عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ، فَإِنَّ شِدَّةَ الخَرِ مِنْ فَيْح جَهَنَّمَ» (بخاري شريف بَابٌ : الْإِبْرَادُ بِالظُّهْرِ فِي شِدَّةِ الخَرِ، نمبر 533/ سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تَأْخِيرِ الظُّهْرِ فِي شِدَّةِ الحَرِ، نمبر 157) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت سَمِعْتُ أَنَسَ بْنَ مَالِكِ يَقُولُ: «كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا اشْتَدَّ الْبَرْدُ بَكَّرَ بِالصَّلَاةِ، وَإِذَا اشْتَدَّ الْخُرُّ أَبْرَدَ بِالصَّلَاةِ، يَعْنِي الظُّهْرَ» (بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : إِذَا اشْتَدَّ الْخَرُّ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ، نمبر 906) اصول : گرمی اور سردی میں موسم کے اعتبار سے ظہر کی نماز کو دیر سے پڑھنے اور جلدی کرنے کی گنجائش ہے۔
It is recommended to pray Fajr when it is light (isfar) and to delay Zuhr in summer and to pray it early in winter. Aspect (1): Hadith for establishing from Rafi' ibn Khadij: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Make Fajr light, for that is greater in reward.' Aspect (2): Hadith for establishing from 'Aisha: she informed that the believing women used to attend Fajr prayer with the Messenger of Allah wrapped in their cloaks, then they would return to their homes after finishing the prayer, not being recognized due to the darkness (ghalas). Aspect (1): Hadith for establishing from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar: they narrated from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'When the heat is severe, postpone the prayer until it cools, for severe heat is from the blast of Hell.' Aspect (2): Hadith for establishing: I heard Anas ibn Malik say: 'When it was very cold, the Prophet would pray early, and when it was very hot, he would postpone the prayer,' meaning Zuhr. Principle: In summer and winter, according to the season, there is allowance to delay or hasten Zuhr prayer.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended times for Fajr and Zuhr prayers. For Fajr, it is recommended to pray it later when there is light (isfar) rather than in the deep darkness (ghalas). The hadith from Rafi' directly commands isfar, and the practice of the women indicates they prayed early but still in some darkness; the command is interpreted as recommended. For Zuhr, in summer it is recommended to delay until the heat subsides (ibrad), while in winter it is recommended to pray early. The hadith from Ibn 'Umar and Anas support this. The Urdu note summarizes the allowance for seasonal adjustment.

Key Terms
الإسْفَار (al-isar): Praying Fajr when the dawn light is bright enough that objects become visible, as opposed to deep darkness (ghalas).
الإبْرَاد (al-ibrad): Delaying Zuhr prayer until the intense heat of midday subsides, in summer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Combine it with 'Asr

Key Takeaway
Isfar for Fajr and ibrad for Zuhr in summer are confirmed sunnah practices based on prophetic commands and practice.

The Time of Witr Prayer and Its Proofs
States Witr time and provides two hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time of Witr prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the hadith evidence for this time.

Core Idea
Witr time spans from after 'Isha until before dawn, as proven by prophetic hadith.

In this passage, the Hanafi matn of al-Quduri states the time for Witr prayer, supported by two hadith. The first hadith directly defines the period, while the second shows the Prophet's practice across the night. Understanding this time is essential for performing this wajib prayer correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on Witr time
From the matn, identify the beginning and end times for Witr prayer.
The text states 'first time after 'Isha, last time before dawn'.
2
Analyze the first hadith (Kharaja ibn Hudhafa)
Read the hadith and identify the phrase that defines the time period.
The key phrase is 'between the prayer of 'Isha until the dawn appears'.
3
Examine the second hadith ('Aisha)
This hadith shows the Prophet performed Witr at various times, ending at dawn.
It confirms the entire night is permissible.
4
Connect to Hanafi fiqh
Recognize that in the Hanafi school, Witr is wajib, and the time is as stated.
Other schools may differ in classification but agree on time generally.
5
Apply to daily practice
Understand that Witr can be performed any time after 'Isha, but the latter part of the night is recommended.
The mufta bihi is that time ends at dawn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الْوِتْرِ بَعْدَ الْعِشَاءِ وَآخِرُ وَقْتِهَا مَا لَمْ يَطْلُعْ الْفَجْرُ . كوجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت عَنْ خَارِجَةَ بْنِ حُذَافَةَ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ: خَرَجَ عَلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ ، فَقَالَ : " إِنَّ اللَّهَ أَمَدَّكُمْ بِصَلَاةٍ هِيَ خَيْرٌ لَكُمْ مِنْ حُمْرِ النَّعَمِ الوِتْرُ، جَعَلَهُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ فِيمَا بَيْنَ صَلَاةِ العِشَاءِ إِلَى أَنْ يَطْلُعَ الفَجْرُ، (سنن ترمذی، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي فَضْلِ الوِتْرِ ، نمبر 452/ سنن ابوداود بَابُ اسْتِحْبَابِ الْوِتْرِ ، نمبر 1418) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت عَنْ مَسْرُوقٍ، أَنَّهُ سَأَلَ عَائِشَةَ عَنْ وِتْرِ رَسُولِ اللهِ ؟ فَقَالَتْ: «مِنْ كُلِ اللَّيْلِ قَدْ أَوْتَرَ أَوَّلَهُ، وَأَوْسَطَهُ، وَآخِرَهُ، فَانْتَهَى وِتْرُهُ حِينَ مَاتَ إِلَى السَّحَرِ،(،(سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الوِتْرِ مِنْ أَوَّلِ اللَّيْلِ وَآخِرِهِ، نمبر 456) اصول : وتر کی نماز بھی ایک اہم اور واجب نماز ہے اور اس کا وقت عشاء کے بعد سے شروع ہوتا ہے اور آخری وقت فجر تک رہتا ہے۔
The first time of Witr is after 'Isha and the last time of it is before dawn. Evidence: (1) Hadith for establishing from Kharaja ibn Hudhafa that he said: The Messenger of Allah came out to us and said: 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer which is better for you than red camels: the Witr. Allah has made it for you between the prayer of 'Isha until the dawn appears.' (2) Hadith for establishing from Masruq that he asked 'Aisha about the Witr of the Messenger of Allah, and she said: 'He performed Witr throughout the night: its beginning, its middle, and its end. His Witr ended at dawn when he died.' Principle: The Witr prayer is also an important and obligatory prayer, and its time begins after 'Isha and lasts until dawn.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the time of Witr prayer and provides two hadith proofs. The first hadith from Kharaja ibn Hudhafa directly specifies that Witr is between 'Isha and the appearance of dawn, confirming the time described. The second hadith from 'Aisha shows the prophetic practice: the Prophet performed Witr at various times of the night, but his final practice was at the latter part of the night (sahar). This indicates the permissibility throughout the night, with the time ending at dawn. The Urdu note reinforces that it is a wājib prayer and its time is after 'Isha until dawn.

Key Terms
الوِتْر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after 'Isha, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Times for 'Asr, Maghrib, and 'Isha
States recommended delay for 'Asr, early Maghrib, and delayed 'Isha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommended times for 'Asr, Maghrib, and 'Isha and cite the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice sets the sunnah: delay 'Asr while white, hasten Maghrib, delay 'Isha until one-third of the night.

This lesson examines the recommended (sunnah) times for three prayers: 'Asr, Maghrib, and 'Isha, as established by the Hanafi school. The matn of al-Quduri states these preferences concisely, and the commentary provides hadith evidence from the Prophet's actual practice. Understanding these times helps one follow the sunnah and avoid common errors in timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prayers and their recommended timings
From the matn, extract the Hanafi position: delay 'Asr while sun is white, hasten Maghrib immediately, delay 'Isha until before one-third of the night.
These are sunnah mu'akkadah, not obligations.
2
Examine the hadith evidence for 'Asr
Read the two hadith: one from Ali ibn Shayban describing the Prophet's practice, and another from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari. Note the description 'white and clear' before yellowing.
Action (fi'l) of the Prophet indicates recommendation.
3
Examine the hadith evidence for Maghrib
Read the hadith from Abu Ayyub quoting the Prophet: 'My ummah will continue in goodness as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine.' This implies hastening is recommended.
Warning against delay shows the disliked nature of delaying.
4
Examine the hadith evidence for 'Isha
Read the hadith from Abu Hurayrah: The Prophet said he would have commanded delay except for hardship. This indicates it is recommended but not obligatory.
Conditional command implies obligation if not for hardship.
5
Synthesize the ruling from the proofs
Each hadith establishes the recommended time. The principle: the Prophet's actions and sayings provide the basis for sunnah rulings. Delaying 'Isha is sunnah mu'akkadah because the Prophet almost made it compulsory.
The Urdu note also clarifies the start and end times for 'Isha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَأْخِيرُ الْعَصْرِ مَا لَمْ تَتَغَيَّرِ الشَّمْسُ وَتَعْجِيلُ الْمَغْرِبِ وَتَأْخِيرُ الْعِشَاءِ إِلَى مَا قَبْلَ ثلث الليل. وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَتَأْخِيرُ الْعَصْرِ مَا لَمْ تَتَغَيَّرُ الشَّمْسُ عَنْ عَلِيَّ بْنِ شَيْبَانَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ عَلِي بْنِ شَيْبَانَ قَالَ: «قَدِمْنَا عَلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمَدِينَةَ فَكَانَ يُؤَخِّرُ الْعَصْرَ مَا دَامَتِ الشَّمْسُ بَيْضَاءَ نَقِيَّةً» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي وَقْتِ صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ،نمبر408) وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَتَأْخِيرُ الْعَصْرِ مَا لَمَّ تَتَغَيَّرُ الشَّمْسُ سَمِعْتُ أَبَا مَسْعُودٍ الْأَنْصَارِيَّ يَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ ..... وَرَأَيْتُهُ يُصَلِّي الْعَصْرَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ بَيْضَاءُ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَدْخُلَهَا الصُّفْرَةُ ، فَيَنْصَرِفُ الرَّجُلُ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ فَيَأْتي ذَا الْحُلَيْفَةِ قَبْلَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسُ وَيُصَلِّي الْمَغْرِبَ حِينَ تَسْقُطُ الشَّمْسُ ، وَيُصَلِّي الْعِشَاءَ حِينَ يَسْوَدُّ الْأُفُقُ وَرُبَّمَا أَخَّرَهَا حَتَّى يَجْتَمِعَ النَّاسُ (سنن دارقطني، بَابُ ذِكْرٍ بَيَانِ الْمَوَاقِيتِ وَاخْتِلَافِ الرِّوَايَاتِ فِي ذَلِكَ ، نمبر 986) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَتَعْجِيلُ الْمَغْرِبِ أَقَامَ إِلَيْهِ أَبُو أَيُّوب، فَقَالَ: لَهُ مَا هَذِهِ الصَّلَاةُ يَا عُقْبَةُ، فَقَالَ: شُغِلْنَا، قَالَ: أَمَا سَمِعْتَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «لَا تَزَالُ أُمَّتِي بِخَيْرٍ» أَوْ قَالَ: «عَلَى الْفِطْرَةِ» مَا لَمْ يُؤَخِّرُوا الْمَغْرِبَ إِلَى أَنْ تَشْتَبِكَ النُّجُومُ (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي وَقْتِ الْمَغْرِبِ، نمبر 618 سنن ابن ماجه بَابُ الْقِرَاءَةِ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ ، نمبر 689) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَتَأْخِيرُ الْعِشَاءِ إِلَى مَا قَبْلَ ثُلُثِ اللَّيْلِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ : «لَوْلَا أَنْ أَشُقَّ عَلَى أُمَّتِي لَأَمَرْتُهُمْ أَنْ يُؤَخِّرُوا العِشَاءَ إِلَى ثُلُثِ اللَّيْلِ أَوْ نِصْفِهِ» (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تَأْخِيرِ الْعِشَاءِ الْآخِرَةِ ،نمبر 167) اصول : عشاء کا اول وقت شفق کے غروب سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے اور آخری وقت فجر تک ہے۔
Delay 'Asr as long as the sun has not changed; hasten Maghrib; delay 'Isha until before one-third of the night. Aspect (1): Hadith for establishing delaying 'Asr as long as the sun has not changed from 'Ali ibn Shayban, from his father, from his grandfather 'Ali ibn Shayban: 'We came to the Messenger of Allah in Madinah, and he used to delay 'Asr as long as the sun was white and clear.' Aspect (2): Hadith for establishing delaying 'Asr as long as the sun has not changed from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: I heard the Messenger of Allah say... and I saw him pray 'Asr with the sun high and white before it became yellow, and a man would leave the prayer and come to Dhu'l-Hulayfah before sunset, and he would pray Maghrib when the sun set, and he would pray 'Isha when the horizon became dark, and sometimes he delayed it until people gathered. Aspect (1): Hadith for establishing hastening Maghrib from Abu Ayyub: He said to 'Uqbah: 'What is this prayer?' He said: 'We were busy.' He said: 'Did you not hear the Messenger of Allah say: My ummah will continue in goodness - or he said: on fitrah - as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine.' Aspect (1): Hadith for establishing delaying 'Isha until before one-third of the night from Abu Hurayrah: The Prophet said: 'Were it not that I would burden my ummah, I would command them to delay 'Isha until one-third or half of the night.' Principle: The first time of 'Isha begins with the disappearance of the twilight (shafaq) and the last time is dawn.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage covers the recommended times for 'Asr, Maghrib, and 'Isha prayers. For 'Asr, it is recommended to delay it while the sun remains white and has not turned yellow; the hadith describe the Prophet's practice. For Maghrib, it is recommended to pray it immediately after sunset, not delaying until the stars appear; the hadith warns against delaying. For 'Isha, it is recommended to delay it until about one-third of the night, as the Prophet refrained from commanding it only out of concern for hardship. The Urdu note mentions the beginning of 'Isha time with the disappearance of twilight and its end at dawn.

Key Terms
تأخير العصر (ta'khir al-'asr): Delaying 'Asr prayer within its time while the sun remains white and bright before it changes to yellow.
تعجيل المغرب (ta'jil al-maghrib): Hastening Maghrib prayer immediately after sunset, without delay.
تأخير العشاء (ta'khir al-'isha): Delaying 'Isha prayer until about one-third of the night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying 'Asr while the sun is white, hastening Maghrib, and delaying 'Isha until one-third of the night, all based on the Prophet's practice and sayings.

Recommended Timings for Asr, Maghrib, and Isha
Matn with hadith proofs for recommended prayer times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended timings for Asr, Maghrib, and Isha according to the Hanafi school and identify the hadith evidence for these timings.

Core Idea
Delay Asr while sun is white, hasten Maghrib, delay Isha to one-third night — all sunnah, not fard.

This passage from al-Quduri outlines preferred times for three prayers. While each prayer has a fixed window, the Prophet's practice (sunnah) recommends specific moments within that window. Understanding these rulings helps you follow the Sunnah with precision and avoid common misconceptions about obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each prayer (Asr, Maghrib, Isha), note whether the text recommends ta'khir (delay) or ta'jil (hastening). Classify the ruling as mustahabb (recommended), not fard.
The prayer itself is fard; the timing preference is sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil for each timing
Trace each hadith: For Asr, the Prophet's practice of delaying while sun was white; for Maghrib, his warning against delay until stars appear; for Isha, his statement about delaying if not for hardship.
All hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for recommendation.
3
Trace how the dalil indicates recommendation
The Prophet's fi'l (action) for Asr and Isha shows recommendation; for Maghrib, the explicit qaul (saying) praises those who pray early; for Isha, the conditional 'lawla' indicates permissibility not obligation.
Hanafi usul: al-amr (imperative) would indicate obligation, but here there is no imperative.
4
Note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school prefers earlier Asr (shadow equal length) and earlier Isha, based on other hadith. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith cited here.
Both positions are valid; the difference is in the evidence preferred.
5
Confirm the Hanafi mufta bihi
The recommended timings are established in Zahir al-Riwayah and are followed in practice. They are mustahabb, not obligatory.
If one prays outside these recommended times but within the valid time, the prayer is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَأْخِيرُ الْعَصْرِ مَا لَمْ تَتَغَيَّرِ الشَّمْسُ، وَتَعْجِيلُ الْمَغْرِبِ، وَتَأْخِيرُ الْعِشَاءِ إِلَى مَا قَبْلَ ثُلُثِ اللَّيْلِ.
عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ شَيْبَانَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ قَالَ: قَدِمْنَا عَلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمَدِينَةَ فَكَانَ يُؤَخِّرُ الْعَصْرَ مَا دَامَتِ الشَّمْسُ بَيْضَاءَ نَقِيَّةً. (سنن أبي داود)
وَعَنْ أَبِي مَسْعُودٍ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ ... وَرَأَيْتُهُ يُصَلِّي الْعَصْرَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ بَيْضَاءُ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَدْخُلَهَا الصُّفْرَةُ. (سنن الدارقطني)
وَعَنْ أَبِي أَيُّوبَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا تَزَالُ أُمَّتِي بِخَيْرٍ» أَوْ قَالَ: «عَلَى الْفِطْرَةِ» مَا لَمْ يُؤَخِّرُوا الْمَغْرِبَ إِلَى أَنْ تَشْتَبِكَ النُّجُومُ. (سنن أبي داود وابن ماجه)
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَوْلَا أَنْ أَشُقَّ عَلَى أُمَّتِي لَأَمَرْتُهُمْ أَنْ يُؤَخِّرُوا الْعِشَاءَ إِلَى ثُلُثِ اللَّيْلِ أَوْ نِصْفِهِ». (سنن الترمذي)
And delaying Asr as long as the sun has not changed color, and hastening Maghrib, and delaying Isha until before one-third of the night. From Ali ibn Shayban from his father from his grandfather: 'We came to Medina to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he used to delay Asr as long as the sun was white and pure.' (Sunan Abu Dawud) And from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say... and I saw him praying Asr while the sun was high, white, before it turned yellow.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni) And from Abu Ayyub that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'My community will continue to be in good' or 'upon the fitrah as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars appear.' (Sunan Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah) And from Abu Hurairah: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: If it were not for the difficulty on my community, I would have commanded them to delay Isha until one-third or half the night.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the matn of al-Quduri, stating recommended (mustahabb) timings for three prayers. First, Asr should be delayed as long as the sun's color has not changed from white to yellow; the hadith of Ali ibn Shayban shows the Prophet would pray Asr while the sun was still white. Second, Maghrib should be prayed immediately after sunset without delay; the hadith warns against delaying until stars appear. Third, Isha may be delayed up to before one-third of the night; the hadith indicates that delaying is recommended but not obligatory to avoid hardship. The Hanafi school considers these timings as sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.

Key Terms
تَأْخِير (ta'khir): Delaying the prayer within its permissible time, considered mustahabb for Asr and Isha.
تَعْجِيل (ta'jil): Praying immediately at the start of the time, mustahabb for Maghrib.
ثُلُثُ اللَّيْل (thuluth al-layl): One-third of the night, calculated from sunset to dawn; delaying Isha until before this point is mustahabb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory (fard) to delay Asr until the sun changes color.
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) to delay Asr as long as the sun is white.
C) It is forbidden (haram) to delay Asr beyond its initial time.
D) It is permissible to delay Asr until just before sunset.

Key Takeaway
The recommended timings for Asr, Maghrib, and Isha are established by hadith and are mustahabb, not fard.

Salah — Prayer

Recommended Time for Witr Prayer
Ruling with hadith on preferring to delay Witr for night prayer performers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preferred time for Witr prayer and apply the condition that determines whether to delay or pray before sleep.

Core Idea
Delay Witr to the end of night if confident to wake; otherwise pray before sleep — virtue balanced with practicality.

This lesson addresses a practical concern for the worshipper: when should one pray Witr? The Hanafi school, based on a clear hadith, recommends delaying for those who are regular in night prayer and confident they will wake. But if there is fear of missing the prayer entirely, the ruling shifts to caution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its overall ruling
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school. The lesson focuses on its timing, which is mustahabb (recommended). Understand that timing preference does not change the wajib nature.
Witr's wajib status is distinct from the recommended timing.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The hadith from Jabir (RA) is cited. Identify the key phrases: 'fal-yūtir awwalahu' (let him pray at its beginning) and 'dhālika afḍal' (that is better).
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Ibn Majah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'fal-yūtir' indicates permissibility; the phrase 'dhālika afḍal' establishes preference for delaying. The explicit preference is the basis for the recommendation.
4
Identify the condition
The text adds a condition: 'if he does not trust himself to wake up, he should pray Witr before sleep.' This condition overrides the general recommendation.
The condition is practical, not a legal restriction.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a person's confidence in waking, determine whether to delay Witr or pray early. Know that the default for those confident is delay, but fear of missing triggers early prayer.
The goal is to balance virtue with the risk of missing a wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ فِي الْوِتْرِ لِمَنْ يَأْلَفُ صَلَاةَ اللَّيْلِ أَنْ يُؤَخِّرَهَا إِلَى آخِرِ اللَّيْلِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَثِقُ بِالْإِنْتِبَاهِ: أَوْتَرَ قَبْلَ النَّوْمِ.
عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ خَافَ أَنْ لَا يَقُومَ مِنْ آخِرِ اللَّيْلِ فَلْيُوتِرْ أَوَّلَهُ، وَمَنْ طَمِعَ أَنْ يَقُومَ آخِرَهُ فَلْيُوتِرْ آخِرَ اللَّيْلِ، فَإِنَّ صَلَاةَ آخِرِ اللَّيْلِ مَشْهُودَةٌ، وَذَلِكَ أَفْضَلُ». (مسلم، وابن ماجه)
And it is recommended regarding Witr for one who is accustomed to night prayer to delay it to the end of the night; if he does not trust himself to wake up, he should pray Witr before sleep. From Jabir who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever fears that he will not wake up at the end of the night, let him pray Witr at its beginning, and whoever hopes to wake up at its end, let him pray Witr at the end of the night, for prayer at the end of the night is witnessed, and that is better.' (Muslim and Ibn Majah)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof regarding the preferred time for the Witr prayer. The matn states it is mustahabb (recommended) for those who regularly pray at night (tahajjud) to delay Witr until the end of the night. For those who fear they may not wake up, it is better to pray Witr before sleeping. The hadith of Jabir confirms this: the Prophet explicitly allowed both options but declared Witr at the end of night as afḍal (more virtuous). The Hanafi school adopts this recommendation; Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school and its time is after Isha until dawn. The ruling balances between attaining virtue and practicality.

Key Terms
وِتْر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
يَأْلَفُ صَلَاةَ اللَّيْل (ya'lafu salat al-layl): One who is habituated to performing night prayer (tahajjud) regularly.
ثِقْ بِالْإِنْتِبَاه (thiq bi-al-intibah): Confidence in waking up; if one doubts ability to wake, prayer before sleep is better.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) At the end of the night, before Fajr
C) Before sleeping, regardless of whether they wake
D) Only before midnight

Key Takeaway
Delaying Witr to the end of night is recommended for those confident of waking; otherwise, pray before sleep to avoid missing a wajib.

The Iqama is Like the Adhan with Addition of 'Qad Qamat al-Salah'
Ruling on the wording of iqama with multiple hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact wording of the iqama according to the Hanafi school and identify the single addition compared to the adhan.

Core Idea
The iqama mirrors the adhan word-for-word, but adds 'qad qamat al-salah' twice after 'hayya 'ala al-falah.'

In this lesson, we examine the wording of the iqama, the second call to prayer. According to the Hanafi school, the iqama is essentially the same as the adhan, with one key difference: after 'Hayya 'ala al-falah,' the caller says 'Qad qamat al-salah' twice. This ruling is supported by multiple authentic hadith, which the text presents as proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on iqama wording
The matn states that the iqama is like the adhan except for the addition. Understand that the Hanafis say the iqama is recited in pairs (two repetitions) similar to the adhan.
2
Pinpoint the specific addition
After 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', the caller must add 'Qad qamat al-salah' twice.
3
Review the hadith proofs
The text cites four hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud and Bukhari/Muslim showing that the Prophet (saw) taught Bilal to say it twice.
The hadith from Anas about 'make the iqama odd' is interpreted by Hanafis as meaning the iqama is recited in pairs except for this addition.
4
Understand the usul principle
The Hanafi principle that the iqama mirrors the adhan in repetition (even numbers) except for the added phrase, which is also said twice.

اصول : حنفیہ کے نزدیک اقامت بھی اذان ہی طرح ہے یعنی دو دو مرتبہ کہا جائے۔
L: The iqama is like the adhan, except that he adds in it after 'falah': 'qad qamat al-salah' twice. H: And he should be deliberate in the adhan and swift in the iqama. Proof (1): Hadith for establishing that the iqama is like the adhan except that he adds in it after 'falah': from Ibn Abi Layla from Mu'adh ibn Jabal... then he paused a moment, then stood and said the like, except that he added after saying 'Hayya 'ala al-falah': 'qad qamat al-salah, qad qamat al-salah'. He said: the Messenger of Allah (saw) said: 'Teach it to Bilal.' Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter: How is the adhan, no. 507. Proof (2): Hadith... Proof (3): Hadith 'He taught me the iqama two by two.' Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the iqama, the second call to prayer. The matn (core text) states that the iqama is like the adhan in wording and repetition, except that after 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', one says 'Qad qamat al-salah' twice instead of once. The mas'ala clarifies: the iqama does not repeat the takbir and other phrases like the adhan; only this specific addition differs. The text then provides four hadith proofs from Sunan Abi Dawud and the two Sahihs, showing that the Prophet (saw) taught Bilal to say 'Qad qamat al-salah' twice in the iqama. The Urdu usul note confirms the Hanafi position that the iqama is recited in pairs (two repetitions), consistent with the adhan. The student should understand that this ruling is established by multiple authentic hadith, making it a sunnah mu'akkadah practice.

Key Terms
إِقَامَة (iqāma): The second call to prayer, consisting of similar phrases to the adhan but with the addition of 'qad qamat al-salah' twice after 'hayya 'ala al-falah', and recited more quickly.

The Tathwib: Adding 'Al-Salatu Khayrun min al-Nawm' in Fajr Adhan
Ruling on the Fajr adhan addition with its hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the tathwib in the Fajr adhan, identify its proof, and apply the ruling to determine when the phrase is recited.

Core Idea
The phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is a sunnah addition exclusive to the Fajr adhan.

The Fajr adhan has a unique element that distinguishes it from the adhans of the other four prayers. After the mu'adhdhin calls 'hayya 'ala al-falah', he adds 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' twice. This lesson examines the ruling of this addition and the evidence from the Sunnah that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific addition? What is its legal status? The passage states it is added (yazidu) in the Fajr adhan, indicating it is a sunnah practice.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The passage references a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud. Understand the hadith's content and its chain.
The OCR text is corrupted; the correct hadith is well-known.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the addition? The hadith describes the Prophet's (saw) adhan for Fajr including this phrase.
The hadith's operative part is the description of the adhan.
4
Note the scope
Is this addition only for Fajr? Yes, the text specifies 'in the adhan of Fajr'. Understand that this does not apply to other prayers.

This passage is a ruling with proof on a special addition specific to the Fajr adhan. The matn states that after 'hayya 'ala al-falah', the mu'adhdhin says 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep) twice. This phrase is known as the 'tathwib' and is a sunnah for Fajr only. The hadith cited in the text is meant to support this, although the OCR may have corrupted the hadith content. The correct hadith is well-known: Bilal used to say this phrase in the Fajr adhan and the Prophet (saw) approved it (Sunan Abi Dawud no. 506). The Hanafi school considers this addition as sunnah mu'akkadah for Fajr.

Tarassul in Adhan and Hadr in Iqama
Ruling with proof on pace of adhan and iqama

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended pace for adhan and iqama and explain the evidence from the hadith of the Prophet (saw).

Core Idea
The adhan is recited slowly to reach afar; the iqama is recited swiftly for those present.

The manner of reciting the call to prayer is not left to personal preference; the Prophet (saw) instructed Bilal specifically. This lesson unpacks the ruling that the adhan is to be recited with deliberation (tarassul) and the iqama with swiftness (hadr), supported by a direct hadith and a clear rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: 'He should be deliberate in the adhan and swift in the iqama.' This is the core ruling of the lesson.
The ruling is a recommendation (sunnah), not an obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Jabir: the Prophet (saw) told Bilal to be deliberate when calling the adhan and swift when giving the iqama.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Tirmidhi, classified as hasan.
3
Analyze the imperative
The command 'fa-tarassal' and 'fa-ahdur' are imperatives. In Hanafi usul, an imperative from the Prophet (saw) that is not accompanied by a qarīna of obligation indicates sunnah (recommendation).
Context: the adhan is a call; the iqama is an assembly.
4
Understand the rationale
The Urdu usul note explains: the adhan is meant to reach distant people, so it is recited slowly; the iqama is for those already near, so it is recited quickly.
This rationale is based on the wisdom behind the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه وَيَتَرَسَّلُ فِي الْأَذَانِ وَيَحْدُرُ فِي الْإِقَامَةِ
d. وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَرَسَّلُ فِي الْأَذَانِ وَيَحْدُرُ فِي الْإِقَامَةِ أَعَنْ جَابِرٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ لِبِلَالٍ: «يَا بِلَالُ، إِذَا أَذَنْتَ فَتَرَسَّلْ فِي أَذَانِكَ، وَإِذَا أَقَمْتَ فَاحْدُرْ،(سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّرَسُلِ فِي الأَذَانِ ،نمبر 195)
اصول : اذان میں چونکہ دور آواز پہنچانی ہوتی ہے اسلئے ٹھہر ٹھہر کر دے اور اقامت میں جلدی دے۔
H: And he should be deliberate (tarassul) in the adhan and swift (hadr) in the iqama. d. Proof (1): Hadith for establishing 'and he should be deliberate in the adhan and swift in the iqama': from Jabir that the Messenger of Allah (saw) said to Bilal: 'O Bilal, when you call the adhan, be deliberate in your adhan, and when you give the iqama, be swift.' Urdu principle: Because in the adhan the voice needs to reach a distance, so it should be given slowly, and in the iqama, quickly.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the manner of reciting the adhan and iqama. The matn commands 'tarassul' (deliberateness) in the adhan and 'hadr' (swiftness) in the iqama. Tarassul means pausing between phrases and prolonging the call to allow people to hear and respond. Hadr means reciting quickly in succession, as the iqama is meant to assemble those already present. The hadith from Jabir directly quotes the Prophet (saw) instructing Bilal accordingly. The Urdu usul adds the rationale: the adhan is a call to distances, so it needs slowness; the iqama is for those already near, so it can be fast. This ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
التَّرَسُّل (al-tarassul): Reciting the adhan slowly, with pauses between phrases, to ensure the call reaches distant listeners.
الحَدْر (al-ḥadr): Reciting the iqama quickly, without prolonged pauses, as it is for those already present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Deliberate (tarassul)
C) Loud only
D) It does not matter

Key Takeaway
The adhan is sunnah to recite slowly (tarassul) and the iqama swiftly (hadr), based on the Prophet's instruction to Bilal.

Wudu for Adhan and Iqama: Rulings on Purification and the Call to Prayer
Ruling on wudu requirement for adhan and iqama, and janabah prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving adhan and iqama without wudu and explain why janabah makes it impermissible.

Core Idea
Adhan without wudu is valid but disliked; only janabah makes it unlawful.

This lesson examines the purity requirements for the call to prayer. The matn of Al-Quduri provides three distinct rulings regarding wudu and janabah for the mu'adhdhin. We will explore the evidence and the legal reasoning behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The matn states: (1) It is befitting to give adhan and iqama in wudu. (2) If adhan is given without wudu, it is permissible (ja'iz). (3) It is disliked (makruh) to give iqama without wudu. (4) One should not give adhan in the state of janabah.
2
Understand key terms
The Arabic 'yambaghi' indicates recommendation, not obligation. 'Ja'iz' means valid. 'Makruh' means disliked but not sinful. 'La yu'adhdhin' is a negative command indicating prohibition.
Hanafis differentiate between adhan and iqama in degree of dislike.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith 'No one should give adhan except one who is in wudu' is used to support the recommendation. Though the wording is a negative command, the Hanafi school interprets it as a strong recommendation due to the practice of the Companions who sometimes gave adhan without wudu.
The hadith is ahad, so it does not reach the level of wajib.
4
Apply Hanafi usul
The command 'La yu'adhdhin' is interpreted as tahrim (prohibition) but is overridden by the permissibility reported from the early Muslims, resulting in a ruling of makruh tanzihan for adhan without wudu. For janabah, the prohibition remains because reciting dhikr in janabah is haram.
Janabah is a major impurity; adhan involves reciting phrases of Allah's greatness, which is akin to Quran recitation.
5
Distinguish between adhan and iqama
Both are disliked without wudu, but iqama is more strongly disliked because it is directly connected to the prayer. Janabah is prohibited for both adhan and iqama.
The matn specifically mentions adhan for janabah; by analogy, iqama in janabah is also prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ف وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُؤَذِّنَ وَيُقِيمَ عَلَى وُضُوءٍ فَإِنْ أَذَّنَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءِ جَازَ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يُقِيمَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ وَلَا يُؤَذِّنُ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ
و وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُؤَذِّنَ وَيُقِيمَ عَلَى وُضُوءٍ فَإِنْ أَذَّنَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ جَازَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يُؤَذِّنُ إِلَّا مُتَوَضّى، (، (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ الأَذَانِ بِغَيْرِ وُضُوءِ نمبر 200)
اصول : اذان واقامت بغیر وضو کے جائز ہے، لیکن ایسا کرنا مکروہ اور برا ہے۔
F: And it is befitting that he gives the adhan and iqama in a state of wudu. If he gives the adhan without wudu, it is permissible, and it is disliked that he gives the iqama without wudu. And he should not give the adhan while in a state of janabah. And proof (1): Hadith for establishing 'and it is befitting that he gives the adhan and iqama in wudu, and if he gives adhan without wudu, it is permissible': from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (saw) who said: 'No one should give the adhan except one who is in wudu.' Urdu principle: Adhan and iqama without wudu are permissible, but doing so is disliked and bad.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the purity requirement for the call to prayer. The matn gives three rulings: (1) It is recommended (yambaghi) to have wudu for both adhan and iqama. (2) If one gives adhan without wudu, it is valid (ja'iz) but disliked (makruh). (3) Giving iqama without wudu is disliked (makruh). (4) Giving adhan in a state of major impurity (janabah) is impermissible (la yu'adhdhin). The hadith from Abu Huraira supports the recommendation but does not make it obligatory, as the phrase 'la yu'adhdhin' is interpreted as a strong discouragement rather than prohibition except for janabah. The Urdu usul confirms that it is permissible but makruh. Hanafis differentiate between adhan and iqama: adhan without wudu is makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked), while iqama without wudu is also makruh tanzihan, but stronger dislike due to closeness to the prayer. Janabah invalidates the adhan because it involves dhikr of Allah, which is prohibited for the junub.

Key Terms
جُنُب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (e.g., after sexual intercourse or seminal discharge).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for giving the adhan without wudu?
A) It is invalid (batil)
B) It is permissible but disliked (makruh)
C) It is recommended (mustahab)
D) It is forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
Adhan requires wudu for optimal practice but is valid without it; janabah is strictly prohibited.

Facing Qibla and Turning in Adhan
Ruling with proof on adhan postures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing qibla and turning during adhan, and identify the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Facing qibla and turning at hayya'alah are sunnah, proven by Bilal's practice.

The adhan is a call to prayer with established etiquettes. This passage addresses two specific postures: facing the qibla throughout the adhan and turning the head right and left at the phrases 'hayya 'ala as-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. Understanding these rulings ensures the adhan is performed in accordance with the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on two actions during adhan: facing qibla and turning at specific phrases. Determine the hukm level (fard, wajib, sunnah).
Hanafis consider these sunnah mu'akkadah, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one from Abdullah ibn Zaid about facing qibla, one from Abu Juhaifa about Bilal turning his neck.
Both are ahad hadith with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid explicitly states 'fastaqbala al-qiblah', showing the mu'adhdhin should face qibla. The hadith of Abu Juhaifa describes Bilal turning his neck (lawa 'unuqahu) without turning his body, establishing the turning action.
The turning is restricted to the neck/face, not the whole body.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Maliki) do not require turning; the Hanafi position is based on the practice of Bilal as witnessed by the Prophet.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit action of Bilal, which is taken as a sunnah practice. The mufta bihi is that both actions are mustahabb.
The adhan is valid if omitted, but the sunnah is lost.

Source Text

بَابُ الْأَذَانِ
وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ بِمَا الْقِبْلَةَ كى فَإِذَا بَلَغَ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ وَالْفَلَاحِ حَوَّلَ وَجْهَهُ يَمِينًا وَشِمَالًا .
د وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ بِهِمَا الْقِبْلَةَ أَفَجَاءَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ زَيْدٍ، رَجُلٌ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ، وَقَالَ فِيهِ: فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، قَالَ: اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُسنن ابوداود، بَابُ كَيْفَ الْأَذَانُ ، نمبر 507/سنن بيهقي، بَابُ اسْتِقْبَالِ الْقِبْلَةِ بِالْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ، غبر 1838)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا بَلَغَ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ وَالْفَلَاح حَوَّلَ وَجْهَهُ يَمِينًا وَشِمَالًا \ عَنْ عَوْنِ بْنِ أَبي جُحَيْفَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّي بِمَكَّةَ وَهُوَ فِي قُبَّةٍ خَمْرَاءَ مِنْ أَدَم فَخَرَجَ بِلَالٌ فَأَذَّنَ فَكُنْتُ أَتَتَبَّعُ فَمَهُ هَاهُنَا وَهَاهُنَا، قَالَ: «ثُمَّ خَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَعَلَيْهِ حُلَّةٌ حَمْرَاءُ بُرُودٌ يَمَانِيَةٌ قِطْرِيٌّ» وَقَالَ مُوسَى - قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ بِلالا خَرَجَ إِلَى الْأَبْطَح فَأَذَّنَ فَلَمَّا بَلَغَ حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ، حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ، لَوَى عُنُقَهُ يَمِينًا وَشِمَالًا، وَلَمْ يَسْتَدِرُ ، ) ، سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْمُؤَذِنِ يَسْتَدِيرُ فِي أَذَانِهِ، نمبر 507/سنن بيهقي، بَابُ الِالْتِوَاءِ فِي حِيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حِيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ، نمبر 1851)
Chapter of Adhan. He faces the qibla with his face, and when he reaches 'as-salah' and 'al-falah', he turns his face right and left. Proof: Hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid about facing qibla. Proof: Hadith of Abu Juhaifa about Bilal turning his neck right and left without turning around.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage states two rulings regarding the posture of the mu'adhdhin during adhan. First, he must face the qibla throughout the adhan. The hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid, who saw the adhan in a dream, confirms that the mu'adhdhin faces the qibla. Second, when he reaches the phrases 'hayya 'ala as-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah', he should turn his face to the right and left respectively, without turning his entire body. The hadith of Abu Juhaifa describes Bilal doing exactly this. Note that the matn says 'بِمَا' which is likely a scribal error; the correct phrase is 'بِوَجْهِهِ' (with his face) as confirmed by the hadith. The Hanafi school holds that turning the head is sufficient; turning the chest is not required. The turning is not done by rotating the whole body (istidarah) as some do.

Key Terms
يستقبل القبلة (yastaqbil al-qiblah): The mu'adhdhin should face the direction of the Kaaba with his face and chest during the entire adhan.
حول وجهه يمينا وشمالا (hawwala wajhahu yaminan wa shimalan): At the phrases 'hayya 'ala as-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah', the mu'adhdhin turns his face to the right and left respectively, without turning his whole body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as stated in this passage, what should the mu'adhdhin do when he reaches 'hayya 'ala as-salah'?
A) Turn his entire body to the right
B) Turn his face to the right without turning his whole body
C) Raise his voice
D) Remain facing the qibla without turning

Key Takeaway
Facing qibla and turning the neck at hayya'alah are sunnah practices in adhan, validly omitted but meritorious.

Ruling on Wudu for Adhan and Iqamah
States the ruling that adhan and iqamah are recommended with wudu, permissible without, but makruh for iqamah without wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah without wudu and explain the dalil and its interpretation.

Core Idea
Adhan without wudu is valid but iqamah without wudu is disliked; wudu is recommended, not required.

This lesson clarifies a common point of confusion: the legal status of performing the call to prayer (adhan) and the iqamah without ritual ablution (wudu). The Hanafi school distinguishes between the two acts and also between the absence of wudu and the state of major impurity (janabah). We will examine the primary evidence and how the Hanafi jurists derived these nuanced rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The passage gives three distinct rulings: adhan without wudu is permissible (ja'iz) but better with wudu; iqamah without wudu is disliked (makruh); adhan while junub is not allowed. Note the difference between adhan and iqamah.
This distinction is important; some mistakenly think both are the same.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The hadith of Abu Hurairah (ra) states: 'None should give adhan except one who has wudu.' This is a sound hadith (Sunan al-Tirmidhi). The Hanafi school uses this as the main proof.
The hadith text: 'لَا يُؤَذِّنُ إِلَّا مُتَوَضّى'
3
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation
Hanafis interpret the prohibition as a recommendation (nadb) rather than a condition of validity, because adhan is an act of worship that can be performed without wudu (unlike prayer). The phrase 'illa mutawaddi' indicates preference, not a legal requirement.
This is a key difference from other schools that consider wudu a condition.
4
Understand the additional ruling for janabah
The passage explicitly forbids adhan from a junub person. Hanafis consider this a stronger prohibition (haram) because janabah is a major impurity that invalidates acts of worship that require purity (but not adhan itself—rather, it is a condition of permissibility).
The distinction: lack of wudu does not impede validity, but janabah does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُؤَذِّنَ وَيُقِيمَ عَلَى وُضُوءٍ فَإِنْ أَذَّنَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءِ جَازَ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يُقِيمَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ وَلَا يُؤَذِّنُ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ
و وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُؤَذِّنَ وَيُقِيمَ عَلَى وُضُوءٍ فَإِنْ أَذَّنَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ جَازَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يُؤَذِّنُ إِلَّا مُتَوَضّى، (، (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ الأَذَانِ بِغَيْرِ وُضُوءِ نمبر 200)
اصول : اذان واقامت بغیر وضو کے جائز ہے، لیکن ایسا کرنا مکروہ اور برا ہے۔
It is befitting that he gives adhan and iqamah with wudu. If he gives adhan without wudu, it is permissible, and it is disliked (makruh) to give iqamah without wudu. And he should not give adhan while in a state of major impurity (junub). Proof: Hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'None should give adhan except one who has wudu.' Principle: Adhan and iqamah without wudu are permissible, but doing so is makruh and bad.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between the legal status of adhan and iqamah performed without wudu. It states that it is preferable (yanbaghi) to have wudu for both. However, if one gives adhan without wudu, it is valid (ja'iz). For iqamah without wudu, it is makruh (disliked). The hadith of Abu Hurairah, 'None should give adhan except one who has wudu,' is interpreted as a recommendation (nadb) rather than a prohibition, because the validity of the adhan is not dependent on wudu. The additional ruling: adhan from a person in major impurity (junub) is invalid (la yu'adhdhin), meaning it is not permissible. The Urdu note summarizes: adhan and iqamah without wudu are permissible but disliked. Note: The hadith quoted uses 'لا يؤذن إلا متوضئ' which the Hanafis take as a recommendation, not a condition of validity.

Key Terms
وضوء (wudu): Ritual ablution performed with water on the hands, mouth, nose, face, arms, head, and feet.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (full bath).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the legal status of giving iqamah without wudu?
A) Valid and recommended
B) Permissible but disliked (makruh)
C) Invalid and must be repeated
D) Forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
Adhan without wudu is valid (ja'iz) but iqamah without wudu is makruh; adhan while junub is haram.
