Adhan for Missed Prayers: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on adhan for missed prayers with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan for a single missed prayer and for multiple missed prayers, and apply the dalil from the hadith of the Battle of the Trench.

Core Idea
Adhan for missed prayers is sunnah; for multiple, adhan only for the first is sufficient.

When we miss a prayer, we must make it up (qada). But what about the adhan? Is it required? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) during the Battle of the Trench. Al-Quduri's matn provides the ruling, supported by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on adhan for missed prayers. First, note that the act is adhan (call to prayer) and iqamah for a missed (faa'itah) prayer. The hukm level is sunnah muakkadah—strongly recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud about the Battle of the Trench. Locate the specific proof: the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered Bilal to give adhan only for the first missed prayer (zuhr) and then iqamah for each subsequent prayer.
Hadith recorded by Tirmidhi and Nasa'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key point is that the Prophet commanded adhan for the first prayer only, and then only iqamah for the rest. This indicates that adhan for each subsequent prayer is not obligatory but optional. The Hanafi school derives the option from this silence.
The absence of a command for adhan for the later prayers shows permissibility of omission.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that adhan is required for each missed prayer, based on the general command to give adhan for every prayer. The Hanafi school responds that the specific practice of the Prophet limits the general rule.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both sides have evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (adhan for first, option for rest) is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view. It is based on the explicit action of the Prophet, which takes precedence over general commands.
Al-Quduri's matn is authoritative in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُؤَذِّنُ لِلْفَائِتَةِ وَيُقِيمُ فَإِنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَوَاتٌ أَذَّنَ لِلْأُولَى وَأَقَامَ وَكَانَ مُخَيَّرًا فِي الثَّانِيَةِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَذَّنَ وَأَقَامَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ اقْتَصَرَ عَلَى الْإِقَامَةِ .
د وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَيُؤَذِّنُ لِلْفَائِتَةِ وَيُقِيمُ فَإِنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَوَاتٌ أَذَّنَ لِلْأُولَى \ عَنْ أَبِي عُبَيْدَةَ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: «إِنَّ الْمُشْرِكِينَ شَغَلُوا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ أَرْبَعِ صَلَوَاتٍ يَوْمَ الْخَنْدَقِ، حَتَّى ذَهَبَ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ مَا شَاءَ اللَّهُ، فَأَمَرَ بِلَالًا فَأَذَّنَ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى العَصْرَ ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى المَغْرِبَ ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى العِشَاءَ ، (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الرَّجُلِ تَفُوتُهُ الصَّلَوَاتُ بِأَيَّتِهِنَّ يَبْدَأُ ، نمبر 179 /سنن نسائي، (55) كَيْفَ يُقْضَى الْفَائِتُ مِنَ الصَّلاةِ، غير (623)

اصول : فائتہ نمازوں کے لئے بھی اذان واقامت کہنا مسنون ہے۔
اصول : اگر فائتہ زائد ہوں تو اختیار ہے کہ ہر ایک لئے اذان واقامت کہے یا شروع میں اذان واقامت کہے اور باقی میں صرف اقامت کہے۔
He performs adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah. If he missed several prayers, he gives adhan for the first and iqamah, and he has a choice for the second: if he wishes, he gives adhan and iqamah, and if he wishes, he suffices with iqamah. Proof: Hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud about the Battle of the Trench. Principle: It is sunnah to give adhan and iqamah for missed prayers. Principle: If there are multiple missed prayers, he has the choice to give adhan and iqamah for each or to give adhan for the first and then only iqamah for the rest.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage rules on adhan for missed (faa'itah) prayers. For a single missed prayer, it is sunnah to call both adhan and iqamah. This is based on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who reported that on the day of Khandaq, the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered Bilal to give adhan for the first missed prayer (zuhr) and then iqamah for each subsequent prayer. When multiple prayers are missed, the mu'adhdhin must give adhan for the first missed prayer only; after that, he has a choice: either give adhan and iqamah for each subsequent prayer, or suffice with iqamah only for the rest. The Hanafi school holds that adhan is not obligatory (fard) but sunnah mu'akkadah; this ruling extends to qada' prayers. The Urdu uṣul notes clarify that it is sunnah to call adhan and iqamah for missed prayers, and if multiple, the option exists.

Key Terms
الفائتة (al-faa'itah): A prayer that was missed from its prescribed time and is now being performed as qada'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a person missed four prayers and is making them up, what is required regarding adhan?
A) Adhan for each of the four prayers
B) Adhan for the first prayer only, then iqamah for the rest, with option to add adhan for the second
C) No adhan at all for missed prayers
D) Iqamah for all without adhan

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that adhan for missed prayers is sunnah, and for multiple prayers, adhan is only required for the first, with an option for the rest.

Adhan Not Permitted Before the Time
States the ruling that adhan is not valid before the prescribed prayer time enters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on giving adhan before the prescribed prayer time and identify the evidence from hadith that supports the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Adhan is only valid after the prayer time enters; an early adhan must be repeated.

This lesson establishes a fundamental principle: the adhan is tied to the prayer time. The matn from Al-Quduri clearly states that adhan must not be given before the time. We will examine the hadith proofs that the Hanafi school uses to support this ruling, including the clarification that the pre-dawn call of Bilal was not the actual fajr adhan.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling from the matn
Read the matn 'وَلَا يُؤَذِّنُ لِصَلَاةٍ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ وَقْتِهَا' and note that it is a clear prohibition of adhan before time.
The matn is from Al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text.
2
Examine the first hadith proof
The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud explains that Bilal's adhan before dawn is not for Fajr; it is to wake people and stop them from eating. This shows that an adhan before time is not the actual adhan for the prayer.
This hadith is in Sahih al-Bukhari and other collections.
3
Understand the distinction between pre-dawn call and actual adhan
The hadith from Aisha and Ibn Umar further clarify that the early call is not the adhan for Fajr; the real adhan is given by Ibn Umm Maktum later. The Prophet ordered Bilal to announce that he slept, meaning the adhan was not effective.
This distinction is crucial to avoid confusion.
4
Apply the principle
The Urdu principle summarizes: for any prayer, adhan before time is not valid, and if given, it must be repeated. Apply this to all five daily prayers.
The only exception is the pre-dawn adhan for Ramadan, which is a separate sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُؤَذِّنُ لِصَلَاةٍ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ وَقْتِهَا
10 وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُؤَذِّنُ لِصَلَاةٍ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ وَقْتِهَا \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، عَنِ التي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يَنْعَنَّ أَحَدَكُمْ، أَوْ أَحَدًا مِنْكُمْ، أَذَانُ بِلَالٍ مِنْ سَحُورِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ يُؤَذِّنُ، أَوْ يُنَادِي بِلَيْلِ لِيَرْجِعَ قَائِمَكُمْ، وَلِيُنَبِّهَ نَائِمَكُمْ، وَلَيْسَ أَنْ يَقُولَ الْفَجْرُ، أَوِ الصُّبْحُ. وَقَالَ بِأَصَابِعِهِ، وَرَفَعَهَا إلَى فَوْقُ، وَطَأْطَأَ إِلَى أَسْفَلْ: حَتَّى يَقُولَ هَكَذَا وَقَالَ زُهَيْرٌ بِسَبَّابَتَيْهِ، إِحْدَاهُمَا فَوْقَ الْأُخْرَى ثُمَّ مَدَّهَا عَنْ يَمِينِهِ وَشِمَالِهِ، (بخاري شريف، ب بَابُ الْأَذَانِ قَبْلَ الْفَجْرِ،نمبر 621/سنن نسائي، في غَيْر وَقْتِ الصَّلَاةِ، غمبر (642)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُؤَذِّنُ لِصَلَاةٍ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ وَقْتِهَا \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «إِنَّ بِلَالًا يُؤَذِّنُ بِلَيْلِ، فَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يُؤَذِنَ ابْنُ أُمَ مَكْتُومِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الْأَذَانِ قَبْلَ الْفَجْرِ، نمبر 623 سنن ترمذى بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الأَذَانِ بِاللَّيْل، غبر (203)
لْأَذَانُ
وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُؤَذِّنُ لِصَلَاةٍ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ وَقْتِهَا \ عَنْ ابْنِ عُمَرَ: أَنَّ بِلَالًا أَذَّنَ بِلَيْلِ، فَأَمَرَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنْ يُنَادِي: «إِنَّ العَبْدَ نَامَ،، سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْأَذَانِ بِاللَّيْلِ، نمبر 203/، (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْأَذَانِ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ الْوَقْتِ، نمبر 532)
وجه (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُؤَذِّنُ لِصَلَاةٍ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ وَقْتِهَا \ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ لَهُ: «لَا تُؤَذِنْ حَتَّى يَسْتَبِينَ لَكَ الْفَجْرُ هَكَذَا» وَمَدَّ يَدَيْهِ عَرْضًا، سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْأَذَانِ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ الْوَقْتِ نمبر 534)
اصول : طرفین : کسی بھی نماز کے لیے وقت سے قبل اذان درست نہیں ہے اور اگر اذان دے دی گئی تو وہ قابل اعادہ ہے۔
He does not give adhan for a prayer before the entry of its time. Proof: Hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud about Bilal's adhan before dawn. Proof: Hadith of Aisha that Bilal gives adhan at night, so eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum gives adhan. Proof: Hadith of Ibn Umar that Bilal gave adhan at night and the Prophet ordered him to announce 'The slave (i.e., Bilal) slept.' Proof: The Prophet said to him: 'Do not give adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you like this' and spread his hands wide. Principle: For both (adhan and iqamah?), adhan before the time is not valid for any prayer, and if it was given, it must be repeated.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage establishes the fundamental principle that adhan is tied to the prayer time. The matn states clearly: 'He does not give adhan for a prayer before the entry of its time.' Four hadith are provided as proofs. The first (from Ibn Mas'ud) explains that Bilal's adhan before dawn is not for fajr but to wake people; the real adhan for fajr is later. The second (from Aisha) similarly distinguishes between Bilal's night adhan and the actual fajr adhan by Ibn Umm Maktum. The third (from Ibn Umar) reports that when Bilal gave adhan at night, the Prophet ordered him to announce 'the slave (meaning Bilal) slept' (i.e., the adhan was not effective). The fourth (from Abu Dawud) has the Prophet directly instructing to wait until dawn is clear. The Urdu principle at the end summarizes: for any prayer, adhan before time is not valid, and if given, it must be repeated (qaabil-e-i'aadah). This ruling applies to all five daily prayers; adhan must be after the time has entered. The exception is the pre-dawn adhan for Ramadan/fasting, which is not considered the adhan for fajr prayer but a separate call.

Key Terms
دخول الوقت (dukhul al-waqt): The moment when the prescribed time for a prayer begins according to Islamic law (e.g., true dawn for Fajr, sun's zawaal for Zuhr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mu'adhdhin gives the adhan for Fajr before true dawn, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The adhan is valid and does not need to be repeated
B) The adhan is invalid and must be repeated after dawn
C) The adhan is valid but disliked
D) The adhan is valid only if it is the month of Ramadan

Key Takeaway
Adhan is only valid after the prescribed prayer time has entered; an adhan given before time is invalid and must be repeated.

Ruling for the Naked Person's Prayer
Ruling with proof from Salaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a naked person's prayer and explain why sitting is better when others can see.

Core Idea
When praying naked, sitting is better than standing to preserve modesty when seen.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a specific case — a person who must pray without clothing. The matn gives a clear ruling, and the commentator supplements it with two proofs from the Companions and Successors. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between validity and virtue. The prayer is valid either way, but the preferred posture depends on being seen.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling
The matn states: 'If he prays standing, it suffices him, but the first (sitting) is better.' Identify that both postures are valid, but sitting is more virtuous (afdal).
The level of hukm for sitting is sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Examine Proof 1
The saying of 'Ali narrated by Maymun ibn Mihran: differentiate between being seen (pray sitting) and not seen (pray standing). This shows the ruling hinges on modesty.
The chain is from a Tabi'i, so the thubut is zanni.
3
Examine Proof 2
The saying of Ibn 'Abbas: analogizes the naked person to the one praying on a ship — both pray sitting. This reinforces the preference for sitting.
Ibn 'Abbas is a Companion, so his saying is a qawl sahabi.
4
Synthesize the proofs
Both proofs indicate that when others are present, sitting is recommended to avoid exposure. When alone, standing is permissible.
The common thread is modesty (sitr al-'awrah).
5
Apply the ruling
In public: pray sitting. In private: standing is permissible, though sitting is still better as per the general statement 'the first is better'.
This rule applies only when one is compelled to pray without clothing (e.g., loss of garments).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ شُرُوطِ الصَّلَاةِ فَإِنْ صَلَّى قَائِمًا أَجْزَأَهُ وَالأَوَّلُ أَفْضَلُ. وَجْهٌ (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ مَيْمُونِ بْنِ مِهْرَانَ قَالَ: سُئِلَ عَلِيٌّ عَنْ صَلَاةِ الْعُرْيَانِ، فَقَالَ: «إِنْ كَانَ حَيْثُ يَرَاهُ النَّاسُ صَلَّى جَالِسًا، وَإِنْ كَانَ حَيْثُ لَا يَرَاهُ النَّاسُ صَلَّى قَائِمًا». (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْعُرْيَانِ، رقم 4566) وَجْهٌ (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «الَّذِي يُصَلِّي فِي السَّفِينَةِ، وَالَّذِي يُصَلِّي عُرْيَانًا، يُصَلِّي جَالِسًا». (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْعُرْيَانِ، رقم 4565)
Chapter on Conditions of Prayer. If he prays standing, it suffices him, but the first (sitting) is better. Proof 1: The saying of a Tabi'i for its establishment: from Maymun ibn Mihran, he said: 'Ali was asked about the prayer of the naked person, so he said: "If he is where people can see him, he prays sitting; if he is where people do not see him, he prays standing."' Proof 2: The saying of a Companion for its establishment: from Ibn 'Abbas, he said: 'The one who prays in a ship, and the one who prays naked, prays sitting.'
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the prayer of a naked person. The matn states that if he prays standing, his prayer is valid, but it is better (afdal) to pray sitting. The commentator then provides two proofs: first, a narration from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, who distinguished between being seen and not seen; second, a narration from Ibn 'Abbas who analogized the naked person to the one on a ship—both pray sitting. The Hanafi ruling: for a naked person in the presence of others, it is recommended (sunnah) to pray sitting to avoid exposure; if alone, standing is permissible. The prayer is valid in either case, but the more virtuous is sitting when others may see him.

Key Terms
العريان (al-'uryan): The naked person who must pray without clothing due to lack of covering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a naked person who can be seen by others, what is the better posture for prayer?
A) Standing
B) Sitting
C) Lying down
D) Any posture

Key Takeaway
For a naked person praying in public, sitting is superior to standing to preserve modesty, though both are valid.

Niyyah in Prayer: Obligation and Connection to Takbir
Establishes the obligation of intention and the prohibition of separating it from the opening takbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on niyyah in prayer and explain why it must be connected to the opening takbir without any separation.

Core Idea
The intention for prayer must be made at the very first moment, inseparable from the takbir.

The beginning of prayer is a precise moment: the heart must be set on the specific prayer just as the tongue utters Allahu Akbar. The classical Hanafi text makes this clear: any gap, even a small action, breaks the connection and the prayer does not begin. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the four proofs that support it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Niyyah
Read the opening phrase: 'And he intends the prayer he enters into with an intention.' This establishes that niyyah is an obligatory (fard) part of starting prayer. Note the prohibition: 'he does not separate between it and the takbirat al-ihram by an action or anything else.'
The ruling is fard 'ayn – every individual must perform it correctly.
2
Understand the Connection Requirement
The text explicitly forbids any fasl (separation) between the niyyah and the takbir. This includes physical actions, speech, or even a long pause. Without this immediate connection, the intention is not valid and the prayer has not begun.
This requirement is specific to the start of prayer; ongoing intention is maintained internally.
3
Analyze the First Proof: The Niyyah Hadith
The hadith 'Innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyat' is cited. In Hanafi usul, this general statement indicates wujub (obligation) because it links all acts to their intentions. Since prayer is an act, it requires a valid intention at its inception.
This hadith is the primary evidence; its general ('amm) wording is taken as applying to all acts of worship.
4
Analyze the Remaining Three Proofs
The second proof from Ibn Mas'ud urges guarding intentions in prayer, reinforcing that intention must be present. The third proof (about following the imam) implies the follower's intention must synchronize with the imam's takbir. The fourth proof (imam as guarantor) highlights the importance of exact timing in congregational prayer.
These proofs serve as additional corroboration (shawahid) for the obligation.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
If someone makes the intention long before the takbir, or performs an action (e.g., adjusting clothes) between the intention and the takbir, the intention is invalid. The prayer must be recommenced with a fresh intention connected directly to the takbir.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَنْوِي الصَّلَاةَ الَّتِي يَدْخُلُ فِيهِ بِنِيَّةٍ لَا يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ التَّحْرِيمَةِ بِعَمَلٍ وَلَا غَيْرِهِ. وَجْهٌ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ سَمِعْتُ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ عَلَى الْمِنْبَرِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «إِنَّمَا الْأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ». (بخاري، كَيْفَ كَانَ بَدْءُ الْوَحْيِ، رقم 1) وَجْهٌ (٢) عِبَارَةُ الْمُعْجَمِ الْكَبِيرِ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ قَالَ: «تَعَوَّدُوا الْخَيْرَ فَإِنَّ الْخَيْرَ بِالْعَادَةِ، وَحَافِظُوا عَلَى نِيَّاتِكُمْ فِي الصَّلَاةِ». (المعجم الكبير للطبراني، رقم 8755) وَجْهٌ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِنَّمَا الْإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ فَلَا تَخْتَلِفُوا عَلَيْهِ فَإِذَا كَبَّرَ فَكَبِّرُوا». (مسلم، باب انْتِمَامِ الْمَأْمُومِ بِالْإِمَامِ، 414 / بخاري، بَابٌ: إِنَّمَا جُعِلَ الْإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ، غير 688) وَجْهٌ (٤) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «الْإِمَامُ ضَامِنٌ، وَالْمُؤَذِّنُ مُؤْتَمَنٌ، اللَّهُمَّ أَرْشِدِ الْأَئِمَّةَ، وَاغْفِرْ لِلْمُؤَذِّنِينَ». (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الْإِمَامَ ضَامِنٌ، رقم 207)
And he intends the prayer he enters into with an intention that he does not separate between it and the takbirat al-ihram by an action or anything else. Proof 1: The hadith for its establishment: I heard 'Umar ibn al-Khattab on the pulpit say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Deeds are [judged] by intentions.' Proof 2: The wording of al-Mu'jam al-Kabir for its establishment: from 'Abdullah, he said: 'Accustom yourselves to good, for good is by habit, and guard your intentions in prayer.' Proof 3: The hadith for its establishment: from Abu Hurayra that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ with him; when he says takbir, say takbir.' Proof 4: The hadith for its establishment: from Abu Hurayra, he said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is entrusted; O Allah, guide the imams and forgive the mu'adhdhins.'
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the obligation of niyyah (intention) in prayer. The matn states that one must intend the specific prayer he is entering, and this intention must be directly connected to the takbirat al-ihram (opening takbir) without any intervening action, speech, or other separating element. The commentator then provides four proofs: the famous hadith 'Innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyat' which is the primary evidence for the obligation of intention in all acts of worship; a narration from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud urging preservation of intention during prayer; the hadith about following the imam, which implies that the follower's intention is tied to the imam's actions; and the hadith that the imam is a guarantor, emphasizing the importance of synchronization. In the Hanafi school, niyyah is a fard (obligatory) condition for the validity of prayer, and it must be performed at the very beginning, connected to the takbir without any break (fasl). If there is a significant separation, the intention is not valid and the prayer does not begin.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform a specific prayer, required at the beginning of prayer.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that starts the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on separating the intention (niyyah) from the takbirat al-ihram by an action?
A) It is makruh but valid
B) It invalidates the intention
C) It is recommended
D) It has no effect

Key Takeaway
The intention for prayer must be made at the same moment as the opening takbir; any separation, no matter how small, invalidates the intention and thus the prayer does not begin.

Obligation of Facing the Qibla and Ijtihad When Direction is Unknown
Sets the obligation of facing the qibla, exception for fear, and rules for ijtihad when direction is unclear.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla, identify the exception for fear, and apply the rules for ijtihad and post-prayer error.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla is a fard condition; ijtihad suffices when uncertain, and no repeat is needed if mistaken.

This passage from al-Quduri establishes the fundamental obligation of facing the qibla for every prayer, while providing a clear exception for those in genuine fear. It then addresses the practical situation when the direction is unknown, outlining the duty of ijtihad and the consequences of discovering an error. The proofs from the Quran and Sunnah reinforce these rulings, demonstrating the school's reliance on definitive texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and exception
Read the opening line of the matn: 'And he faces the qibla, unless he is fearful.' Recognize that facing the qibla is the default obligation, and fear (e.g., battle, imminent danger) permits prayer in any direction one is able.
Fear is defined as a situation where one cannot safely turn towards the qibla.
2
Understand ijtihad when qibla is ambiguous
When the qibla direction is unclear and no knowledgeable person is available, one must exert effort (ijtihad) using signs (e.g., stars, landmarks) to determine the direction, then pray according to that estimation.
Ijtihad is obligatory (fard) in this situation; praying without effort is invalid.
3
Analyze the post-prayer error scenario
If after completing the prayer one realizes they prayed in the wrong direction, the prayer is valid and no repetition is required. This is based on the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet validated the prayers of companions who erred in a cloudy night.
The principle is that one who exercises ijtihad is excused if mistaken.
4
Analyze the mid-prayer error scenario
If the error is discovered during the prayer, one must turn towards the correct direction and continue from where they are, building upon the prayer already performed. This is supported by the hadith of the qibla change at Quba'.
Turning does not invalidate the prayer; one continues with the same intention.
5
Examine the proofs
The passage cites two Quranic verses and two hadiths. The first verse (2:144) establishes the obligation; the second (2:115) shows Allah's mercy in exceptional circumstances. The hadith of Jabir validates ijtihad and error forgiveness; the hadith of Ibn Umar confirms turning during prayer.
These proofs are dari (definitive) in transmission and meaning for the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْقِبْلَةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ خَائِفًا فَيُصَلِّيَ إِلَى أَيِّ وِجْهَةٍ قَدَرَ. فَإِنْ اشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْقِبْلَةُ وَلَيْسَ بِحَضْرَتِهِ مَنْ يَسْأَلُهُ عَنْهَا اجْتَهَدَ وَصَلَّى فَإِنْ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ أَخْطَأَ بَعْدَ مَا صَلَّى فَلَا إِعَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ. وَإِنْ عَلِمَ ذَلِكَ وَهُوَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ اسْتَدَارَ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ وَبَنَى عَلَيْهِ. وَجْهٌ (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ {فَوَلِّ وَجْهَكَ شَطْرَ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ وَحَيْثُ مَا كُنْتُمْ فَوَلُّوا وُجُوهَكُمْ شَطْرَهُ} (سورة البقرة، آية 144) وَجْهٌ (٢) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ {وَلِلَّهِ الْمَشْرِقُ وَالْمَغْرِبُ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ اللهِ} (سورة البقرة، آية 115) وَجْهٌ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: كُنَّا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي مَسِيرٍ أَوْ سَرِيَّةٍ فَأَصَابَنَا غَيْمٌ فَتَحَرَّيْنَا، وَاخْتَلَفْنَا فِي الْقِبْلَةِ فَصَلَّى كُلُّ رَجُلٍ مِنَّا عَلَى حِدَةٍ، فَجَعَلَ أَحَدُنَا يَخُطُّ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ لِنَعْلَمَ أَمْكِنَتَنَا، فَلَمَّا أَصْبَحْنَا نَظَرْنَاهُ، فَإِذَا نَحْنُ قَدْ صَلَّيْنَا عَلَى غَيْرِ الْقِبْلَةِ، فَذَكَرْنَا ذَلِكَ لِلنَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ: «قَدْ أَجْزَأَتْ صَلَاتُكُمْ». (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ الِاخْتِلَافِ فِي الْقِبْلَةِ عِنْدَ التَّحَرِّي، رقم 2235 / سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الرَّجُلِ يُصَلِّي لِغَيْرِ الْقِبْلَةِ فِي الْغَيْمِ، رقم 345) وَجْهٌ (٢) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ قَالَ: وَلَوِ افْتَتَحَ الصَّلَاةَ عَلَى اجْتِهَادِهِ ثُمَّ رَأَى الْقِبْلَةَ فِي غَيْرِهِ، (كِتَابُ الْأُمِّ لِلشَّافِعِيِّ) وَجْهٌ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: بَيْنَا النَّاسُ بِقُبَاءَ فِي صَلَاةِ الصُّبْحِ، إِذْ جَاءَهُمْ آتٍ فَقَالَ: إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَدْ أُنْزِلَ عَلَيْهِ اللَّيْلَةَ قُرْآنٌ، وَقَدْ أُمِرَ أَنْ يَسْتَقْبِلَ الْكَعْبَةَ، فَاسْتَقْبِلُوهَا، وَكَانَتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ إِلَى الشَّامِ، فَاسْتَدَارُوا إِلَى الْكَعْبَةِ. (بخاري، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْقِبْلَةِ، رقم 403 / مسلم، بَاب تَحْوِيلِ الْقِبْلَةِ، رقم 526)
And he faces the qibla, unless he is fearful, then he prays towards whatever direction he can. If the qibla is ambiguous to him and there is no one present to ask about it, he exerts his effort (ijtihad) and prays. Then if he knows that he erred after having prayed, there is no repetition upon him. And if he knows that while in prayer, he turns towards the qibla and builds upon it. Proof 1: The verse for its establishment: 'Turn your face toward al-Masjid al-Haram, and wherever you are, turn your faces toward it.' Proof 2: The verse for its establishment: 'To Allah belongs the east and the west, so wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah.' Proof 1: The hadith for its establishment: from Jabir, he said: We were with the Messenger of Allah on a journey or expedition, and a cloud came over us, so we tried to determine (the direction) and differed about the qibla. Each man prayed individually, and one of us drew lines in front of us to know our positions. When morning came we looked and saw we had prayed other than the qibla. So we mentioned that to the Prophet, and he said: 'Your prayer has sufficed (is valid).' Proof 2: The saying of a Tabi'i for its establishment: He said: If he begins the prayer based on his ijtihad, then sees the qibla in another direction, [he turns] from the book al-Umm by al-Shafi'i. Proof 3: The hadith for its establishment: from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, he said: While the people were at Quba' in the morning prayer, a visitor came and said: The Messenger of Allah has received a revelation tonight, and he has been commanded to face the Ka'ba, so face it. Their faces were towards Syria, so they turned around towards the Ka'ba.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the obligation of facing the qibla in prayer. The matn states that facing the qibla is required except when one is in a state of fear (e.g., battle, extreme danger), in which case one may pray in any direction they are able. If the qibla direction is unknown and there is no knowledgeable person to ask, one must perform ijtihad (individual reasoning based on signs) and pray according to his best estimation. If after prayer he discovers he was wrong, his prayer is still valid and no repetition is required. If he realizes the error during the prayer, he should turn towards the correct direction and continue his prayer from that point (build upon it by making the necessary turning). The commentator then provides proofs: two verses from Surah al-Baqarah (2:144 and 2:115) establishing the general obligation and the exception in hardship; the hadith of Jabir about the cloudy night where the Prophet validated their prayer prayed in the wrong direction; a quote from al-Shafi'i's al-Umm regarding ijtihad; and the hadith of the change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Ka'ba, showing that turning during prayer is valid. In the Hanafi school, facing the qibla is a shart (condition) for the validity of prayer, and ijtihad is obligatory when the direction is uncertain. The ruling that no repetition is required after ijtihad, even if wrong, is based on the principle that one who exercises ijtihad is excused if mistaken (al-mujtahid mukhti' lahu ajr).

Key Terms
قبلة (qiblah): The direction of the Ka'ba in Mecca which must be faced during prayer.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): The effort to determine the correct qibla direction by using signs and reasoning when the direction is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If after completing prayer in ijtihad, a person realizes they faced the wrong direction, what is the ruling?
A) Prayer is invalid, must repeat
B) Prayer is valid, no repeat
C) Prayer is valid but must repeat before next prayer
D) Prayer is invalid only if wrong

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla is a fard condition, but fear allows any direction, and sincere ijtihad excuses post-prayer error.

Salah — Prayer

The Six Faraid of Prayer: Enumeration and Proofs
Enumeration of the six faraid of prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six faraid of prayer in the Hanafi school and cite the Quranic and hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
The six faraid are the indispensable pillars of prayer; omitting any invalidates the prayer.

Prayer is built upon essential pillars (faraid) that, if any is omitted, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated. This passage from Al-Quduri enumerates these six faraid and provides scriptural proofs, laying the foundation for understanding the structure of salah. While the text mentions five due to an OCR issue, the Hanafi school consistently counts six, with the final sitting as the sixth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Listed Faraid
Read the Arabic text and find the five faraid explicitly mentioned: takbir (tahrimah), standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud). Note that the sixth, final sitting (qa'dah akhirah), is missing due to OCR corruption; it is part of the full Hanafi list.
The text says 'six' but only shows five; the sixth is found in complete manuscripts.
2
Examine the Proofs for Each Fard
The passage quotes verses and a hadith for each fard. For takbir: Surah al-Muddaththir (3) and the hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir'. For qiyam: Surah al-Baqarah (238). For qira'ah: Surah al-Muzzammil (20). For ruku': Surah al-Hajj (77) and Surah al-Baqarah (43). For sujud: part of the same verse from Surah al-Hajj.
The proofs are from 'dalil naqli' (textual evidence).
3
Understand the Hanafi Classification of Fard vs. Wajib
In the Hanafi school, these six acts are fard (obligatory pillars) that cannot be omitted without invalidating the prayer. Other acts like reciting Al-Fatihah are considered wajib (obligatory but requiring compensation if missed).
Distinguish between rukn (fard) and wajib; omission of a rukn makes the prayer batil, while omission of a wajib requires sujud al-sahw.
4
Apply the Knowledge to Prayer Practice
When performing any fard prayer, ensure all six faraid are present. If any is missed intentionally or unintentionally, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. Use the proofs to justify the ruling.
This lesson focuses on identification and proof; practical implementation comes in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صِفَةِ الصَّلَاةِ فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ : التَّحْرِيمَةُ : وَالْقِيَامُ وَالْقِرَاءَةُ لِ وَالرَّكُوعُ هي وَالسُّجُودُ اوجه (۱) الأية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ التَّحْرِيمَةُ \ وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبّر ، (سورة المدثر، أيت (3) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ التَّحْرِيمَةُ \ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ : «مِفْتَاحُ الصَّلَاةِ الطُّهُورُ، وَتَحْرِيمُهَا التَّكْبِيرُ ، وَتَحْلِيلُها التَسْلِيمُ، وَلَا صَلَاةَ لِمَنْ ثُمَّ يَقْرَأْ بِالحَمْدُ، 2/سنن وَسُورَةٍ فِي فَرِيضَةٍ أَوْ غَيْرِهَا، سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تَحْرِيمِ الصَّلَاةِ وَتَحْلِيلِهَا ، نمبر 238 / ابوداود، بَابُ الْإِمَامِ يُحْدِثُ بَعْدَ مَا يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنْ آخِرِ الرَّكْعَةِ، نمبر 618) وجه (۳) قول التابعِي لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ التَّحْرِيمَةُ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «إِذَا نَسِيَ تكْبِيرَةَ الِافْتِتَاح اسْتَأْنَفَ، مصنف ابن شيبه فِي الرَّجُلِ يَنْسَى تَكْبِيرَةَ الافتتاح، نمبر 2465/مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ مَنْ نَسِيَ تَكْبِيرَةَ الِاسْتِفْتَاح، نمبر 2537) وجه (۴) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ التَّحْرِيمَةُ وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى ) ، (سورة الاعلي، أيت (15) وجه: (ا) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ .... وَالْقِيَامُ \ ﴿وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَنِتِينَ﴾ (سورة البقرة، أيت 238) وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ .... وَالْقِرَاءَةُ \ فَأَقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَوٰةَ وَءَاتُوا الزَّكَوةَ ،(سورة المزمل، أيت 20) وجه: (ا) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةَ.... وَالرَّكُوعُ يَتأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُواْ أَرْكَعُواْ وَاسْجُدُوا وَاعْبُدُوا رَبَّكُمْ وَأَفْعَلُوا الْخَيْرَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تُفْلِحُونَ﴾ (سورة الحج 77) ه وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ .... وَالرّكُوعُ الوَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَوةَ وَءَاتُوا الزَّكَوةَ وَأَرْكَعُوا مَعَ الرَّاكِعِينَ) ،(سورة البقرة، أيت 43) اصول : صفت نماز سے مراد ہیئت نماز ہے کہ نماز کس طرح پڑھے اور اس میں کیا کیا پڑھا جائے۔
Chapter of Description of Prayer: The obligatory acts of prayer are six: the takbir (prohibition), standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. [Proofs:] Face (1): The verse to establish the six faraid, the takbir: 'And your Lord glorify' (Surah al-Muddaththir 3). Face (2): The hadith... from Abu Sa'id: 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is the takbir, and its permission (to leave) is the taslim.' Face (3): The saying of the Tabi'i... from Ibrahim: 'If one forgets the opening takbir, he must start over.' Face (4): The verse '...and mentioned the name of his Lord and prayed' (Surah al-A'la 15). Face (a): The verse for standing: 'And stand before Allah with devotion' (Surah al-Baqarah 238). Face (1): The verse for recitation: 'So recite what is easy of it and establish prayer and give zakah' (Surah al-Muzzammil 20). Face (a): The verse for bowing: 'O you who have believed, bow and prostrate...' (Surah al-Hajj 77). Face (1): The verse for bowing: '...and bow with those who bow.' (Surah al-Baqarah 43). Principle: The description of prayer means the form of prayer—how to pray and what to recite.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage enumerates the six fard (obligatory) acts of prayer according to the Hanafi school, though the text only lists five due to OCR corruption; the sixth is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah). The first fard is Takbirat al-Ihram (opening takbir), proven by Quranic command to glorify Allah (Surah al-Muddaththir 3) and the hadith 'its prohibition is the takbir.' The second is Qiyam (standing) from Surah al-Baqarah 238. The third is Qira'ah (recitation of Quran) from Surah al-Muzzammil 20. The fourth is Ruku' (bowing) from Surah al-Hajj 77 and Surah al-Baqarah 43. The fifth is Sujud (prostration) from the same verse (Surah al-Hajj 77 includes 'prostrate'). The sixth, missing here, is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) for the amount of reciting the tashahhud. The Urdu note defines 'sifat al-salah' as the practical manner of performing prayer.

Key Terms
التَّحْرِيمَةُ (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that prohibits worldly actions and begins the prayer.
الْقِرَاءَةُ (al-qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran during prayer, at least one short verse or equivalent.
الرَّكُوعُ (al-ruku'): Bowing so that hands reach knees and back is straight.

Key Takeaway
The six faraid are the essential pillars of prayer; their omission invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer

The Six Obligatory Elements of Prayer: Ruling and Proofs
Listing and proving the six obligatory elements of salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six fara'id of salah and explain the evidence for each from Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
Six pillars uphold the prayer — omit any one, and the prayer collapses.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn establishes the six obligatory elements of Salah. Each element is supported by clear textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding these pillars and their proofs is essential for correct prayer and for appreciating how the Hanafi school derives rulings from primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six elements
Read the matn's opening statement: 'The obligatory elements of prayer are six'. List them in order: takbir (tahrimah), standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), prostration (sujud), and final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) for the duration of tashahhud.
Memorize this list — it is foundational for the rest of salah fiqh.
2
Locate the proof for each element
The author provides multiple proofs for the takbir and the final sitting, and single proofs for the others. For example, the takbir is proven by the verse 'Wa rabbaka fakabbir' and the hadith 'Miftah al-salah al-tuhur...'. Identify the primary proof for each of the six.
Some proofs are repeated (e.g., takbir has two verses and a hadith). Focus on the strongest or most direct proof.
3
Analyze how each proof indicates obligation
For each verse or hadith, determine the imperative or explicit command. For example, 'Fakabbir' is an imperative (amr) and in Hanafi usul, an imperative indicates obligation (wujub) unless a qarinah specifies otherwise. Similarly, the hadith 'la salata liman lam yaqra' indicates that recitation is obligatory.
The Hanafi principle 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub' is applied to each command.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on the final sitting
The matn says the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is fard. However, Abu Yusuf considers it wajib (omission requires sajdah sahw but does not invalidate). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is fard, as held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
This dispute does not affect the list of six — both agree it is an obligatory element, but differ on whether it can be compensated.
5
Understand the consequences of omission
If any of the six fara'id is omitted deliberately or forgetfully, the prayer is invalid (batil) and must be repeated. This is in contrast to wajibat (like tasbih in ruku') which can be compensated by sajdah sahw.
The Urdu explanation at the end emphasizes: if the worshipper stands before completing the final sitting, the prayer is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صِفَةِ الصَّلَاةِ. فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةٌ: التَّحْرِيمَةُ، وَالْقِيَامُ، وَالْقِرَاءَةُ، وَالرَّكُوعُ، وَالسُّجُودُ، وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ. وَمَا زَادَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ. وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الرَّجُلُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ كَبَّرَ.
وجه: (١) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ التَّحْرِيمَةُ: ﴿وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِّرْ﴾ (سورة المدثر، آية ٣).
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ التَّحْرِيمَةُ: عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «مِفْتَاحُ الصَّلَاةِ الطُّهُورُ، وَتَحْرِيمُهَا التَّكْبِيرُ، وَتَحْلِيلُهَا التَّسْلِيمُ، وَلَا صَلَاةَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَقْرَأْ بِالْحَمْدُ وَسُورَةٍ فِي فَرِيضَةٍ أَوْ غَيْرِهَا». (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تَحْرِيمِ الصَّلَاةِ وَتَحْلِيلِهَا، نمبر ٢٣٨ / أبو داود، بَابُ الْإِمَامِ يُحْدِثُ بَعْدَ مَا يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنْ آخِرِ الرَّكْعَةِ، نمبر ٦١٨).
وجه: (٣) قول التابعي لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ التَّحْرِيمَةُ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا نَسِيَ تَكْبِيرَةَ الِافْتِتَاحِ اسْتَأْنَفَ». (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَنْسَى تَكْبِيرَةَ الِافْتِتَاحِ، نمبر ٢٤٦٥ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ مَنْ نَسِيَ تَكْبِيرَةَ الِاسْتِفْتَاحِ، نمبر ٢٥٣٧).
وجه: (٤) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ التَّحْرِيمَةُ: ﴿وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى﴾ (سورة الأعلى، آية ١٥).
وجه: (١) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ وَالْقِيَامُ: ﴿وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَانِتِينَ﴾ (سورة البقرة، آية ٢٣٨).
وجه: (١) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ وَالْقِرَاءَةُ: ﴿فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَاةَ وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ﴾ (سورة المزمل، آية ٢٠).
وجه: (١) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةَ وَالرَّكُوعُ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ارْكَعُوا وَاسْجُدُوا وَاعْبُدُوا رَبَّكُمْ وَافْعَلُوا الْخَيْرَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تُفْلِحُونَ﴾ (سورة الحج، آية ٧٧).
وجه: (١) الآية لثبوت فَرَائِضُ الصَّلَاةِ سِتَّةُ وَالرَّكُوعُ: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَاةَ وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ وَارْكَعُوا مَعَ الرَّاكِعِينَ﴾ (سورة البقرة، آية ٤٣).
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ: عَنْ رِفَاعَةَ بْنِ رَافِعٍ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ ... فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَكَ قُرْآنٌ فَاقْرَأْ، وَإِلَّا فَاحْمَدِ اللَّهَ وَكَبِّرْهُ وَهَلِّلْهُ، ثُمَّ ارْكَعْ فَاطْمَئِنَّ رَاكِعًا، ثُمَّ اعْتَدِلْ قَائِمًا، ثُمَّ اسْجُدْ فَاعْتَدِلْ سَاجِدًا، ثُمَّ اجْلِسْ فَاطْمَئِنَّ جَالِسًا، ثُمَّ قُمْ، فَإِذَا فَعَلْتَ ذَلِكَ فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُكَ، وَإِنْ انْتَقَصْتَ مِنْهُ شَيْئًا انْتَقَصْتَ مِنْ صَلَاتِكَ. (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي وَصْفِ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر ٣٠٢).
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ: ثُمَّ ارْفَعْ حَتَّى تَطْمَئِنَّ جَالِسًا، وَافْعَلْ ذَلِكَ فِي صَلَاتِكَ كُلِّهَا. (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي وَصْفِ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر ٣٠٣).
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ: أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ مَسْعُودٍ أَخَذَ بِيَدِهِ، وَأَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَخَذَ بِيَدِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، فَعَلَّمَهُ التَّشَهُدَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، فَذَكَرَ مِثْلَ دُعَاءِ حَدِيثِ الْأَعْمَشِ: «إِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا أَوْ قَضَيْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ قَضَيْتَ صَلَاتَكَ، إِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقُومَ فَقُمْ، وَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقْعُدَ فَاقْعُدْ». (سنن أبي داود، بَابُ التَّشَهُدِ، نمبر ٩٧٠).
وجه: (٤) الحديث لثبوت وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَضَى الْإِمَامُ الصَّلَاةَ وَقَعَدَ فَأَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمَ، فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ، وَمَنْ كَانَ خَلْفَهُ مِمَّنْ أَتَمَّ الصَّلَاةَ». (سنن أبي داود، بَابُ الْإِمَامِ يُحْدِثُ بَعْدَ مَا يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنْ آخِرِ الرَّكْعَةِ، نمبر ٦١٧).
وجه: (١) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الرَّجُلُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ كَبَّرَ: ﴿وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِّرْ﴾ (سورة المدثر، آية ٣).
وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الرَّجُلُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ كَبَّرَ: ﴿وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى﴾ (سورة الأعلى، آية ١٥).
اصول: صفت نماز سے مراد ہیئت نماز ہے کہ نماز کس طرح پڑھے اور اس میں کیا کیا پڑھی جائے۔ تعدہ اخیرہ میں اتنی مقدار میں بیٹھنا کہ جتنی دیر میں تشہد پڑھا جاتا ہے یہ فرض ہے اگر اس سے پہلے مصلی کھڑا ہو جائے تو نماز نہیں ہو گی۔
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. The obligatory elements of prayer are six: the takbir (tahrimah), standing, recitation, bowing, prostration, and the final sitting for the duration of the tashahhud. Anything beyond that is sunnah. And when a man enters his prayer, he says the takbir. Proof (1): The verse for the establishment of the six obligatory elements, the takbir: 'And your Lord, glorify.' (Surah al-Muddaththir, 3). Proof (2): The hadith for the establishment of the six obligatory elements, the takbir: From Abu Sa'id, he said: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, 'The key to prayer is purification, its opening is the takbir, its closing is the taslim, and there is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in an obligatory or supererogatory prayer.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on the opening and closing of prayer, no. 238; Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the imam who has an event after raising his head from the last rak'ah, no. 618). Proof (3): The saying of the tabi'i for the establishment of the six obligatory elements, the takbir: From Ibrahim, he said, 'If one forgets the takbir of iftitah, he must start over.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, on the man who forgets the takbir of iftitah; no. 2465; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on one who forgets the takbir of iftitah, no. 2537). Proof (4): The verse for the establishment of the six obligatory elements, the takbir: 'And he mentions the name of his Lord and prays.' (Surah al-A'la, 15). Proof (1): The verse for the establishment of standing: 'And stand before Allah in devotion.' (Surah al-Baqarah, 238). Proof (1): The verse for the establishment of recitation: 'So recite what is easy of it, and establish prayer and give zakah.' (Surah al-Muzzammil, 20). Proof (1): The verse for the establishment of bowing: 'O you who have believed, bow and prostrate and worship your Lord and do good that you may succeed.' (Surah al-Hajj, 77). Proof (1): The verse for the establishment of bowing: 'And establish prayer and give zakah and bow with those who bow.' (Surah al-Baqarah, 43). Proof (1): The hadith for the establishment of the final sitting for the duration of the tashahhud: From Rifa'ah ibn Rafi' that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ ... 'If you have some Quran, recite; otherwise, praise Allah, magnify Him, and say La ilaha illa Allah. Then bow and be still while bowing; then rise and stand straight; then prostrate and be still while prostrating; then sit and be still while sitting; then stand. If you do that, your prayer is complete, and if you omit anything, you have diminished your prayer.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on the description of prayer, no. 302). Proof (2): The hadith for the establishment of the final sitting: 'Then raise until you are still while sitting, and do that throughout your prayer.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 303). Proof (3): The hadith for the establishment of the final sitting: That Abdullah ibn Mas'ud took his hand, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ took the hand of Abdullah and taught him the tashahhud in prayer, and he mentioned similar to the supplication of the hadith of al-A'mash: 'When you say this or complete this, you have completed your prayer; if you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the tashahhud, no. 970). Proof (4): The hadith for the establishment of the final sitting: From Abdullah ibn Amr that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, 'When the imam completes the prayer and sits, and then has an event before speaking, his prayer is complete, and those behind him who completed the prayer as well.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the imam who has an event after raising his head from the last rak'ah, no. 617). Proof (1): The verse for the establishment of 'when a man enters his prayer, he says takbir': 'And your Lord, glorify' (Surah al-Muddaththir, 3). Proof (2): The verse: 'And he mentions the name of his Lord and prays' (Surah al-A'la, 15). Principles: The description of prayer means the form of prayer: how to pray and what to recite. The final sitting for the duration of the tashahhud is obligatory; if the worshipper stands before that, his prayer is not valid.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof statement from al-Quduri's matn, clarified with Quranic verses and hadiths. It lists the six obligatory elements (fara'id) of salah: 1) takbirat al-ihram (the opening takbir), 2) standing (qiyam), 3) recitation (qira'ah), 4) bowing (ruku'), 5) prostration (sujud), and 6) the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) for the duration of the tashahhud. Anything beyond these is sunnah, not fard. The author then supports each element with textual evidence. For the takbir, he quotes Surah al-Muddaththir 3 and the hadith 'the key to prayer is purification, its opening is the takbir, its closing is the taslim.' Also the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that forgetting the takbir necessitates restarting. For standing, the verse 'Stand before Allah in devotion' (Surah al-Baqarah 238). For recitation, 'So recite what is easy of it' (Surah al-Muzzammil 20). For bowing, two verses: Surah al-Hajj 77 and Surah al-Baqarah 43. For prostration, it is included in the bowing verse. For the final sitting, four proofs: the hadith of Rifa'ah ibn Rafi' describing the prayer with the explicit instruction to sit and be still; another hadith from Tirmidhi; the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud teaching tashahhud and saying 'when you have said this, you have completed your prayer'; and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr about the imam whose prayer is complete after sitting. The final sitting is considered fard, not just wajib, because omitting it before reaching the tashahhud invalidates the prayer. The Urdu explanation (usul) clarifies that the ‘description of prayer’ refers to its form (hay'ah), and stresses that the final sitting for the tashahhud is fard; if the worshipper stands before that, the prayer is invalid. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position, though Abu Yusuf considers it wajib (requiring sajdah sahw). The mufta bihi is that it is fard, as stated by al-Quduri.

Key Terms
التَّحْرِيمَةُ (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that makes the prayer begin and prohibits worldly actions.
الْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ (al-qa'dah fi akhir al-salah): The final sitting after the last sujud, for the duration of the tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many obligatory elements (fara'id) are in Salah?
A) Five
B) Six
C) Seven
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school identifies six obligatory elements (fara'id) of prayer, each proven by clear dalil from Quran and Sunnah; omitting any one invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Final Sitting of Prayer: Obligation and Duration
Ruling on obligatory sitting duration and opening takbir with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum obligation of the final sitting in prayer and identify the proofs for the opening takbir.

Core Idea
The final sitting must last the tashahhud; the prayer opens with takbir — each proven by hadith and Quran.

This lesson anchors two essential rulings from al-Quduri: the minimum duration of the final sitting and the commencement of prayer with takbir. Beginners often assume the sitting is merely recommended, but the text and its proofs establish obligation. Understanding these rulings with their evidence builds a strong foundation for salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate in the text: (1) the final sitting must be at least the time to recite tashahhud; extra is sunnah. (2) The prayer begins with takbir.
2
Examine the proof for the sitting
The text quotes four hadith: three from Tirmidhi and one from Abu Dawud. The key phrase is 'then sit until you are at ease' from the hadith of Rifa'ah ibn Rafi', indicating obligation via command.
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud allows standing after tashahhud, confirming its completion.
3
Examine the proof for the opening takbir
Two Quranic verses: 'And your Lord magnify' (74:3) and 'And mentions the name of his Lord and prays' (87:15). The first directly commands takbir, the second pairs remembrance with prayer.
4
Understand the legal consequence
The Urdu gloss states: sitting for the duration of tashahhud is fard; if the worshipper stands before completing it, the prayer is invalid. This shows the binding nature.
In Hanafi terminology, the final sitting is wajib (obligatory), while some later scholars called it fard to emphasize its necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صِفَةِ الصَّلَاةِ
وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ وَمَا زَادَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ. وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الرَّجُلُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ كَبَّرَ.
ثُمَّ ذُكِرَتِ الْأَحَادِيثُ:
وجه (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ: عَنْ رِفَاعَةَ بْنِ رَافِعٍ، رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَمَا هُوَ جَالِسٌ فِي المَسْجِدِ يَوْمًا .... فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَكَ قُرْآنٌ فَاقْرَأْ، وَإِلَّا فَاحْمَدِ اللَّهَ وَكَبِرْهُ وَهَلِلْهُ، ثُمَّ ارْكَعْ فَاطْمَئِنَّ رَاكِعًا ثُمَّ اعْتَدِلْ قَائِمًا، ثُمَّ اسْجُدْ فَاعْتَدِلْ سَاجِدًا، ثُمَّ اجْلِسْ فَاطْمَئِنَّ جَالِسًا، ثُمَّ قُمْ، فَإِذَا فَعَلْتَ ذَلِكَ فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُكَ، وَإِنْ انْتَقَصْتَ مِنْهُ شَيْئًا انْتَقَصْتَ مِنْ صَلَاتِكَ (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي وَصْفِ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر 302)
وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ: ثُمَّ ارْفَعْ حَتَّى تَطْمَئِنَّ جَالِسًا، وَافْعَلْ ذَلِكَ فِي صَلَاتِكَ كُلِّهَا (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي وَصْفِ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر 303)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ: أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ مَسْعُودٍ، بِيَدِهِ، وَأَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَخَذَ بِيَدِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، فَعَلَّمَهُ التَّشَهدَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، فَذَكَرَ مِثْلَ دُعَاءِ حَدِيثِ الْأَعْمَشِ: «إِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا أَوْ قَضَيْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ قَضَيْتَ صَلَاتَكَ، إِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقُومَ فَقُمْ، وَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقْعُدَ فَاقْعُدْ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ التَّشَهدِ، نمبر 970)
وجه (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَالْقَعْدَةُ فِي آخِرِ الصَّلَاةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا قَضَى الْإِمَامُ الصَّلَاةَ وَقَعَدَ فَأَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمَ، فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ، وَمَنْ كَانَ خَلْفَهُ مِمَّنْ أَتَمَّ الصَّلَاةَ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الْإِمَامِ يُحْدِثُ بَعْدَ مَا يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنْ آخِرِ الركعة، نمبر 617)
وجه (ا) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الرَّجُلُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ كَبَّرَ: وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِّر (سورة المدثر، آية 3)
وجه (۲) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الرَّجُلُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ كَبَّرَ: وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى (سورة الاعلي، آية 15)
اصول: تعدہ اخیرہ میں اتنی مقدار میں بیٹھنا کہ جتنی دیر میں تشہد پڑھا جاتا ہے یہ فرض ہے اگر اس سے پہلے مصلی کھڑا ہو جائے تو نماز نہیں ہو گی.
Chapter on the description of prayer. And the sitting at the end of prayer for the duration of the tashahhud, and what is more than that is sunnah. And when a man enters his prayer, he says takbir. Then the hadith are mentioned: (first) hadith for proof of the sitting at the end of prayer for the duration of tashahhud: from Rifa'ah ibn Rafi'... (second) hadith for proof of the sitting... (third) hadith for proof of the sitting... (fourth) hadith for proof of the sitting... (first) verse for proof of when a man enters his prayer he says takbir: And your Lord magnify (al-Muddaththir 3). (second) verse for proof: And mentions the name of his Lord and prays (al-A'la 15). Principle: In the final sitting, sitting for the duration in which tashahhud is recited is fard; if the worshipper stands before that, the prayer is not valid.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn presents two foundational rulings of prayer description. First, the final sitting (qa'dah) at the end of prayer must last at least the time needed to recite the tashahhud; any additional sitting is sunnah. This indicates that the qa'dah itself is obligatory (fard in the Urdu gloss, or wajib in Hanafi technical terms). Second, the prayer begins with the takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) upon entering. The author then provides four hadith proofs for the sitting ruling and two Quranic verses for the takbir. The hadith include the well-known hadith of Rifa'ah ibn Rafi' describing the complete prayer, and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud teaching the tashahhud and stating that after that one may stand or sit. The verses cited are 'And your Lord magnify' (74:3) and 'And mentions the name of his Lord and prays' (87:15). The Urdu principle at the end confirms that the sitting for tashahhud is considered fard (obligatory) such that if the worshipper stands before completing it, the prayer is invalid. This passage is a memorization anchor for basic prayer rulings.

Key Terms
الْقَعْدَة (al-qa‘dah): The sitting posture in prayer, specifically the final sitting at the end of prayer.
التَّشَهُد (al-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting of prayer.
كَبَّرَ (kabbara): He said 'Allahu Akbar', specifically the takbirat al-ihram opening the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum obligatory duration for the final sitting in prayer?
A) The time to recite al-Fatihah
B) The time to recite the tashahhud
C) The time to say Subhanallah three times
D) There is no minimum; any sitting suffices

Key Takeaway
The final sitting in prayer must last at least the time to recite tashahhud; the opening takbir is obligatory by Quran and Sunnah.

Raising Hands and Substituting Takbir Words
Ruling on raising hands and substitution of takbir with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah method of raising hands with takbir, identify the three alternative phrases accepted by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, explain why Abu Yusuf differs, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Raising hands to ears is sunnah; the takbir can be any phrase conveying Allah's greatness according to the majority.

This passage from al-Quduri covers two practical aspects of starting prayer: how to raise the hands and what counts as the opening takbir. While the hand-raising is a settled sunnah, the wording of the takbir reveals an important intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position and appreciate the school's flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah act of raising hands
Locate the description: the hands are raised with the takbir until the thumbs align with the earlobes. This is the preferred method (sunnah).
Multiple hadith support this, including from Ibn Umar and Malik ibn al-Huwayrith.
2
Recognize the dispute on alternative takbir phrases
The text states that saying 'Allahu Ajal', 'Allahu A'zam', or 'al-Rahmanu Akbar' suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf restricts it to forms containing 'Allahu Akbar' or similar.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Trace the proofs from Quran and Hadith
The author cites verses 74:3 ('magnify your Lord') and 87:15 as general commands for glorification, and a hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet said takbir generally.
The proofs emphasize the essence of takbir, not a specific wording.
4
Analyze the reasoning of both sides
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rely on the quranic generality; Abu Yusuf insists on the exact prophetic practice. Consider which proof is stronger in Hanafi usul.
The dispute revolves around whether the takbir is a fixed worship (tawqifi) or flexible in wording.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The passage and later Hanafi works adopt the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) as the operative fatwa.
The practice is lenient, and the school accepts alternatives.

Source Text

بَابُ صِفَةِ الصَّلَاةِ
وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ مَعَ التَّكْبِيرَةِ حَتَّى يُحَاذِيَ بِإِبْهَامَيْهِ شَحْمَيْ أُذُنَيْهِ. فَإِنْ قَالَ بَدَلًا مِنْ التَّكْبِيرِ اللَّهُ أَجَلُّ أَوْ أَعْظَمُ أَوْ الرَّحْمَنُ أَكْبَرُ أَجْزَاهُ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوْسُف: لا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَقُولَ الله أكبر أو الله الأكبر الله الكبير.
ثُمَّ ذُكِرَتِ الْأَحَادِيثُ:
وجه (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ مَعَ التَّكْبِيرَةِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ، إِذَا قَامَ لِلصَّلَاةِ، رَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ حَتَّى تَكُونَا حَذْوَ مَنْكِبَيْهِ. ثُمَّ كَبَّرَ (مسلم، باب اسْتِحْبَابِ رَفْعِ الْيَدَيْنِ حَذْوَ الْمَنْكِبَيْنِ مَعَ تَكْبِيرَةِ الإِحْرَامِ، نمبر 390/سنن ابوداود، باب رَفْعِ الْيَدَيْنِ في الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر 722)
وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ مَعَ التَّكْبِيرَةِ: أَنَّهُ رَأَى مَالِكَ بْنَ الْحُوَيْرِثِ، إِذَا صَلَّى كَبَّرَ ثُمَّ رَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ. وَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَرْكَعَ رَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ. وَإِذَا رَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ مِنَ الرَّكُوعِ رَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ وَحَدَّثَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يَفْعَلُ هَكَذَا (مسلم، باب اسْتِحْبَابِ رَفْعِ الْيَدَيْنِ حَذْوَ الْمَنْكِبَيْنِ مَعَ تَكْبِيرَةِ الإِحْرَامِ، نمبر 391/سنن ابوداود، باب رَفْعِ الْيَدَيْنِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر 726)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ مَعَ التَّكْبِيرَةِ: عَنْ مَالِكِ بْنِ الْحُوَيْرِثِ؛ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ إِذَا كَبَّرَ رَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ حَتَّى يُحَاذِيَ بِهِمَا أُذُنَيْهِ. وَإِذَا رَكَعَ رَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ حَتَّى يُحَاذِيَ بِهِمَا أُذُنَيْهِ (مسلم، باب اسْتِحْبَابِ رَفْعِ الْيَدَيْنِ حَذْوَ الْمَنْكِبَيْنِ مَعَ تَكْبِيرَةِ الإِحْرَامِ، نمبر 391)
وجه (ا) الآية لثبوت فَإِنْ قَالَ بَدَلًا مِنْ التَّكْبِيرِ اللَّهُ أَجَلُّ ...: وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِّر (سورة المدثر، آية 3)
وجه (۲) الآية لثبوت فَإِنْ قَالَ بَدَلًا مِنْ التَّكْبِيرِ ...: وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى (سورة الاعلي، آية 15)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ قَالَ بَدَلًا مِنْ التَّكْبِيرِ ...: عَنْ أَبي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِي، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا قَامَ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ بِاللَّيْلِ كَبَّرَ (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا يَقُولُ عِنْدَ افْتِتَاحَ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر 242)
اصول: نماز میں پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے یا تکبیر تحریمہ کہے دونوں درست ہے، البتہ احناف: پہلے ہاتھ اٹھانا بہتر ہے۔
Chapter on the description of prayer. And he raises his hands with the takbir until he aligns with his thumbs the lobes of his ears. Then if he says instead of the takbir 'Allahu Ajal' or 'A'zam' or 'al-Rahmanu Akbar', it suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible unless he says 'Allahu Akbar' or 'Allahu al-Akbar' or 'Allahu al-Kabir'. Then the hadith are mentioned: (first) hadith for proof of raising hands with the takbir: from Ibn Umar... (second) hadith... (third) hadith... (first) verse for proof of if he says instead of takbir...: And your Lord magnify (al-Muddaththir 3). (second) verse: And mentions the name of his Lord and prays (al-A'la 15). (third) hadith for proof: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... Principle: In prayer, whether one raises hands first or says the takbir, both are correct, but the Hanafis: raising hands first is better.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on prayer description with two rulings. First, the sunnah method of raising hands with the opening takbir: the hands are raised until the thumbs align with the earlobes. This is supported by multiple hadith, including from Ibn Umar and Malik ibn al-Huwayrith. Second, a more subtle issue: if someone substitutes the phrase 'Allahu Akbar' with other words like 'Allahu Ajal' (Allah is more majestic) or 'Allahu A'zam' (Allah is greater) or 'al-Rahmanu Akbar' (the Most Merciful is greater), does it suffice? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say yes, because the essence is glorification of Allah. Abu Yusuf disagrees, requiring the exact words 'Allahu Akbar', 'Allahu al-Akbar', or 'Allahu al-Kabir'. The author provides Quranic verses (74:3 and 87:15) as general proofs for takbir, and a hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing the Prophet said takbir at night prayer. The Urdu principle notes that while both sequences (hands first then takbir or takbir first then hands) are permissible, the preferred Hanafi practice is to raise hands first. This passage is significant for its intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, showing that even within the school there is room for difference on the precise wording of the takbir.

Key Terms
يُحَاذِيَ (yuḥādhī): To align or make parallel; here used for the thumbs reaching the earlobes.
بَدَلًا (badalan): As a substitute; in place of the usual takbir phrase.
أَجْزَاهُ (ajzāhu): It suffices him; the action is valid and acceptable.
شَحْمَيْ أُذُنَيْهِ (shaḥmay udhunayhi): The lobes of his ears.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Allahu al-Akbar
B) Allahu al-Kabir
C) al-Rahmanu Akbar
D) Allahu al-Asghar

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is fulfilled by any phrase clearly meaning 'Allah is greater'; the Hanafi school's majority view provides flexibility.

Placing Right Hand on Left in Prayer: Sunnah Muakkadah
Ruling with three hadith proofs for hand placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement in prayer and identify the three hadith proofs that establish it as a sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
Placing right hand on left is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib, proven by prophetic practice.

The Hanafi school teaches that during prayer, a person should place the right hand over the left, below the navel. This lesson examines the three key hadith proofs cited in the classical texts, showing how the Prophet's own practice (fi'l) establishes a recommended act, not an obligatory one. Understanding this helps distinguish between sunnah and wajib in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing the right hand over the left during prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed recommended act), not wajib.
The Arabic word 'ya'tamidu' implies a resting action, not a commanded pillar.
2
Locate the three hadith proofs
The passage cites three hadith: (1) Wail ibn Hujr's report of seeing the Prophet place right hand on left, (2) Qabisa ibn Hulb reporting that the Prophet used to take his left hand with his right while leading prayer, (3) Ali's statement that 'it is from the sunnah to place palm on palm below the navel.'
These hadith are ahad (single-transmitter) but collectively strengthen the practice.
3
Analyze the nature of the proof
All three proofs are reports of the Prophet's actual practice (fi'l). According to Hanafi usul, a prophetic action (fi'l) indicates desirability (sunnah) unless there is evidence indicating obligation. Since no commanding text is present, the action remains at the level of sunnah.
This contrasts with a fard or wajib which would require a command (amr) in the Quran or mutawatir hadith.
4
Note the placement detail
The hadith from Ali specifies 'below the navel' (tahta al-surrah). This is the relied-upon Hanafi position. Other schools differ: Shafi'i places hands on the chest, Maliki leaves them at sides.
The Hanafi position is based on this explicit wording from Ali, who is a major Companion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صِفَةِ الصَّلَاةِ
ال وَيَعْتَمِدُ بِيَدِهِ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى 
لوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَعْتَمِدُ بِيَدِهِ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى \ عَنْ أَبِيهِ، وَائِلِ بْنِ حُجْرٍ ؛ رَأَى النَّبِيَّ .... ثُمَّ وَضَعَ يَدَهُ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى، (مسلم شريف، بَاب وَضْعِ يَدِهِ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى بَعْدَ تَكْبِيرَةِ الإِحْرَامِ ، نمبر 401 سنن ابوداود بَابُ وَضْعِ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى فِي الصَّلاة، نمبر 755 / بخاري شريف، بَابُ وَضْع الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى، غبر 740)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيَعْتَمِدُ بِيَدِهِ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى \ عَنْ قَبِيصَةَ بْنِ هُلْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: «كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَؤُمُّنَا، فَيَأْخُذُ شِمَالَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ، سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي وَضْعِ اليَمِينِ عَلَى الشِّمَالِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ ، نمبر 252/
وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وَيَعْتَمِدُ بِيَدِهِ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى \ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا ، قَالَ: «مِنَ السُّنَّةِ وَضْعُ الْكَفِّ عَلَى الْكَفِّ فِي الصَّلَاةِ تَحْتَ السُّرَّةِ، سنن ابوداود بَابُ وَضْعِ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى الْيُسْرَى في الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر 756/سنن دارقطني، بَابُ مَنْ يَصْلُحُ أَنْ يَقُومَ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ، نمبر 1089/سنن بيهقي، بَابُ وَضْع الْيَدَيْنِ عَلَى الصَّدْرِ في الصَّلَاةِ مِنَ السُّنَّةِ، نمبر 2341)
Chapter of the description of prayer. And he places his right hand on his left. Then he says: 'Glory be to You, O Allah, and with Your praise, and blessed is Your name, and exalted is Your majesty, and there is no deity besides You.' And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan. [Proof 1] The hadith establishing 'And he places his right hand on his left' from Wail ibn Hujr: He saw the Prophet... then he placed his right hand on his left. (Muslim, etc.) [Proof 2] The hadith establishing 'And he places his right hand on his left' from Qabisa ibn Hulb from his father: 'The Messenger of Allah used to lead us in prayer, and he would take his left hand with his right.' (Tirmidhi) [Proof 3] The hadith establishing 'And he places his right hand on his left': 'Ali said: 'It is from the sunnah to place the palm on the palm in prayer below the navel.' (Abu Dawud, Darqutni, Bayhaqi)
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on placing the right hand over the left during prayer, a practice established by the Hanafi school. The commentary provides three hadith proofs. The first from Wail ibn Hujr reports that the Prophet placed his right hand on his left. The second from Qabisa ibn Hulb confirms the same practice. The third, from Ali ibn Abi Talib, specifies that the hands should be placed below the navel, which is the Hanafi position. The passage thus grounds a sunnah act in prophetic practice.

Key Terms
يَعْتَمِدُ (ya'tamidu): to place, to rest upon (the hand on the other hand)
السُّنَّةِ (al-sunnah): The prophetic practice; here specifically the way the Prophet prayed with hands folded
تَحْتَ السُّرَّةِ (tahta al-surrah): below the navel

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Placing the right hand on the left below the navel is a confirmed sunnah of the Prophet, established by multiple ahadith, and is the relied-upon practice in the Hanafi school.

Reciting Thana (Subhanaka) After Takbir
Ruling with hadith proofs for reciting Thana at start of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Thana after Takbir and identify its proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Reciting Thana (Subhanaka) after Takbir is sunnah muakkadah, preferred over other opening supplications.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi position on the opening supplication after the first takbir in prayer. It specifies that the recitation of Thana (Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...) is sunnah and superior to other transmitted supplications. The author supports this with two hadith references, though they are not direct proofs of the exact wording. The Urdu usul note clarifies that while other supplications are reported, reciting Thana is better according to the Hanafis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting Thana (Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...) immediately after the opening takbir. The Hanafi ruling: sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet consistently performed it and recommended it, but it is not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text cites two hadith: one from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (Tirmidhi) that the Prophet would say takbir when starting night prayer, and another from Ali (Muslim) that he said 'Wajjahtu wajhiya'. These show the Prophet recited an opening supplication but do not specify Thana.
The Hanafi school uses these as evidence that some supplication is sunnah; the specific preference for Thana comes from other narrations (e.g., from Aisha).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith prove that the Prophet recited something after takbir. Since there are multiple authentic narrations, the Hanafis prefer Thana because it is more comprehensive in praise and has a stronger chain according to their criteria.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah; wajh al-dalalah is that the Prophet's action indicates sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) prefer different openings like 'Wajjahtu wajhiya'. All are permissible and sunnah; the difference is in preference (afdaliyyah).
The Hanafis consider Thana better, but the prayer is valid with any authentic opening supplication.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is to recite Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika after the opening takbir. This is the recommended practice.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَقُولُ سُبْحَانَكَ اللَّهُمَّ وَبِحَمْدِكَ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا قَامَ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ بِاللَّيْلِ كَبَّرَ ، سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا يَقُولُ عِنْدَ افْتِتَاحِ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر (242)

أصول : نماز میں دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھے۔ اور ثنا پڑھے ، یوں تو دوسری دعائیں بھی منقول ہیں لیکن ثنا پڑھنا بہتر ہے احناف کے نزدیک۔
Then he says: 'Glory be to You, O Allah, and with Your praise, and blessed is Your name, and exalted is Your majesty, and there is no deity besides You.' The Ruling of Isti'adha (Seeking Refuge) in Prayer: Sunnah Not Wajib
Ruling with Quranic and hadith proofs for seeking refuge before recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Isti'adha and explain why the Quranic command is interpreted as sunnah rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Isti'adha before recitation is sunnah muakkadah — the Quranic command is a recommendation, not an obligation.

The practice of seeking refuge from Satan before reciting the Quran is rooted in a clear Quranic verse. However, the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah, not fard or wajib. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning behind that classification, drawing on the Quran, prophetic practice, and Hanafi usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Isti'adha (saying 'A'udhu billah') before reciting the Quran in prayer. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet consistently did it and encouraged it, but it is not obligatory.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 16:98: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan.' This is a direct command.
The command is general for all Quran recitation, including in prayer.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fasta'idh' is a command. In Hanafi usul, commands can be for obligation (wujub) or recommendation (nadb). The context and prophetic practice show it is nadb here.
The Prophet did not always command it; his practice indicates recommendation.
4
Consider secondary proofs from hadith
Hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri shows the Prophet saying Isti'adha in night prayer. Other hadiths (though some may relate to Basmalah) are cited as supporting evidence for opening recitation.
Proofs 3 and 4 in the text may have been misaligned by OCR, but they reinforce the idea of opening prayer with remembrance.
5
Note cross-madhhab status
The Hanafi position is sunnah muakkadah. Other schools also consider it sunnah or mustahabb; no school holds it as wajib.
The practical difference is slight: all agree the prayer is valid without it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وجه : (1) الآية لثبوت وَيَسْتَعِيذُ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ الشَّيْطَانِ الرَّحِيمِ ﴿فَإِذَا قَرَأْتَ الْقُرْءَانَ فَاسْتَعِذْ بِاللَّهِ مِنَ الشَّيْطَنِ الرَّجِيمِ﴾ (سورة النحل، ايت98)

وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَيَسْتَعِيذُ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ الشَّيْطَانِ الرَّحِيمِ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ، قَالَ: " كَانَ النَّبِيُّ يَفْتَتِحُ صَلَاتَهُ بِ بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَنْ رَأَى الْجَهْرَ بِ بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ} نمبر 245 سنن نسائي، تَرْكُ الجَهْرِ بِه بِسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ ، نمبر 906)

And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan. [Proof 1] The verse establishing this: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan.' (Surah an-Nahl, 16:98) [Proof 2] The hadith establishing this from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for night prayer, he would say takbir, then say Subhanaka... then say 'I seek refuge with Allah, the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing, from the accursed Satan, from his madness, his arrogance, and his poetry.' (Abu Dawud no. 775) [Proof 3] The hadith establishing this from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet used to open his prayer with Bismillahir Rahmanir Rahim.' (Tirmidhi no. 245, Nasa'i no. 906) [Proof 4] The hadith establishing this from Abdullah ibn Mughaffal: 'My father heard me saying Bismillah in prayer and told me to avoid innovation...' Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of saying Isti'adha (A'udhu billah) before Quranic recitation in prayer. The primary proof is the Quranic command in Surah an-Nahl, verse 98, which is general for all Quran recitation, including in prayer. The Hanafi school holds that Isti'adha is sunnah, not wajib, because the command in the verse is interpreted as recommended (nadb) rather than obligatory due to other contextual factors. The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri provides a specific example of the Prophet's practice. The later hadith proofs (3 and 4) appear to be about Basmalah, but are included under Isti'adha possibly because they relate to opening recitation. The text reflects the author's method of citing all relevant transmissions, even if they touch on adjacent topics.

Key Terms
الاستعاذة (al-isti'adha): The act of seeking refuge with Allah from Satan, usually by saying 'A'udhu billahi min ash-shaytan ir-rajim'
الشَّيْطَانِ الرَّحِيمِ (ash-shaytan ar-rajim): The accursed Satan, from whom refuge is sought
