The Tashahhud Wording: Proofs and Hanafi Preference
Ruling on the wording of tashahhud with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi tashahhud wording and explain why it is preferred based on the hadith evidences and usul reasoning.

Core Idea
The tashahhud wording is sunnah, not fard; its preference is proven by the Prophet's command and teaching method.

This passage presents the precise wording of the tashahhud as transmitted in the Hanafi matn, followed by three hadith proofs from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas. Understanding why Hanafis prefer this version over others requires attention to the command form (amr) in the hadith and the Prophet's pedagogical emphasis. We will work through the textual evidence and the usul reasoning that establishes the wording as sunnah muakkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Wording
Read the matn's tashahhud: 'al-tahiyyatu lillah...' and note each phrase. This is the standard Hanafi recitation.
The matn does not include 'al-mubarakatu' which appears in other versions.
2
Analyze the First Hadith Evidence (Ibn Mas'ud)
The Prophet corrected the companions' practice and commanded 'falyaqul' (let him say) the specific wording. In Hanafi usul, this imperative indicates recommendation (istihbab) for this phrasing.
The hadith is sahih (Bukhari, Muslim) but ahad, hence zanni thubut.
3
Examine the Second and Third Evidences (Ibn 'Abbas)
The Prophet taught the tashahhud as carefully as the Qur'an, emphasizing its importance. These narrations support the same core wording with minor variations ('al-mubarakatu' added).
Hanafis prefer the Ibn Mas'ud version due to the explicit command and earlier transmission.
4
Understand the Hanafi Usul Reasoning
The command form and the Prophet's hands-on teaching method make this version more recommended. Other authentic versions are permissible but not preferred.
This reasoning is from the Urdu usul note in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَتَشَهَّدُ وَالتَّشَهدُ التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ وَالصَّلَوَاتُ وَالطَّيِّبَاتُ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِينَ أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَه إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَ مُحَمَّدًا عَبْدُهُ وَرَسُوْلُهُ
اليُسْرَى، وَوَضَعَ يَدَهُ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى فَخِذِهِ اليُمْنَى وَقَبَضَ أَصَابِعَهُ وَبَسَطَ السَّبَّابَةَ، (مسلم شريف، باب نمبر 3587/ سنن نسائي ، بَابُ قَبْض القِنْتَيْنِ مِنْ أَصَابع الْيَدِ الْيُمْنَ، وَعَقْدِ الْوُسْطَى وَالْإِنْهَامِ مِنْهَا ، نمبر 1268)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَشَهَدُ وَالتَّشَهُدُ التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ وَالصَّلَوَاتُ \ قَالَ: قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ : كُنَّا إِذَا صَلَّيْنَا خَلْفَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قُلْنَا : السَّلَامُ عَلَى جِبْرِيلَ وَمِيكَائِيلَ، السَّلَامُ عَلَى فُلَانٍ وَفُلَانٍ، فَالْتَفَتَ إِلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: إِنَّ اللهَ هُوَ السَّلَامُ، فَإِذَا صَلَّى أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَقُلِ: التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلهِ، وَالصَّلَوَاتُ وَالطَّيِّبَاتُ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، السَّلَامُ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِين الخ، بخاري شريف، بَابُ التَّشَهُدِ فِي الْآخِرَةِ، نمبر 831/(سنن ابوداود، بَابُ التَّشَهُدِ، نمبر 968/ مسلم ، باب التشهد في الصلاة،نمبر402)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَشَهدُ وَالتَّشَهدُ التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ وَالصَّلَوَاتُ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُعَلِّمُنَا التَّشَهدَ كَمَا يُعَلِّمُنَا القُرْآنَ، فَكَانَ يَقُولُ: «التَّحِيَّاتُ الْمُبَارَكَاتُ، الصَّلَوَاتُ الطَّيِّبَاتُ لِلَّهِ، سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، سَلَامٌ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِينَ، أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ، ، سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مِنْهُ أَيْضًا، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّشَهدِ، نمبر 290/سنن نسائي، نَوْعٌ آخَرُ مِنْ التَّشَهُدِ، نمبر 1175)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَشَهَّدُ وَالتَّشَهدُ التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ وَالصَّلَوَاتُ اعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ؛ أَنَّهُ قَالَ كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يُعَلِّمُنَا التَّشَهدَ كَمَا يُعَلِّمُنَا السُّورَةَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ فَكَانَ يَقُولُ التَّحِيَّاتُ الْمُبَارَكَاتُ الصَّلَوَاتُ لطَّيِّبَاتُ لِلَّهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِينَ. أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ، مسلم شریف، بَاب التَّشَهُدِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ ، نمبر 403 ، سنن ابوداود، بَابُ التَّشَهدِ، نمبر 974)
اصول : احناف کے نزدیک مذکورہ منقول دعاء پڑھنا زیادہ بہتر ہے کیونکہ اس میں امر کا صیغہ ہے جس سے مستحب ہو نا معلوم ہوتا ہے، نیز ہاتھ پکڑ کر سکھانے میں اہمیت بھی ہے،
And he recites the tashahhud: 'Al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibatu, al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, al-salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillahi al-salihin, ashhadu an la ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh.' [Then a hadith about hand position:] ... 'the left, and he placed his right hand on his right thigh, clasped his fingers and extended the index finger.' (Muslim 3587, Nasa'i 1268). Evidence (1) for the tashahhud: 'Abdullah said: 'When we prayed behind the Prophet, we used to say: Peace be upon Jibril and Mika'il...' The Prophet turned to us and said: 'Allah is al-Salam. When one of you prays, let him say: al-Tahiyyatu lillah...'' (Bukhari 831, Abu Dawud 968, Muslim 402). Evidence (2): Ibn 'Abbas said: 'The Messenger of Allah used to teach us the tashahhud as he taught us the Qur'an, and he would say: al-Tahiyyatu al-mubarakatu...' (Tirmidhi 290, Nasa'i 1175). Evidence (3): Ibn 'Abbas: 'He used to teach us the tashahhud as he taught us a surah of the Qur'an, saying: al-Tahiyyatu al-mubarakatu...' (Muslim 403, Abu Dawud 974). Usul: According to the Hanafis, reciting this transmitted supplication is better because it contains a command form, indicating recommendation, and also because the Prophet taught it by taking the hand, showing importance.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi matn for the tashahhud recitation. The wording begins with 'al-tahiyyatu lillah' and includes salutations upon the Prophet and the righteous servants, followed by the two testimonies of faith. The commentator then adduces a hadith about hand position (clasping fingers and extending the index finger), which is part of the sunnah gesture during tashahhud. Then three sets of hadith evidences support the tashahhud wording: the first from Ibn Mas'ud (via 'Abdullah) narrates that the Prophet instructed them to use this specific phrasing after they initially sent salams to angels and individuals. The second and third from Ibn 'Abbas confirm that the Prophet taught this tashahhud as carefully as the Qur'an. The Urdu usul note explains that the Hanafi preference for this wording is based on the command (amr) in the hadith and the fact that the Prophet personally taught it, making it a highly recommended (mustahabb) practice.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The specific recitation of praises and testimonies during the sitting in prayer.
التحيات لله (al-tahiyyātu lillāh): All greetings, blessings, and prayers belong to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it has only one version.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi tashahhud is based on the Prophet's direct instruction in the Ibn Mas'ud hadith; the wording is sunnah muakkadah, and other authentic versions are permissible but less preferred.

The Tashahhud: Ruling, Wording, and Evidence
Ruling on tashahhud with three supporting hadiths and Hanafi usul note

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the tashahhud, recite its transmitted wording, and explain why it is considered sunnah muakkadah based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The tashahhud is a sunnah muakkadah, not fard — the imperative in the hadith indicates recommendation, not obligation.

In this lesson, we examine the tashahhud — the supplication recited in the sitting of prayer. The matn from Al-Quduri provides the exact wording, and the author supports it with three authentic hadiths. The key takeaway: the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah, deriving this from the imperative form in the hadith, consistent with Hanafi usul al-fiqh principles. We will walk through the evidence and understand how the ruling is derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting the tashahhud during the final sitting of prayer. The ruling in the Hanafi school is sunnah muakkadah (emphatically recommended).
Sunnah muakkadah is a level between fard and ordinary sunnah; the Prophet consistently performed it.
2
Locate the dalil
Three authentic hadiths are cited: the first from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (Bukhari, Muslim), the second from Ibn Abbas (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i), and a third similar version. All show the Prophet teaching the tashahhud with an explicit command.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key evidence is the imperative verb "فليقل" (so let him say) in the hadith. In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) without a qarinah (contextual evidence) of obligation indicates istihbab (recommendation).
This is a standard principle: al-amr yufidu al-nadb illa bi qarinah.
4
Note the Hanafi usul note
The author explicitly states that the imperative indicates mustahabb. Additionally, the Prophet teaching the tashahhud while holding the Companion's hand shows its importance but not obligation.
The hand placement description (left hand on left thigh, right hand clenched except index finger) is also a sunnah practice.
5
Apply the ruling
Therefore, reciting the transmitted wording of the tashahhud is sunnah muakkadah. If omitted, the prayer remains valid but the act is incomplete; no compensation is required.
This contrasts with the common misunderstanding that tashahhud is obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صِفَةِ الصَّلَاةِ
٣٢ وَيَتَشَهَّدُ وَالتَّشَهدُ التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ وَالصَّلَوَاتُ وَالطَّيِّبَاتُ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِينَ أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَه إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَ مُحَمَّدًا عَبْدُهُ وَرَسُوْلُهُ
اليُسْرَى، وَوَضَعَ يَدَهُ الْيُمْنَى عَلَى فَخِذِهِ اليُمْنَى وَقَبَضَ أَصَابِعَهُ وَبَسَطَ السَّبَّابَةَ، (مسلم شريف، باب نمبر 3587/ سنن نسائي ، بَابُ قَبْض القِنْتَيْنِ مِنْ أَصَابع الْيَدِ الْيُمْنَ، وَعَقْدِ الْوُسْطَى وَالْإِنْهَامِ مِنْهَا ، نمبر 1268)
۳۴ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَشَهَّدُ وَالتَّشَهُدُ التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ وَالصَّلَوَاتُ \ قَالَ: قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ : كُنَّا إِذَا صَلَّيْنَا خَلْفَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قُلْنَا : السَّلَامُ عَلَى جِبْرِيلَ وَمِيكَائِيلَ، السَّلَامُ عَلَى فُلَانٍ وَفُلَانٍ، فَالْتَفَتَ إِلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: إِنَّ اللهَ هُوَ السَّلَامُ، فَإِذَا صَلَّى أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَقُلِ: التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلهِ، وَالصَّلَوَاتُ وَالطَّيِّبَاتُ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، السَّلَامُ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِين الخ، بخاري شريف، بَابُ التَّشَهُدِ فِي الْآخِرَةِ، نمبر 831/(سنن ابوداود، بَابُ التَّشَهُدِ، نمبر 968/ مسلم ، باب التشهد في الصلاة،نمبر402)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَشَهدُ وَالتَّشَهدُ التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ وَالصَّلَوَاتُ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُعَلِّمُنَا التَّشَهدَ كَمَا يُعَلِّمُنَا القُرْآنَ، فَكَانَ يَقُولُ: «التَّحِيَّاتُ الْمُبَارَكَاتُ، الصَّلَوَاتُ الطَّيِّبَاتُ لِلَّهِ، سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، سَلَامٌ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِينَ، أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ، ، سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مِنْهُ أَيْضًا، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّشَهدِ، نمبر 290/سنن نسائي، نَوْعٌ آخَرُ مِنْ التَّشَهُدِ، نمبر 1175)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَشَهَّدُ وَالتَّشَهدُ التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ وَالصَّلَوَاتُ اعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ؛ أَنَّهُ قَالَ كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يُعَلِّمُنَا التَّشَهدَ كَمَا يُعَلِّمُنَا السُّورَةَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ فَكَانَ يَقُولُ التَّحِيَّاتُ الْمُبَارَكَاتُ الصَّلَوَاتُ لطَّيِّبَاتُ لِلَّهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِينَ. أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ، مسلم شریف، بَاب التَّشَهُدِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ ، نمبر 403 ، سنن ابوداود، بَابُ التَّشَهدِ، نمبر 974) اصول : احناف کے نزدیک مذکورہ منقول دعاء پڑھنا زیادہ بہتر ہے کیونکہ اس میں امر کا صیغہ ہے جس سے مستحب ہو نا معلوم ہوتا ہے، نیز ہاتھ پکڑ کر سکھانے میں اہمیت بھی ہے،
Chapter: Description of Prayer. 32. And he recites the tashahhud, and the tashahhud is: 'The greetings, blessings, and good words are for Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Peace be upon us and upon the righteous servants of Allah. I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger.' ... He places his left hand on his left thigh, and his right hand on his right thigh, and he clenches his fingers and extends the index finger. (Muslim, chapter number 3587 / Sunan Nasa'i ...) 34. Evidence: (1) The hadith establishing 'He recites the tashahhud' ... Abdullah said: We used to say ... The Prophet said: Allah is the giver of peace, so say ... (Bukhari, Muslim) (2) The hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet taught us the tashahhud as he taught us the Quran ... (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) (3) Another hadith from Ibn Abbas ... (Muslim, Abu Dawud) Principle: According to the Hanafis, reciting this transmitted supplication is better because it contains the imperative form which indicates that it is recommended, and also because he taught it while holding their hands.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the tashahhud in prayer from the matn of Al-Quduri, followed by extensive hadith evidence and a Hanafi usul note. The matn states the specific wording of the tashahhud that one should recite. The author then cites three authentic hadiths: the first from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud reports that the Prophet taught them to say 'At-tahiyyatu lillah...' instead of greeting angels; the second from Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet taught tashahhud meticulously like the Quran; the third is a similar narration. The Hanafi principle at the end explains that reciting this transmitted wording is recommended (mustahabb) because the command form implies recommendation, and the fact that the Prophet held their hands while teaching shows its importance.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The supplication recited while sitting in prayer, beginning with 'At-tahiyyatu lillah'.
مستحب (mustahabb): An action recommended and rewarded but not obligatory; leaving it does not incur sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul note, what indicates that reciting the transmitted tashahhud wording is recommended (mustahabb)?
A) Consensus of the Companions
B) The imperative form (فليقل) in the hadith
C) The fact that the Prophet taught it to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud
D) The chapter title

Key Takeaway
The tashahhud is a sunnah muakkadah in Hanafi fiqh, supported by the Prophet's command and taught as he taught the Quran; its omission does not invalidate the prayer.

6 min
No Addition in the First Sitting
Ruling that nothing is added to the tashahhud in the first sitting with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on additions in the first sitting and identify the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
The first sitting is for brief tashahhud only—no extra supplications.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling regarding the first sitting in prayers of three or four rak'ahs. The Hanafi school holds that nothing beyond the tashahhud should be recited, based on the Prophet's practice of sitting briefly. This short ruling is supported by a hadith that describes the Prophet's sitting as if on hot stones, indicating brevity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the first sitting (al-qa'dah al-ula) after two rak'ahs. The ruling is that one does not add anything beyond the tashahhud.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet sat as if on hot stones. This is an ahad hadith found in Sunan Nasa'i and Sunan Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The description of extreme brevity implies that the Prophet did not recite any additional supplications, as that would lengthen the sitting. Thus, only the tashahhud was recited.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools, such as the Shafi'is, allow adding salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet in the first sitting. The Hanafi view restricts it to the tashahhud alone.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered mufta bihi based on the apparent brevity indicated by the hadith and the principle of following the Prophet's practice closely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۵ ولا يَزِيدُ عَلَى هَذَا فِي الْقَعْدَةِ الأُولَى ٣٥وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَزِيدُ عَلَى هَذَا فِي الْقَعْدَةِ الْأُولَى \ عَنْ أَبِي عُبَيْدَةَ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: «كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ، كَأَنَّهُ عَلَى الرَّضْفِ» قُلْتُ: حَتَّى يَقُومَ قَالَ: ذَلِكَ يُرِيدُ، سنن نسائي، بَابُ التَّخْفِيفِ فِي التَّشَهُدِ الْأَوَّلِ ،نمبر1176/،(سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي تَخْفِيفِ الْقُعُودِ نمبر 995)
35. And he does not add anything to this in the first sitting. Evidence (1): The hadith establishing 'he does not add anything in the first sitting' from Abu Ubaydah ibn Abdullah ibn Mas'ud from his father, who said: 'The Messenger of Allah, during the two rak'ahs, was as if [sitting] on hot stones.' I asked: 'Until he stands?' He said: 'That is what he intended.' Sunan Nasa'i, chapter on lightening the first tashahhud, no. 1176; Sunan Abu Dawud, chapter on lightening the sitting, no. 995.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This lesson presents the ruling that in the first sitting (after the first two rak'ahs), one should not add anything beyond the tashahhud. The proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud describing that the Prophet would sit briefly in the first sitting, as if on hot stones, indicating he did not prolong it and did not add extra supplications. The hadith shows that the first sitting is meant to be light, restricting it to just the tashahhud. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
القعدة الأولى (al-qa'dah al-ula): The sitting after the first two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (sitting like on hot stones) indicate about the first sitting?
A) The Prophet would prolong the sitting
B) The first sitting should be brief and contain only tashahhud
C) The Prophet would recite additional supplications
D) The first sitting is optional

Key Takeaway
In the first sitting of salah, the Hanafi school restricts recitation to the tashahhud only, based on the Prophet's practice of brevity.

Sending Salutations upon the Prophet in the Final Sitting
Ruling to send salutations upon the Prophet in the final sitting with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending salutations upon the Prophet in prayer and identify the Quranic and hadith evidence for this ruling.

Core Idea
In the final sitting, salutations upon the Prophet are a sunnah confirmed by Quran and hadith.

This lesson examines the ruling on reciting salutations (durood) upon the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) during the prayer. While many Muslims know the importance of sending blessings, the exact position and legal weight differ among schools. Here we focus on the Hanafi view, which places this act in the final sitting after tashahhud, and we explore the primary textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
First, note that the passage explicitly states that the worshipper sends salutations upon the Prophet in prayer. Determine the legal classification of this act within the Hanafi school.
The ruling is sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the Primary Proof (Quran)
The passage cites Surah al-Ahzab, verse 56. Read the verse carefully and understand its apparent command.
The imperative 'sallu' (send blessings) is the key operative word.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah (Indicative Aspect)
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a qarinah (context) showing recommendation. Here, the school interprets the command as sunnah due to other evidences, such as the Prophet's practice.
The dalala (clarity of meaning) is zanni (speculative), not qat'i.
4
Examine the Hadith Evidence
The passage also references a hadith from Ka'b ibn Ujrah. The text is partially preserved, but the key is that it provides a second proof for sending salutations.
The hadith strengthens the evidence but still supports sunnah, not obligation.
5
Understand the Hanafi Position in Context
The final part in Urdu clarifies the Hanafi practice: only tashahhud in the first sitting, and salutations (durood) plus any transmitted supplication in the final sitting. This is the mufta bihi view.
Some other schools require salutations in the first sitting as well, leading to a valid ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۷ وَيُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ٣٧وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الوَإِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلَائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيُّ يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ وَسَلِّمُوا تَسْلِيمًا﴾ سورة الاحزاب
، أيت 56) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَا سَمِعْتُ ابن أبي ليلى. فقال : لَقِيَنِي كَعْبُ بْنُ عُجْرَةَ فَقَالَ : أَلَا أُهْدِي لَكَ هَدِيَّةً؟ خَرَجَ عَلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقُلْنَا: قَدْ عَرَفْنَا اصول: احناف کے یہاں قعدہ اولی میں صرف التحیات پڑھے اور قعدہ اخیرہ میں درود اور کوئی ماثورہ دعا بھی۔
37. And he sends salutations upon the Prophet. Evidence (1): The verse for establishing 'He sends salutations upon the Prophet': 'Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet. O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with peace.' [Surah al-Ahzab, verse 56]. Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing 'He sends salutations upon the Prophet': I heard Ibn Abi Layla say: Ka'b ibn Ujrah met me and said: Shall I gift you? The Messenger of Allah came out to us and we said: We have known... Principle: According to the Hanafis, in the first sitting only the tashahhud is recited, and in the final sitting, salutations and any transmitted supplication are also recited.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This lesson presents the ruling that one must send salutations (durood) upon the Prophet in the final sitting of prayer. The proof is first from the Quran (Surah al-Ahzab, 56), which commands believers to send blessings upon the Prophet. The imperative 'sallu' indicates obligation or recommendation; the Hanafis consider it wajib in prayer? Actually the text does not specify the level, but it is generally considered sunnah or wajib. The second proof is a hadith from Ka'b ibn Ujrah, though the text is cut off. The Urdu principle at the end clarifies the Hanafi position: in the first sitting only tashahhud, and in the final sitting, durood and any transmitted supplication. This is the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat 'ala al-nabi): Sending blessings and salutations upon the Prophet Muhammad, e.g., 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Surah al-Ikhlas
D) Surah al-Baqarah, verse 255

Key Takeaway
Sending salutations upon the Prophet in the final sitting of prayer is sunnah in the Hanafi school, supported by Quran and hadith.

Ruling on Qunut in Witr Prayer
States ruling on qunut in Witr with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qunut in Witr, identify its textual proofs, and distinguish its timing from other madhahib.

Core Idea
Qunut in Witr is sunnah muakkadah before ruku' in the third rak'ah all year.

This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's matn establishes the Hanafi position on qunut in Witr prayer. It presents a clear ruling along with multiple proofs from the sunnah and the actions of the Companions. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly performing Witr and avoiding confusion with other schools that place qunut in Fajr or restrict it to Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening statement: 'وَيَقْرَأُ فِي كُلّ رَكْعَةٍ مِنْ الْوِتْرِ فَاتِحَةَ الْكِتَابِ وَسُورَةً فَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَقْنُتَ كَبَّرَ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ ثُمَّ يَقْنتُ'. This tells you the basic acts: reciting Fatiha and a surah, then takbir, raising hands, and qunut.
2
Locate the specific timing
The author then explicitly states: 'وَيَقْنُتُ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ قَبْلَ الرَّكُوعِ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ'. This fixes the timing: third rak'ah, before ruku', throughout the entire year.
Contrast with other schools: Shafi'is do qunut after ruku' in Fajr; Malikis do it after ruku' in Witr only in Ramadan.
3
Examine the proofs
The passage cites multiple evidences: hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b describing the Prophet's Witr practice, narrations from Ibn Mas'ud showing his takbir and hand-raising, and a hadith that the Prophet abandoned qunut in other prayers.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but their meaning (dalala) is clear.
4
Understand the restriction
The author adds: 'وَلَا يَقْنُتُ فِي صَلَاةٍ غَيْرِهَا'. Qunut is exclusive to Witr; it is not performed in Fajr or any other prayer. This is a key point of divergence from the Shafi'i school.
Evidence: hadith of Anas that the Prophet recited qunut for a month then left it, indicating it was not a permanent sunnah in other prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةُ الْوِتْرِ وَيَقْرَأُ فِي كُلّ رَكْعَةٍ مِنْ الْوِتْرِ فَاتِحَةَ الْكِتَابِ وَسُورَةً فَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَقْنُتَ كَبَّرَ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ ثُمَّ يَقْنتُ ووَلَا يَقْنُتُ فِي صَلَاةٍ غَيْرِهَا وجه: (ا)الحديث لثبوت وَيَقْنُتُ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ قَبْلَ الرَّكُوعِ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ \ عَنْ عَلِقٍ، قَالَ: " كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُوتِرُ بِثَلَاثٍ يَقْرَأُ فِيهِنَّ بِتِسْعِ سُوَرٍ مِنَ الْمُفَصَّلِ، يَقْرَأُ فِي كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ بِثَلَاثِ سُوَرٍ آخِرُهُنَّ : قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الوِتْرِ بِثَلَاثٍ، نمبر 460) وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَيَقْنُتُ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ قَبْلَ الرَّكُوعِ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ \ عَنْ أُتِيَ بْنِ كَعْبٍ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم «كَانَ يُوتِرُ بِثَلَاثِ رَكَعَاتٍ كَانَ يَقْرَأُ فِي الْأُولَى بِ سَبِّحِ اسْمَ رَبِّكَ الْأَعْلَى ، وَفِي الثَّانِيَةِ بِ {قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الْكَافِرُونَ، وَفِي الثَّالِثَةِ بِ {قُلْ هُوَ اللهُ أَحَدٌ، وَيَقْنُتُ قَبْلَ الرَّكُوعِ، فَإِذَا فَرَغَ قَالَ عِنْدَ فَرَاغِهِ: سُبْحَانَ الْمَلِكِ الْقُدُّوسِ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ يُطِيلُ فِي آخِرِهِنَّ، (سنن نسائي، ذِكْرُ اخْتِلَافِ أَلْفَاظِ النَّاقِلِينَ لِخَبَرِ أُيَ بْنِ كَعْبٍ فِي الْوِتْرِ ، نمبر 1699/المستدرك للحاكم، كِتَابُ الْوِتْرِ، وَأَمَّا حَدِيثُ بَكْرِ بْنِ وَائِلِ نمبر 1139/سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ مَا يُقْرَأُ فِي الوِتْرِ،نمبر 463/سنن ابوداود بَابُ مَا يَقْرَأُ فِي الْوِتْرِ ، نمبر 1423) وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَقْنُتُ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ قَبْلَ الرَّكُوعِ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ \ أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ مَسْعُودٍ، «كَانَ إِذَا فَرَغَ مِنَ الْقِرَاءَةِ كَبَّرَ ثُمَّ قَنَتَ، فَإِذَا فَرَغَ مِنَ الْقُنُوتِ، كَبَّرَ ثُمَّ رَكَعَ،،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في التَّكْبِيرِ لِلْقُنُوتِ نمبر 6948) وجه: (١)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَقْنُتُ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ قَبْلَ الرَّكُوعِ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، «أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ فِي قُنُوتِ الْوَتْرِ ، مصنف ابن شيبه فِي رَفْعِ الْيَدَيْنِ فِي قُنُوتِ الْوَتْرِ، غبر 6954) وجه (۳) عمل الصحابي لثبوت وَيَقْنُتُ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ قَبْلَ الرَّكُوعِ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ الْأَسْوَدِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: "كَانَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ فِي الْقُنُوتِ إِلَى ثَدْيَيْهِ،(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ رَفْعِ الْيَدَيْنِ فِي الْقُنُوتِ نمبر 4867) د وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْنُتُ فِي صَلَاةٍ غَيْرِهَا أَعَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَنَتَ شَهْرًا، ثُمَّ تَرَكَهُ، سنن ابوداود بَابُ الْقُنُوتِ فِي الصَّلَوَاتِ ، نمبر 1445) لغات : يَقْنُتَ : قنوت پڑھنا، مراد دعاء قنوت ہے، گبر : تکبیر یعنی اللہ اکبر کہنا، رفع : اٹھانا، مر اور فع یدین کرنا۔
Chapter of Witr prayer. He recites in every rak'ah of Witr al-Fatiha and a surah. When he wants to recite qunut, he says takbir and raises his hands, then recites qunut. And he does not recite qunut in any other prayer. Evidence: (1) The hadith establishing that he recites qunut in the third [rak'ah] before ruku' throughout the year: from 'Aliq? who said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) would pray Witr with three [rak'ahs], reciting in them nine surahs from al-Mufassal, reciting in each rak'ah three surahs, the last of them being Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' (Sunan Tirmidhi). Evidence: (1) The hadith establishing that he recites qunut in the third before ruku' throughout the year: from Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to pray Witr with three rak'ahs: he recited in the first 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la', in the second 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun', and in the third 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad', and he would recite qunut before ruku', and when he finished he said upon finishing: 'Subhan al-Malik al-Quddus' three times, lengthening the last one (Sunan Nasa'i, etc.). Evidence (1) Saying of a companion establishing that he recites qunut in the third before ruku' throughout the year: that Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, when he finished recitation, said takbir then recited qunut, and when he finished qunut, said takbir then bowed (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). Evidence (2) Saying of a companion establishing that he recites qunut in the third before ruku' throughout the year: from Abdullah that he used to raise his hands in qunut of Witr (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). Evidence (3) Action of a companion establishing that he recites qunut in the third before ruku' throughout the year: from Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad from his father who said: 'Ibn Mas'ud would raise his hands in qunut up to his chest' (Sunan Bayhaqi). And evidence (1) The hadith establishing that he does not recite qunut in any other prayer: from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited qunut for a month, then abandoned it (Sunan Abi Dawud). Glossary: yaqnutu: reciting qunut, meaning du'a al-qunut; kabbar: say takbir meaning Allahu Akbar; rafa': raise, meaning raising the hands.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section from the commentary on al-Quduri's matn. The author states the core Hanafi ruling regarding qunut in Witr: one recites Fatiha and a surah in each rak'ah, and when intending qunut, one says the takbir for qunut, raises the hands, and then recites the qunut supplication. Crucially, qunut is restricted to Witr and is not performed in any other prayer, including Fajr. The author then provides multiple evidences: (1) a hadith from 'Ali (or perhaps 'Alqama) about the Prophet reciting specific surahs in Witr; (2) a well-known hadith from Ubayy ibn Ka'b describing the Prophet's Witr practice, including qunut before ruku' and the tasbih after; (3) narrations from Ibn Mas'ud showing his practice of takbir before and after qunut and raising hands; and (4) a hadith from Anas that the Prophet qunut for a month and then left it, indicating that qunut in other prayers is not a permanent sunnah. The glossary explains key terms for non-Arabic readers. This passage establishes that qunut in Witr is a confirmed sunnah, and it is to be done before ruku' in the last rak'ah throughout the year, not only in Ramadan.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A specific supplication recited in Witr prayer after the Quranic recitation and before ruku' in the last rak'ah.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the ears or chest while saying takbir for qunut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is qunut recited in Witr prayer?
A) After ruku' in the second rak'ah
B) Before ruku' in the third rak'ah
C) After ruku' in the third rak'ah
D) Before ruku' in the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Qunut in Witr is a confirmed sunnah performed before ruku' in the third rak'ah all year round.

No Specific Surah Required and the Minimum Recitation in Prayer
States that no specific surah is required and discusses the internal Hanafi dispute on minimum recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the minimum recitation after al-Fatiha and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
No specific surah required; minimum recitation disputed: any recitation suffices (Imam) vs. three short verses (Sahibayn).

This lesson addresses a fundamental aspect of salah: the recitation after al-Fatiha. While no specific surah is mandated, the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on the minimum amount that fulfills the wajib obligation. Abu Hanifa takes a lenient view, while his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani require a more substantial recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Recognize that the text first states that no specific surah is required in any prayer, and that it is makruh to always recite the same surah exclusively.
This applies to all prayers, fard and nafl.
2
Recognize the disputed issue
The second part discusses the minimum recitation that suffices. Understand that this is about the wajib recitation after al-Fatiha in witr and sunnah prayers.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students.
3
State Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa holds that any amount linguistically called 'recitation' suffices, even a single short verse or part of a verse.
His basis is the literal meaning of the command 'recite'.
4
State the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require at least three short verses or one long verse equivalent in length.
They argue for a meaningful recitation, citing the Prophet's (ﷺ) practice.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn, though Abu Hanifa's view is also considered valid.
Later authorities like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah prefer the Sahibayn's view for caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةُ الْوِتْرِ ل وَلَيْسَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنْ الصَّلَوَاتِ قِرَاءَةُ سُورَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا لَا يُجْزِئُ غَيْرُهَا ك وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَتَّخِذ سُورَةَ لِلصَّلَاةِ بِعَيْنِهَا لَا يَقْرَأُ غَيْرَهَا وَأَدْنَ مَا يُجْزِئُ مِنْ الْقِرَاءَةِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ مَا يَتَنَاوَلُهُ اسْمُ الْقِرَاءَةِ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لا يُجْزِئُ أَقَلُّ مِنْ ثَلَاثِ آيَاتٍ قِصَارٍ أَوْ آيَةٍ طَوِيلَةٍ
Chapter of Witr prayer. And in no prayer is there a requirement for a specific surah such that other than it suffices. And it is disliked to adopt a specific surah for a prayer such that one does not recite other than it. And the minimum that suffices of recitation in prayer is what the name 'recitation' applies to according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Less than three short verses or one long verse does not suffice.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This is a ruling statement combined with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author first establishes a general principle: no prayer requires a particular surah after al-Fatiha; one may recite any Quranic passage, and it is makruh to always recite the same surah exclusively. The second part deals with the minimum amount of Quranic recitation that fulfills the wajib obligation of qira'ah in prayer (after Fatiha). Abu Hanifa holds that any amount that is linguistically considered 'recitation' suffices, even a single short verse or part of a verse. His two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that at least three short verses or one long verse (equivalent to three short verses) is required. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn, i.e., three short verses or one long verse, to ensure a meaningful recitation. However, some later Hanafi jurists prefer Abu Hanifa's view. The term 'long verse' refers to a verse of at least three short verses in length, like Ayat al-Kursi.

Key Terms
أدنى ما يجزئ من القراءة (adna ma yujzi' min al-qira'ah): The minimum amount of Quranic recitation that fulfills the obligation of recitation in prayer after al-Fatiha.
سورة بعينها (surah bi 'aynihi): A specific surah designated for a particular prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the minimum recitation after al-Fatiha in prayer?
A) Any amount that is called recitation
B) At least three short verses or one long verse
C) At least one complete surah
D) At least one verse

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position for the minimum recitation after al-Fatiha is at least three short verses or one long verse, though Abu Hanifa allowed any amount.

The Follower's Recitation Behind the Imam: Prohibition and Primary Proofs
Ruling statement followed by Quranic and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's recitation behind the imam in audible prayers and explain the primary evidence from the Quran and the hadith of 'be silent'.

Core Idea
When the imam recites aloud, the follower must be silent – recitation by the follower is prohibited.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that a follower (mu'tam) does not recite behind the imam in prayers where the imam recites aloud. The author of al-Quduri presents a clear ruling followed by a series of proofs from divine revelation and prophetic practice. We focus on the key evidence that anchors the school's stance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The text opens with the direct ruling: 'The follower does not recite behind the imam.' Recognize that this applies to audible prayers (jahr) and that the follower is expected to remain silent and listen.
The ruling is stated as a general principle, but later proofs specify it applies when the imam recites aloud.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse 'When the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent' (7:204) is cited. Understand how the Hanafi school interprets the command to be silent as a prohibition of the follower's recitation during the imam's recitation.
The verse is general, but the school applies it specifically to the prayer context based on other evidence.
3
Analyze the primary hadith proof
The hadith 'The imam is only appointed to be followed… when he recites, be silent' clearly commands silence. Focus on the imperative 'ansitu' (be silent) and its implication of prohibition (tahrim).
This hadith is the central proof; it directly addresses the follower's action during the imam's recitation.
4
Analyze the proof from practice
The Prophet's objection to someone reciting behind him ('I knew that some of you contended with me') shows that recitation behind the imam is displeasing and therefore prohibited. Additionally, the principle 'the imam's recitation is his recitation' (from another hadith) reinforces that the follower relies on the imam.
The combination of explicit command and practical disapproval solidifies the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْقِرَاءَةُ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ
وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ
الْقِرَاءَةُ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ
لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ ﴿وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْءَانُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ و وَأَنصِتُوا لَعَلَّكُمْ تُرْحَمُونَ) (سورة الاعراف 7، أيت 203)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ " إِنَّمَا جُعِلَ الْإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ، فَإِذَا كَبَّرَ فَكَبَرُوا، وَإِذَا قَرَأَ فَأَنْصِتُوا وَإِذَا قَالَ: {غَيْرِ الْمَغْضُوبِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا الضَّالِّينَ} [الفاتحة: 7] ، فَقُولُوا آمِينَ، وَإِذَا رَكَعَ فَارْكَعُوا، وَإِذَا قَالَ: سَمِعَ اللَّهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ، فَقُولُوا: اللَّهُمَّ رَبَّنَا وَلَكَ الْحَمْدُ، وَإِذَا سَجَدَ فَاسْجُدُوا، وَإِذَا صَلَّى جَالِسًا، فَصَلُّوا جُلُوسًا أَجْمَعِينَ (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ إِذَا قَرَأَ الْإِمَامُ فَأَنْصِتُوا، نمبر 846)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ، قَالَ صَلَّى بِنَا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة الظُّهْرِ (أَوِ الْعَصْرِ) فَقَالَ أَيُّكُمْ قَرَأَ خَلْفِي بسبح اسم ربك الأعلى؟ " فقال رَجُلٌ: أَنَا . وَلَمْ أُرِدْ بِمَا إِلَّا الْخَيْرَ. قال قد علمت أن بعضكم خالجنيها،(مسلم شريف،باب نهي المأموم عن جهده بِالْقِرَاءَةِ خَلْفَ إِمَامِهِ، نمبر 398)
وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ قَالَ: «إِنِّي أَقُولُ مَالِي أُنَازَعُ الْقُرْآنَ؟»، قَالَ: فَانْتَهَى النَّاسُ عَنِ الْقِرَاءَةِ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِيمَا جَهَرَ فِيهِ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالْقِرَاءَةِ مِنَ الصَّلَوَاتِ حِينَ سَمِعُوا ذَلِكَ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ( سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ كَرِهَ الْقِرَاءَةَ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ إِذَا جَهَرَ الْإِمَامُ، نمبر، 826، سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تَرْكِ القِرَاءَةِ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ إِذَا جَهَرَ الْإِمَامُ بِالقِرَاءَةِ،312\سنن دارقطني، بَابُ وُجُوبِ قِرَاءَةِ أُمّ الْكِتَابِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَخَلَفَ الْإِمَامِ، 1222) وجه (۵) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، عَنْ أَبِي الزُّبَيْرِ، عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ، فَقِرَاءَةُ الْإِمَامِ لَهُ قِرَاءَةٌ، (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ إِذَا قَرَأَ الْإِمَامُ فَأَنْصِتُوا ، نمبر 1850 سنن دارقطني ، بَابُ وُجُوبِ قِرَاءَةِ أُمِّ الْكِتَابِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَخَلَفَ الإمام، برقم (1220) اصول: حنفیہ کی نزدیک نماز میں امام کے پیچھے قرائت نہیں ہے کیونکہ امام کی قرائت مقتدی کی قرائت ہے۔

الْقِرَاءَةُ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ
ل وَمَنْ أَرَادَ الدُّخُولَ فِي صَلَاةِ غَيْرِهِ احْتَاجَ إِلَى نِيَّتَيْنِ نِيَّةِ الصَّلَاةِ وَنِيَّةِ الْمُتَابَعَةِ وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ \ عَنْ أَبي الدَّرْدَاءِ، سَمِعَهُ يَقُولُ: «سُئِلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَفِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ قِرَاءَةُ؟ قَالَ: نَعَمْ. قَالَ رَجُلٌ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ: وَجَبَتْ هَذِهِ، فَالْتَفَتَ إلَيَّ، وَكُنتُ أَقْرَبَ الْقَوْمِ مِنْهُ فَقَالَ: مَا أَرَى الْإِمَامَ إِذَا أَمَّ الْقَوْمَ، إِلَّا قَدْ كَفَاهُمْ(سنن نسائي، اكْتِفَاءُ الْمَأْمُومِ بِقِرَاءَةِ الْإِمَامِ ، برقم 1823 سنن دارقطني، بَابُ ذِكْرِ قَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ فَقِرَاءَةُ الْإِمَامِ لَهُ قِرَاءَةٌ وَاخْتِلَافِ الرّوَايَاتِ، برقم (1248)
وجه : (۷) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَم خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ \ قَالَ: وَكَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ لَا يَقْرَأُ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ (موطاء امام مالك تَرْكُ الْقِرَاءَةِ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ فِيمَا جَهَرَ فِيهِ، غبر 284) وجه (۸) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ \ عَنْ عُبَادَةَ بْنِ الصَّامِتِ : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَا صَلَاةَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَقْرَأْ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ (صحيح البخاري،بَابُ وُجُوبِ الْقِرَاءَةِ لِلْإِمَام وَالْمَأْمُوم في الصَّلَوَاتِ كَلِهَا فِي الحَضَرِ وَالسَّفَرِ ، نمبر 756 مسلم شریف ، باب وُجُوبِ قِرَاءَةِ الْفَاتِحَةِ فِي كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ، وَإِنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ يُحْسِنُ الْفَاتِحَةَ وَلَا أَمْكَنَهُ تَعَلَّمَهَا قَرَأَ مَا تَيَسَّرَ لَهُ مِنْ غَيْرها ، رقم 1756 سنن ابوداود بَابُ مَنْ تَرَكَ الْقِرَاءَةَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ ، برقم (823). وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ عَنْ أَبي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ : الإِمَامُ ضَامِنٌ، وَالْمُؤَذِّنُ مُؤْتَن، اللَّهُمَّ أَرْشِدِ الأَئِمَّةَ ، وَاغْفِرْ لِلْمُؤَذِّنِينَ (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الإِمَامَ ضَامِنٌ، وَالمُؤَذَنَ مُؤْتَمَن غبر (207) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ \ عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ إِنَّمَا الإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَ بِهِ. فَلَا تَخْتَلِفُوا عَلَيْهِ ، مسلم شريف ، بَاب انْتِمَامِ الْمَأْمُومِ بالإمام، نمبر 414)
اصول امام مقتدی کی نماز کا ضامن ہے اسلئے مقتدی کو اقتدا کی نیت لازمی کرنی ہوگی۔ اصول : امام کے ساتھ نماز میں شامل ہونے کے لئے دو طرح کی نیت کرنی ہے ، اول نماز کی ، دوم امام کی اقتدا کی۔
Recitation behind the Imam. The follower does not recite behind the imam. Recitation behind the Imam. Proof 1: The verse for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: {And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent that you may receive mercy} (Surah al-A'raf, verse 203). Proof 2: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Abu Huraira, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed. So when he makes takbir, make takbir. When he recites, be silent. When he says {Not those who have incurred wrath, nor those who have gone astray}, say Ameen. When he bows, bow. When he says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', say 'Allahumma Rabbana wa lakal hamd'. When he prostrates, prostrate. And if he prays sitting, then pray sitting all together.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter: When the Imam recites, be silent, no. 846). Proof 3: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Imran ibn Husayn, he said: The Messenger of Allah led us in Zuhr (or Asr) prayer, then said: 'Who among you recited behind me 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la'?' A man said: 'I did, and I intended nothing but good.' He said: 'I knew that some of you contended with me.' (Muslim, chapter: Prohibition of the follower reciting loudly behind his imam, no. 398). Proof 4: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: The Prophet said: 'What is the matter with me? I am being contended with in the Quran?' He said: So the people refrained from reciting with the Messenger of Allah in those prayers in which he recited aloud when they heard that from the Messenger of Allah. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter: Whoever disliked reciting al-Fatiha when the imam recites aloud, no. 826, Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Sunan al-Daraqutni). Proof 5: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Jabir from Abu al-Zubayr from Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is his recitation.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter: When the imam recites, be silent, no. 1850; Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 1220). Principle: According to the Hanafis, there is no recitation behind the imam because the imam's recitation is the follower's recitation. Recitation behind the imam. And whoever wishes to enter into the prayer of another needs two intentions: the intention of the prayer and the intention of following (the imam). Proof 6: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Abu al-Darda', he heard him say: The Messenger of Allah was asked: Is there recitation in every prayer? He said: 'Yes.' A man from the Ansar said: 'This has become obligatory.' He turned to me, and I was the closest of the people to him, and said: 'I do not think that the imam, when he leads the people, does not suffice them.' (Sunan al-Nasa'i, chapter: The follower's sufficiency by the imam's recitation, no. 1823; Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 1248). Proof 7: The saying of a companion for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: It is reported that Abdullah ibn Umar did not recite behind the imam. (Muwatta Imam Malik, chapter: Abandoning recitation behind the imam in what is recited aloud, no. 284). Proof 8: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no prayer for the one who does not recite al-Fatiha.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter: The obligation of recitation for the imam and the follower in all prayers at home and on travel, no. 756; Muslim, no. 1756; Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 823). Proof 9: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Abu Huraira, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is entrusted. O Allah, guide the imams and forgive the mu'adhdhins.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter: What has come that the imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is entrusted, no. 207). Proof 10: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is only to be followed, so do not differ with him.' (Muslim, chapter: The follower's following of the imam, no. 414). Principle: The imam is the guarantor of the follower's prayer, therefore the follower must necessarily have the intention of following. Principle: To join in prayer with the imam, one must make two intentions: first the intention of the prayer, second the intention of following the imam.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a collection of proofs (wujuh) from the author of al-Quduri's commentary, presenting the Hanafi ruling that a follower (mu'tam) does not recite behind the imam during prayers in which the imam recites aloud. The ruling is stated clearly: 'The follower does not recite behind the imam.' The author then provides ten proofs: one from the Quran (the verse of silence, 7:204), seven from hadith, one from a companion's practice (Ibn Umar), and one additional hadith. The key hadith is 'The imam is only appointed to be followed, so when he recites, be silent,' which directly commands silence. Another hadith states that the imam's recitation is sufficient for the follower: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is his recitation.' The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn shows that the Prophet objected to someone reciting behind him, establishing prohibition. The principle of the imam being a guarantor (damin) reinforces that the follower relies on the imam. The passage ends with an important usul al-fiqh principle: one who wishes to join the imam's prayer must have two intentions—the intention of the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr) and the intention of following the imam (niyyat al-mutaba'ah). This is derived from the imam's role as guarantor; the follower must consciously submit to the imam's leadership.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The person who prays behind an imam, following him in prayer.
الإمام (al-imam): The person who leads the congregational prayer, whose actions are to be followed by the mu'tam.
نية المتابعة (niyyat al-mutaba'ah): The intention of following the imam, a necessary condition for the validity of following in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi proofs presented, what is the ruling on the follower reciting behind the imam in an audible prayer?
A) Mandatory (wajib)
B) Permissible (mubah)
C) Prohibited (makruh tahrimi)
D) Recommended (mustahab)

Key Takeaway
The follower must be silent when the imam recites aloud; the imam's recitation suffices for the follower.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
Supporting Proofs and the Intention of Following the Imam
Additional hadith proofs and the usul principle of dual intention for the follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the additional hadith proofs that reinforce the follower's silence and state the requirement of niyyat al-mutaba'ah for joining the imam.

Core Idea
The imam is a guarantor for the follower's prayer; the follower must intend to follow the imam along with the prayer itself.

This lesson continues the discussion on the follower's recitation behind the imam by presenting additional prophetic proofs and a key usul principle. The texts establish that the imam suffices for the follower and that the follower must have a dual intention: for the prayer and for following the imam. These elements underpin the Hanafi practice in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Examine the proof from Abu al-Darda'
The hadith 'I do not think that the imam does not suffice them' indicates that the imam's recitation is sufficient for the congregation. This supports the ruling that the follower need not recite.
This hadith is narrated with the understanding that the imam's recitation covers all.
2
Analyze the companion practice
The text mentions that Abdullah ibn Umar did not recite behind the imam. This shows the practice of a knowledgeable companion, which the Hanafi school considers a strong proof (qawl sahabi).
Ibn Umar's action is cited as a corroborating evidence.
3
Understand the principle of the imam as guarantor
The hadith 'The imam is a guarantor (damin)' implies that the imam's prayer covers the follower's prayer, so the follower does not need to recite. This also leads to the requirement of intending to follow the imam.
The concept of damin is unique to the Hanafi understanding of congregational prayer.
4
Derive the dual intention requirement
The passage states that one who enters the imam's prayer needs two intentions: intention of the prayer (e.g., Zuhr) and intention of following the imam (niyyat al-mutaba'ah). This is a necessary condition for the follower's prayer to be valid behind the imam.
The niyyat al-mutaba'ah distinguishes a follower from a solo worshipper and aligns the follower's actions with the imam.

الْقِرَاءَةُ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ
وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ
الْقِرَاءَةُ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ
لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ ﴿وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْءَانُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ و وَأَنصِتُوا لَعَلَّكُمْ تُرْحَمُونَ) (سورة الاعراف 7، أيت 203)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ " إِنَّمَا جُعِلَ الْإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ، فَإِذَا كَبَّرَ فَكَبَرُوا، وَإِذَا قَرَأَ فَأَنْصِتُوا وَإِذَا قَالَ: {غَيْرِ الْمَغْضُوبِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا الضَّالِّينَ} [الفاتحة: 7] ، فَقُولُوا آمِينَ، وَإِذَا رَكَعَ فَارْكَعُوا، وَإِذَا قَالَ: سَمِعَ اللَّهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ، فَقُولُوا: اللَّهُمَّ رَبَّنَا وَلَكَ الْحَمْدُ، وَإِذَا سَجَدَ فَاسْجُدُوا، وَإِذَا صَلَّى جَالِسًا، فَصَلُّوا جُلُوسًا أَجْمَعِينَ (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ إِذَا قَرَأَ الْإِمَامُ فَأَنْصِتُوا، نمبر 846)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ، قَالَ صَلَّى بِنَا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة الظُّهْرِ (أَوِ الْعَصْرِ) فَقَالَ أَيُّكُمْ قَرَأَ خَلْفِي بسبح اسم ربك الأعلى؟ " فقال رَجُلٌ: أَنَا . وَلَمْ أُرِدْ بِمَا إِلَّا الْخَيْرَ. قال قد علمت أن بعضكم خالجنيها،(مسلم شريف،باب نهي المأموم عن جهده بِالْقِرَاءَةِ خَلْفَ إِمَامِهِ، نمبر 398)
وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ قَالَ: «إِنِّي أَقُولُ مَالِي أُنَازَعُ الْقُرْآنَ؟»، قَالَ: فَانْتَهَى النَّاسُ عَنِ الْقِرَاءَةِ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِيمَا جَهَرَ فِيهِ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالْقِرَاءَةِ مِنَ الصَّلَوَاتِ حِينَ سَمِعُوا ذَلِكَ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ( سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ كَرِهَ الْقِرَاءَةَ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ إِذَا جَهَرَ الْإِمَامُ، نمبر، 826، سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تَرْكِ القِرَاءَةِ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ إِذَا جَهَرَ الْإِمَامُ بِالقِرَاءَةِ،312\سنن دارقطني، بَابُ وُجُوبِ قِرَاءَةِ أُمّ الْكِتَابِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَخَلَفَ الْإِمَامِ، 1222) وجه (۵) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، عَنْ أَبِي الزُّبَيْرِ، عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ، فَقِرَاءَةُ الْإِمَامِ لَهُ قِرَاءَةٌ، (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ إِذَا قَرَأَ الْإِمَامُ فَأَنْصِتُوا ، نمبر 1850 سنن دارقطني ، بَابُ وُجُوبِ قِرَاءَةِ أُمِّ الْكِتَابِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَخَلَفَ الإمام، برقم (1220) اصول: حنفیہ کی نزدیک نماز میں امام کے پیچھے قرائت نہیں ہے کیونکہ امام کی قرائت مقتدی کی قرائت ہے۔

الْقِرَاءَةُ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ
ل وَمَنْ أَرَادَ الدُّخُولَ فِي صَلَاةِ غَيْرِهِ احْتَاجَ إِلَى نِيَّتَيْنِ نِيَّةِ الصَّلَاةِ وَنِيَّةِ الْمُتَابَعَةِ وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ \ عَنْ أَبي الدَّرْدَاءِ، سَمِعَهُ يَقُولُ: «سُئِلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَفِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ قِرَاءَةُ؟ قَالَ: نَعَمْ. قَالَ رَجُلٌ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ: وَجَبَتْ هَذِهِ، فَالْتَفَتَ إلَيَّ، وَكُنتُ أَقْرَبَ الْقَوْمِ مِنْهُ فَقَالَ: مَا أَرَى الْإِمَامَ إِذَا أَمَّ الْقَوْمَ، إِلَّا قَدْ كَفَاهُمْ(سنن نسائي، اكْتِفَاءُ الْمَأْمُومِ بِقِرَاءَةِ الْإِمَامِ ، برقم 1823 سنن دارقطني، بَابُ ذِكْرِ قَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ فَقِرَاءَةُ الْإِمَامِ لَهُ قِرَاءَةٌ وَاخْتِلَافِ الرّوَايَاتِ، برقم (1248)
وجه : (۷) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَم خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ \ قَالَ: وَكَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ لَا يَقْرَأُ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ (موطاء امام مالك تَرْكُ الْقِرَاءَةِ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ فِيمَا جَهَرَ فِيهِ، غبر 284) وجه (۸) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ \ عَنْ عُبَادَةَ بْنِ الصَّامِتِ : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَا صَلَاةَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَقْرَأْ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ (صحيح البخاري،بَابُ وُجُوبِ الْقِرَاءَةِ لِلْإِمَام وَالْمَأْمُوم في الصَّلَوَاتِ كَلِهَا فِي الحَضَرِ وَالسَّفَرِ ، نمبر 756 مسلم شریف ، باب وُجُوبِ قِرَاءَةِ الْفَاتِحَةِ فِي كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ، وَإِنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ يُحْسِنُ الْفَاتِحَةَ وَلَا أَمْكَنَهُ تَعَلَّمَهَا قَرَأَ مَا تَيَسَّرَ لَهُ مِنْ غَيْرها ، رقم 1756 سنن ابوداود بَابُ مَنْ تَرَكَ الْقِرَاءَةَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ ، برقم (823). وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ \ عَنْ أَبي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ : الإِمَامُ ضَامِنٌ، وَالْمُؤَذِّنُ مُؤْتَن، اللَّهُمَّ أَرْشِدِ الأَئِمَّةَ ، وَاغْفِرْ لِلْمُؤَذِّنِينَ (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الإِمَامَ ضَامِنٌ، وَالمُؤَذَنَ مُؤْتَمَن غبر (207) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْرَأُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ \ عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ إِنَّمَا الإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَ بِهِ. فَلَا تَخْتَلِفُوا عَلَيْهِ ، مسلم شريف ، بَاب انْتِمَامِ الْمَأْمُومِ بالإمام، نمبر 414)
اصول امام مقتدی کی نماز کا ضامن ہے اسلئے مقتدی کو اقتدا کی نیت لازمی کرنی ہوگی۔ اصول : امام کے ساتھ نماز میں شامل ہونے کے لئے دو طرح کی نیت کرنی ہے ، اول نماز کی ، دوم امام کی اقتدا کی۔
Recitation behind the Imam. The follower does not recite behind the imam. Recitation behind the Imam. Proof 1: The verse for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: {And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent that you may receive mercy} (Surah al-A'raf, verse 203). Proof 2: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Abu Huraira, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed. So when he makes takbir, make takbir. When he recites, be silent. When he says {Not those who have incurred wrath, nor those who have gone astray}, say Ameen. When he bows, bow. When he says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', say 'Allahumma Rabbana wa lakal hamd'. When he prostrates, prostrate. And if he prays sitting, then pray sitting all together.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter: When the Imam recites, be silent, no. 846). Proof 3: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Imran ibn Husayn, he said: The Messenger of Allah led us in Zuhr (or Asr) prayer, then said: 'Who among you recited behind me 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la'?' A man said: 'I did, and I intended nothing but good.' He said: 'I knew that some of you contended with me.' (Muslim, chapter: Prohibition of the follower reciting loudly behind his imam, no. 398). Proof 4: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: The Prophet said: 'What is the matter with me? I am being contended with in the Quran?' He said: So the people refrained from reciting with the Messenger of Allah in those prayers in which he recited aloud when they heard that from the Messenger of Allah. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter: Whoever disliked reciting al-Fatiha when the imam recites aloud, no. 826, Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Sunan al-Daraqutni). Proof 5: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Jabir from Abu al-Zubayr from Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is his recitation.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter: When the imam recites, be silent, no. 1850; Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 1220). Principle: According to the Hanafis, there is no recitation behind the imam because the imam's recitation is the follower's recitation. Recitation behind the imam. And whoever wishes to enter into the prayer of another needs two intentions: the intention of the prayer and the intention of following (the imam). Proof 6: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Abu al-Darda', he heard him say: The Messenger of Allah was asked: Is there recitation in every prayer? He said: 'Yes.' A man from the Ansar said: 'This has become obligatory.' He turned to me, and I was the closest of the people to him, and said: 'I do not think that the imam, when he leads the people, does not suffice them.' (Sunan al-Nasa'i, chapter: The follower's sufficiency by the imam's recitation, no. 1823; Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 1248). Proof 7: The saying of a companion for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: It is reported that Abdullah ibn Umar did not recite behind the imam. (Muwatta Imam Malik, chapter: Abandoning recitation behind the imam in what is recited aloud, no. 284). Proof 8: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no prayer for the one who does not recite al-Fatiha.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter: The obligation of recitation for the imam and the follower in all prayers at home and on travel, no. 756; Muslim, no. 1756; Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 823). Proof 9: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Abu Huraira, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is entrusted. O Allah, guide the imams and forgive the mu'adhdhins.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter: What has come that the imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is entrusted, no. 207). Proof 10: The hadith for establishing that the follower does not recite behind the imam: From Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is only to be followed, so do not differ with him.' (Muslim, chapter: The follower's following of the imam, no. 414). Principle: The imam is the guarantor of the follower's prayer, therefore the follower must necessarily have the intention of following. Principle: To join in prayer with the imam, one must make two intentions: first the intention of the prayer, second the intention of following the imam.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a collection of proofs (wujuh) from the author of al-Quduri's commentary, presenting the Hanafi ruling that a follower (mu'tam) does not recite behind the imam during prayers in which the imam recites aloud. The ruling is stated clearly: 'The follower does not recite behind the imam.' The author then provides ten proofs: one from the Quran (the verse of silence, 7:204), seven from hadith, one from a companion's practice (Ibn Umar), and one additional hadith. The key hadith is 'The imam is only appointed to be followed, so when he recites, be silent,' which directly commands silence. Another hadith states that the imam's recitation is sufficient for the follower: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is his recitation.' The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn shows that the Prophet objected to someone reciting behind him, establishing prohibition. The principle of the imam being a guarantor (damin) reinforces that the follower relies on the imam. The passage ends with an important usul al-fiqh principle: one who wishes to join the imam's prayer must have two intentions—the intention of the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr) and the intention of following the imam (niyyat al-mutaba'ah). This is derived from the imam's role as guarantor; the follower must consciously submit to the imam's leadership.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; the imam is responsible for the validity and completeness of the follower's prayer.
نية المتابعة (niyyat al-mutaba'ah): The intention of following the imam, a necessary condition for the validity of following in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principles in this lesson, what is required for a follower's prayer behind an imam to be considered valid?
A) Only the intention of the prayer itself
B) The intention of both the prayer and following the imam
C) Following the imam without any specific intention
D) The intention of following the imam only

Key Takeaway
The follower must intend both the specific prayer and to follow the imam; this dual intention is wajib based on the imam being a guarantor.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Congregational Prayer: Sunnah Mu'akkadah and the Priority of the Imam
Ruling on congregational prayer and imam criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer, identify the criteria for imam selection, and explain the evidence for the sunnah mu'akkadah status.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is emphatically recommended, not obligatory; the most knowledgeable in sunnah leads.

This passage from al-Quduri establishes two key rulings: the legal status of congregational prayer as sunnah mu'akkadah and the order of priority for who should lead. While some schools consider jama'ah obligatory, the Hanafi school holds it to be a strongly recommended practice, supported by evidence from the Prophet's actions. The passage also provides a clear hierarchy for imam selection based on knowledge, recitation, piety, and age.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage first states the ruling on congregational prayer (sunnah mu'akkadah) and then lists the criteria for the imam.
2
Analyze the evidence for sunnah mu'akkadah
The hadith of Abu Hurairah shows the Prophet's intention to punish those who miss congregation, but he did not execute it, indicating strong encouragement rather than obligation. The hadith of Ibn Abbas mentions valid excuses, confirming it is not fard.
The Hanafi position relies on the absence of an absolute command.
3
Examine the criteria for imam
The order is: knowledge of sunnah, best recitation, piety, then age. This is derived from hadith about the Prophet preferring Abu Bakr and the command to let the most knowledgeable lead.
Knowledge of prayer rulings takes precedence over recitation skill.
4
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute
While Hanafis say sunnah mu'akkadah, other schools like the Hanbalis and some Shafi'is consider it fard kifayah or even fard 'ayn. The practical difference is whether praying alone without excuse invalidates the prayer or makes it merely disliked.
The thamarah al-khilaf affects the validity judgment.
5
Apply the criteria to a real situation
Given multiple qualified individuals, one must apply the hierarchy in order. If two are equal in knowledge, move to recitation, then piety, then age.
In case of tie, the next criterion is used.

Source Text

فصل في الجَمَاعَة
الوَ الجَمَاعَةُ سُنَّةٌ مُؤَكَّدَةٌ : وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالْإِمَامَةِ أَعْلَمُهُمْ بِالسُّنَّةِ فَإِنْ تَسَاوَوْا فَأَقْرَؤُهُمْ لِكِتَابِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فَإِنْ تَسَاوَوْا فَأَوْرَعُهُمْ فَإِنْ تَسَاوَوْا فَأَسَتُهُمْ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَالْجَمَاعَةُ سُنَّةٌ مُؤَكَّدَةٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «وَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ، لَقَدْ هَمَمْتُ أَنْ آمُرَ بِعَطَبٍ فَيُحْطَبَ ثُمَّ آمُرَ بِالصَّلَاةِ فَيُؤَذِّنَ لَهَا، ثُمَّ آمُرَ رَجُلًا فَيَؤُمَّ النَّاسَ ثُمَّ أُخَالِفَ إِلَى رِجَالٍ فَأَحَرّقَ عَلَيْهِمْ بُيُوتَهُمْ، وَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ، لَوْ يَعْلَمُ أَحَدُهُمْ: أَنَّهُ يَجِدُ عَرْقًا سَمِينًا ، أَوْ مِرْمَاتَيْنِ حَسَنَتَيْنِ، لَشَهِدَ الْعِشَاءَ ، (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ وُجُوبِ صَلَاةِ الْجَمَاعَةِ، برقم 644\ سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ في التَّشْدِيدِ في تَرْكِ الْجَمَاعَةِ، رقم (548). وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالجَمَاعَةُ سُنَّةٌ مُؤَكَّدَةٌ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ سَمِعَ الْمُنَادِيَ فَلَمْ يَمْنَعْهُ مِنَ اتِبَاعِهِ، عُذْرٌ»، قَالُوا: وَمَا الْعُذْرُ؟، قَالَ: «خَوْفٌ أَوْ مَرَضٌ لَم تُقْبَلْ مِنْهُ الصَّلَاةُ الَّتِي صَلَّى، ( سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي التَّشْدِيدِ فِي تَرْكِ الْجَمَاعَةِ،رقم 551) لوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالْإِمَامَةِ أَعْلَمُهُمْ بِالسُّنَّةِ \ عَنْ أَبِي مُوسَى قَالَ: «مَرِضَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَاشْتَدَّ مَرَضُهُ فَقَالَ : مُرُوا أَبَا بَكْرٍ فَلْيُصَلِ بِالنَّاسِ، ، صحيح البخاري، بَابٌ: أَهْلُ الْعِلْمِ وَالْفَضْلِ أَحَقُّ بِالْإِمَامَةِ، برقم 678\مسلم شريف، بَاب اسْتِخْلَافِ الإِمَامِ إِذَا عَرَضَ لَهُ عُذْرٌ مِنْ مَرَضٌ وَسَفَرٍ وَغَيْرِهِمَا مَنْ يُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ، وَأَنَّ مَنْ صَلَّى خَلْفَ إِمَام جَالِس لِعَجْزِهِ .... رقم 678) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالْإِمَامَةِ أَعْلَمُهُمْ بِالسُّنَّةِ \ عَنْ أَبِي مَسْعُودٍ. قَالَ كَانَ رسول الله يمسح منا كبنا في الصَّلَاةِ وَيَقُولُ اسْتَوُوا وَلَا تَخْتَلِفُوا فَتَخْتَلِفَ قُلُوبُكُمْ لِيَلِني مِنكُمْ أُولُو الأَحْلَامِ وَالنُّهَى ثُمَّ الَّذِينَ يَلُونَهُمْ ثُمَّ الَّذِينَ يَلُونَهُمْ (مسلم شریف، بَاب تَسْوِيَةِ الصُّفُوفِ وَإِقَامَتِهَا وَفَضْلِ الأَوَّلِ فَالأَوَّلِ مِنْهَا، وَالازْدِحَامِ عَلَى الصَّفَ الأَوَّلِ... ، رقم 432 ) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالْإِمَامَةِ أَعْلَمُهُمْ بِالسُّنَّةِ فَإِنْ تَسَاوَوْا فَأَقْرَؤُهُمْ لِكِتَابِ اللَّهِ ا عَنْ عُقْبَةَ بْنِ عَمْرٍو ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «يَؤُمُّ النَّاسَ أَقْدَمُهُمْ هِجْرَةً ، وَإِنْ كَانُوا فِي الهِجْرَةِ سَوَاءً فَأَفْقَهُهُمْ فِي الدِّينِ ، وَإِنْ كَانُوا فِي الدِّينِ سَوَاءً فَأَقْرَؤُهُمْ لِلْقُرْآنِ (سنن دارقطني ، بَابُ مَنْ أَحَقُّ بِالْإِمَامَةِ، غمبر (1085) اصول: نماز کی امامت میں اولین مستحق بڑا عالم ہے جو احکام نماز کو جاننے والا ہو اگر پہلے سے کوئی متعین نہ ہو۔
Chapter on Congregation. Congregational prayer is an emphatic sunnah. The most deserving of people to lead the prayer is the most knowledgeable of them in the sunnah. If they are equal (in knowledge), then the one with the best recitation of the Book of Allah Most High. If they are equal (in recitation), then the most pious of them. If they are equal (in piety), then the oldest of them. Evidence: (1) Hadith proving that congregational prayer is an emphatic sunnah... (etc.)
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the status of congregational prayer and the criteria for imam selection. The author, Imam al-Quduri, states that jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatic recommended practice) – not fard, but strongly encouraged. This is the Hanafi position; other schools differ on obligation. The text then lists four criteria for the imam in order: 1) knowledge of the sunnah (ahkam of salah), 2) best recitation of Quran, 3) piety (wara'), 4) age (oldest). The hadith proofs are cited: the famous hadith of Abu Hurairah about the Prophet's intention to burn houses of those who miss congregation, the hadith of Ibn Abbas about acceptance of prayer conditioned on excuse, the hadith that the most learned are most worthy (Abu Musa and Abu Mas'ud), and the hadith of Uqbah that preference is given to the one who migrated first, then the most knowledgeable, then the best reciter. The Urdu note at the end clarifies that the first deserving is the great scholar who knows the rulings of prayer, if no one is appointed beforehand.

Key Terms
سُنَّةٌ مُؤَكَّدَةٌ (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphatic recommended practice; a regularly performed sunnah that the Prophet consistently did and encouraged, but whose neglect is not sinful.
أَوْرَعُهُمْ (awra'uhum): The most pious, one who abstains from doubtful matters (shubuhat).
أَسَنُّهُمْ (asannuhum): The oldest in age.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first criterion for choosing an imam?
A) The oldest in age
B) The best in Quran recitation
C) The most knowledgeable in the sunnah
D) The most pious

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard, and the imam is chosen first by knowledge of the sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Disliked Imams and the Obligation to Shorten Prayer
Lists individuals whose imamate is disliked but valid, and commands the imam not to prolong prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imamate of a blind person and a fasiq, and explain why the imam must not prolong prayer for the congregation.

Core Idea
A blind man can lead prayer, but it is disliked — the imamate is valid unless a condition is missing.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses two important practical matters: who may lead the congregation and how the prayer should be conducted. While certain individuals are considered disliked as imams, their leadership is not invalid. The Prophet's severe reaction to long prayers shows the importance of considering the congregation's needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Appointing a slave, bedouin, sinner, illegitimate child, or blind person as imam. The ruling: it is makruh (disliked), but if they lead, it is valid (jaza).
The karaha here is tanzihi (not sinful but better avoided).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr: 'Three people’s prayer is not accepted… one who leads a people while they dislike him.' This indicates dislike, not invalidity.
Also the practice of Aisha being led by her slave shows validity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith says 'prayer is not accepted' — which in Hanafi usul implies karaha tanzihiyya when combined with other evidences, not absolute prohibition.
The phrase 'la yaqbal' is interpreted as lack of acceptance (thawab) rather than invalidity.
4
Analyze the ruling on shortening prayer
The Prophet's anger when told a long prayer caused people to avoid him. The hadith commands the imam to be brief, considering the weak, elderly, and those with needs.
This is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) for the imam.
5
Review the women’s congregation ruling
It is also makruh for women to form a congregation alone. If they do, the imam stands in the middle of the row, following the practice of Aisha as narrated.
This is a separate subsidiary ruling.

Source Text

وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالأَعْرَانِي وَالْفَاسِقِ وَوَلَدِ الزَّنَا وَالْأَعْمَى فَإِنْ تَقَدَّمُوا جَازَلِ وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لَا يُطَوّلَ بِهِمْ الصَّلَاةَ هـ وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً فَإِنْ فَعَلْنَ وَقَفَتْ الْإِمَامَةُ وَسْطَهُنَّ
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ كَانَ يَقُولُ: «ثَلَاثَةٌ لَا يَقْبَلُ اللَّهُ مِنْهُمْ صَلَاةً، مَنْ تَقَدَّمَ قَوْمًا وَهُمْ لَهُ كَارِهُونَ(سنن ،ابوداود بَابُ الرَّجُل يَؤُمُّ الْقَوْمَ وَهُمْ لَهُ كَارِهُونَ ، رقم (685)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَانِي \ وَكَانَتْ عَائِشَةُ يَؤُمُّهَا عَبْدُهَا ذَكْوَانُ مِنَ الْمُصْحَفِ ، (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ إِمَامَةِ الْعَبْدِ وَالْمَوْلَى، رقم692)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي \ عَنْ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَدِي بْنِ خِيَارٍ : «أَنَّهُ دَخَلَ عَلَى عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ ، وَهُوَ تَحْصُورٌ ، فَقَالَ: إِنَّكَ إِمَامُ عَامَّةٍ، وَنَزَلَ بِكَ مَا تَرَى، وَيُصَلِّي لَنَا إِمَامُ فِتْنَةٍ، وَنَتَحَرَّجُ؟ فَقَالَ : الصَّلَاةُ أَحْسَنُ مَا يَعْمَلُ النَّاسُ، فَإِذَا أَحْسَنَ النَّاسُ فَأَحْسِنُ مَعَهُمْ، وَإِذَا أَسَاءُوا فَاجْتَنِبْ إِسَاءَتَهُمْ» (صحيح البخاري بَابُ إِمَامَةِ الْمَفْتُونِ وَالْمُبْتَدِعِ، 695) :"وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لا يُطَوّلَ هِيمُ الصَّلَاةَ أَخْبَرَنِي أَبُو مَسْعُودٍ : «أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَالَ: وَاللَّهِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنِّي لَأَتَأَخَّرُ عَنْ صَلَاةِ الْغَدَاةِ مِنْ أَجْلِ فَلَانٍ، مِمَّا يُطِيلُ بِنَا، فَمَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي مَوْعِظَةٍ أَشَدَّ غَضَبًا مِنْهُ يَوْمَئِذٍ ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: إِنَّ مِنْكُمْ مُنَفِّرِينَ، فَأَيُّكُمْ مَا صَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ فَلْيَتَجَوَّزُ، فَإِنَّ فِيهِمُ الضَّعِيفَ وَالْكَبِيرَ وَذَا الْحَاجَةِ. » (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ تَخْفِيفِ الْإِمَامِ فِي الْقِيَامِ وَإِثْمَامِ الرَّكُوع والسُّجُودِ ، 1702 مسلم شريف، باب الدُّعَاءِ فِي صَلَاةِ اللَّيْلِ وَقِيَامِهِ، 766) هوجه (۱) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةَ اعَنْ رَيْطَةَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ . قَالَتْ: «أَمَّتْنَا عَائِشَةُ فَقَامَتْ بَيْنَهُنَّ فِي الصَّلَاةِ الْمَكْتُوبَةِ »»» ، سنن سنن دارقطني ، بَابُ صَلَاةِ النِّسَاءِ جَمَاعَةً وَمَوْقِفِ إِمَامِهِنَّ، رقم 1507)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ؛ قَالَ: قَالَ اصول : تنہا عورتوں کی جماعت مکروہ ہے، لہذا عور تیں تنہا ہوں یعنی مردنہ ہو تو تنہا نماز پڑھے ، جماعت نہیں، اور اگر تنہا جماعت کرے تو امام صف کے درمیان میں کھڑی ہو یعنی مردوں کی طرح مقتدی سے آگے نہیں۔
And it is disliked to appoint a slave, a bedouin, a sinner, an illegitimate child, and a blind person (as imam). But if they come forward (to lead), it is valid. And it is befitting for the imam not to prolong the prayer for them. And it is disliked for women to pray in congregation alone; if they do so, the imam stands in the middle of their row. Evidence: (1) Hadith proving the dislike of appointing a slave and bedouin...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First: It is makruh tanzihi (disliked) to put forward certain individuals as imam: a slave (due to low social status), a bedouin (who may be ignorant of rulings), a fasiq (open sinner), an illegitimate child (walad al-zina, due to stigma), and a blind person (who cannot see the prayer's conditions). However, if they lead, the prayer is valid because their imamate is not inherently invalid. Second: The imam should shorten the prayer—not prolong it—out of consideration for the weak, elderly, and those with needs. The hadith of Abu Mas'ud is quoted: the Prophet became angry when informed of a long prayer and said there are among you people who cause aversion (munaffirun).

Key Terms
مَكْرُوه (makruh): Disliked; an act whose avoidance is rewarded but whose commission is not sinful (makruh tanzih) or borderline sinful (makruh tahrimi). Here it is tanzih.
أَعْمَى (a'ma): Blind person; here specifically refers to a blind man leading prayer.
وَلَدُ الزِّنَا (walad al-zina): Child born out of wedlock; considered in Hanafi fiqh to have a status that makes leading prayer disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a blind man leads the congregation?
A) His imamate is invalid and must be repeated
B) It is permissible without any dislike
C) It is disliked but valid
D) It is forbidden

Key Takeaway
The imamate of certain individuals is disliked but valid; the imam must be considerate and not prolong the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
