Women's Congregational Prayer: Disliked and Imam's Position
Ruling with proof: women's congregation disliked and imam's position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregation alone and explain the position of the imam when women form a congregation.

Core Idea
Women’s congregation without men is makruh tanzih; but if done, the imam stands in the middle of the row.

This lesson examines a specific aspect of women's prayer in the Hanafi school. While women are generally encouraged to pray at home, forming a congregation without men is considered disliked. However, if they do so, the imam's position differs from that of a male imam. We will explore the ruling, its evidence, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify the act being ruled upon: women praying in congregation without any men present. Note the ruling: it is makruh (disliked).
The term 'makruh' here is makruh tanzih (disliked, not prohibited).
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the evidence cited: the practice of Sayyidah Aisha (رضي الله عنها) leading women in obligatory prayer and standing in their midst, narrated by Raytah al-Hanafiyyah.
This is a qawl al-sahabi (statement of a companion) which is a source of proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the evidence
Understand how the evidence proves the dislike: the fact that Aisha led women in congregation shows it is permissible, but the Hanafi school still considers it makruh because of other considerations (e.g., lack of regular practice, avoiding fitna).
The ruling of dislike is based on ijtihad; the evidence shows permissibility but the school chooses the preferable view.
4
Determine the imam's position
Note the practical ruling: if women do form a congregation, the female imam stands in the middle of the row, not in front like a male imam. This is directly from the evidence of Aisha's action.
This distinguishes from men's congregation where the imam stands ahead.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and ikhtilaf
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is makruh tanzih. Some other schools (Shafi'i, Hanbali) do not consider it disliked but permissible.
The difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school has its own evidence and reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً فَإِنْ فَعَلْنَ وَقَفَتْ الْإِمَامَةُ وَسْطَهُنَّ
وجه: (۱) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةَ اعَنْ رَيْطَةَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ . قَالَتْ: «أَمَّتْنَا عَائِشَةُ فَقَامَتْ بَيْنَهُنَّ فِي الصَّلَاةِ الْمَكْتُوبَةِ »»» ، سنن سنن دارقطني ، بَابُ صَلَاةِ النِّسَاءِ جَمَاعَةً وَمَوْقِفِ إِمَامِهِنَّ، رقم 1507)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ؛ قَالَ: قَالَ اصول : تنہا عورتوں کی جماعت مکروہ ہے، لہذا عور تیں تنہا ہوں یعنی مردنہ ہو تو تنہا نماز پڑھے ، جماعت نہیں، اور اگر تنہا جماعت کرے تو امام صف کے درمیان میں کھڑی ہو یعنی مردوں کی طرح مقتدی سے آگے نہیں۔
And it is disliked for women to pray in congregation alone (without men). If they do so, the imam stands in their middle. Evidence: (1) Statement of a female companion to prove the dislike... From Raytah al-Hanafiyyah: 'Aisha led us and stood between us in the obligatory prayer.' (2) Hadith... Urdu: The congregation of women alone is disliked; therefore, when women are alone (without men), they should pray individually, not in congregation. If they do form a congregation, the imam stands in the middle of the row, not ahead like men.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage addresses women's congregational prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh for women to form their own congregation when no men are present. They are better advised to pray individually. This is because a women's congregation may attract unnecessary attention and is not established as a regular practice from the earliest generations. However, if they do form a congregation, it is valid (jaza). The imam must stand in the middle of the row, not in front like a male imam. This is based on the practice of Sayyidah Aisha (رضي الله عنها) who led women in prayer and stood in the middle. The evidence from hadith (though the second one is incomplete) supports the dislike.

Key Terms
وَقَفَتْ (waqafat): The imam stands; specifically, the imam stands in the middle of the row.
وَسْطَهُنَّ (wasatahunna): In their middle; the imam stands at the center of the row of women, not in front.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where should the female imam stand when leading women in congregation?
A) In front of the row, like a male imam
B) At the back of the row
C) In the middle of the row
D) Outside the prayer area

Key Takeaway
Women's congregation without men is makruh tanzih; if performed, the imam stands in the middle of the row.
